Imam's Hadath in Janazah Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Followers' Validity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of janazah prayer when imam becomes impure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar regarding the validity of janazah prayer when the imam becomes impure and performs tayammum, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When the imam in janazah prayer becomes impure and uses tayammum, Abu Hanifa rules the prayer valid for all; Muhammad rules it invalid for those with wudu.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of the janazah prayer when the imam experiences a nullifier of wudu during the prayer. The dispute focuses on whether followers who themselves have wudu can validly follow an imam who has performed tayammum. Understanding this ikhtilaf deepens your grasp of the conditions for following an imam and the scope of tayammum in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Understand the two scenarios: the imam appoints a successor (istikhlaf) who then uses tayammum, or the imam himself performs tayammum and continues leading. The dispute concerns the second scenario.
The first scenario is agreed upon; all imams deem it valid.
2
State the Positions
For the second scenario, state that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule the prayer of all followers (both with wudu and with tayammum) valid. Muhammad and Zufar rule that the prayer of followers with wudu is invalid, but the prayer of those with tayammum is valid.
This is a clear intra-school ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Dispute's Basis
Identify the reasoning: Muhammad and Zufar consider that a person with wudu following a mutayammim without a valid excuse is invalid. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider tayammum a valid purification and allow following in janazah prayer specifically.
The text notes that following a mutayammim in janazah is agreed upon, hinting at the strength of the permissive view.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: if you are a follower with wudu in such a congregation, your prayer may be invalid according to one opinion, requiring repetition. Knowing the relied-upon view in your locale is important.
The text does not specify mufta bihi, but later fatwa collections often prefer the permissive view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجعل في المبسوط المسائل المجمع عليها مختلفاً فيها إذا أحدث الإمام في صلاة الجنازة قال ابن الفضل : إن استخلف متوضئاً ثم تيمم وصلى خلفه أجزأه في قولهم جميعاً، وإن تيمم هذا الذي أحدث وأم وأتم جازت صلاة الكل في قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف وعلى قوله محمد وزفر صلاة المتوضئين فاسدة وصلاة المتيممين جائزة، وهذه المسألة دليل على أن في صلاة الجنازة يجوز البناء والاستخلاف ويصح فيها اقتداء المتوضىء بالمتيمم كما في غيرها من الصلاة. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان من التيمم. من كتاب الصلاة في صحة الاقتداء: وأما اقتداء المتوضيء بالمتيمم في صلاة الجنازة فجائزة بلا خلاف .اهـ.
And it is stated in al-Mabsut that the issues of consensus differ. When the imam has minor impurity in the janazah prayer, Ibn al-Fadl said: If he appoints a successor who has wudu, then the successor performs tayammum and prays behind him, it suffices according to all. And if the one who had impurity performs tayammum and leads the prayer and completes it, the prayer of the whole congregation is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but according to Muhammad and Zufar, the prayer of those who had wudu is invalid, while the prayer of those who had tayammum is valid. This issue indicates that in janazah prayer, building (bina') and appointing a successor are permissible, and that a person with wudu following a mutayammim is valid, as in other prayers. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan from the book of tayammum from the book of prayer on the validity of following: And regarding a person with wudu following a mutayammim in janazah prayer, it is permissible without disagreement.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of janazah prayer when the imam experiences a nullifier of wudu during the prayer. Ibn al-Fadl's narration distinguishes two scenarios: if the imam appoints a successor who has wudu, then that successor performs tayammum (due to harm?) and leads, the prayer is valid by all. If the original imam himself performs tayammum and leads, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule that the prayer of all (both those with wudu and those with tayammum) is valid, while Muhammad and Zufar rule that the prayer of those who had wudu is invalid (because they followed a mutayammim without excuse) but the prayer of those who themselves had tayammum is valid. The text notes that this case proves the permissibility of building (bina') and deputizing in janazah prayer, and that a person with wudu can follow a mutayammim, which is also mentioned as agreed upon.

Key Terms
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): The funeral prayer, which is a communal obligation.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlaf): Appointing a successor imam during the prayer by the original imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if the imam in janazah prayer becomes impure and then performs tayammum and leads the prayer, what is the ruling for the followers who had wudu?
A) Their prayer is invalid
B) Their prayer is valid
C) They must repeat the prayer
D) They must leave the congregation

Key Takeaway
In janazah prayer, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of following a mutayammim imam: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit it for all, while Muhammad and Zufar restrict it to those who themselves have tayammum.

The Effect of Intention on Quranic Recitation in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intention's effect on recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether intending supplication while reciting Quran in prayer affects the validity of the recitation, and identify the conditions under which it is sufficient or insufficient.

Core Idea
Intention does not change the ruling of recitation when it is in its proper place; outside it is insufficient.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether reciting Quranic verses with the intention of supplication (du'a) changes the nature of the recitation in prayer. Al-Khasi raises an objection: if intention changes recitation, then even reciting Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs with supplication intent would be invalid—but scholars say it is valid. The text resolves this by distinguishing between recitation in its proper place (first two rak'ahs) and elsewhere.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the objection
The base ruling states that the Quran changes with intention (azimah). Al-Khasi objects: if intention changes recitation, then reciting Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs with supplication intent would not be sufficient, but scholars rule it sufficient.
The objection sets up the need for a distinction.
2
Understand the distinction of mahall
The answer: when recitation is in its proper place (first two rak'ahs), intention does not alter its ruling. Outside that place, it does.
The proper place is the first two rak'ahs for obligatory recitation.
3
Trace the conflicting views
Al-Tanjis holds that recitation with praise intention in its proper place is valid. Al-Qunyah records a different view from Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani that such recitation never substitutes for obligatory recitation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
If one recites Fatiha with supplication intent in the last two rak'ahs, it does not substitute; the prayer is invalid unless repeated. In the first two, it is valid.
The practical difference rests on the place of recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنهم قالوا هنا وفي باب ما يفسد الصلاة أن القرآن يتغير بعزيمته فأورد الإمام الخاصي كما نقله عنه السراج الهندي في التوشيح بأن العزيمة لو كانت مغيرة للقراءة لكان ينبغي أنه إذا قرأ الفاتحة في الأوليين بنية الدعاء لا تكون مجزئة وقد نصوا على أنها مجزئة . وأجاب بأنها إذا كانت في محلها لا تتغير بالعزيمة حتى لو لم يقرأ في الأوليين فقرأ في الأخريين بنية الدعاء لا يجزئه .اهـ. والمنقول في التنجيس أنه قرأ في الصلاة فاتحة الكتاب على قصد الثناء جازت صلاته لأنه وجدت القراءة في محلها فلا يتغير حكمها بقصد اهـ. ولم يقيد بالأوليين، ولا شك أن الأخريين محل القراءة المفروضة فإن القراءة فرض في ركعتين غير عين وإن كان تعيينها في الأوليين واجباً. وذكر في القنية خلافاً فيما إذا قرأ الفاتحة على قصد الدعاء فرقم لشرح شمس الأئمة الحلواني أنها لا تنوب عن القراءة .اهـ.
Then know that they said here and in the chapter on what invalidates prayer that the Quran changes with intention (azimah). Al-Khasi objected, as narrated by Siraj al-Hindi in al-Tawshih, that if intention changed recitation, then reading al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs with intention of supplication would not be sufficient, but they ruled it sufficient. He answered that if it is in its proper place, it does not change with intention; indeed, if one did not recite in the first two rak'ahs and recited in the last two with intention of supplication, it is not sufficient. The transmitted ruling in al-Tanjis is that if one recited al-Fatiha in prayer with the intention of praise, his prayer is valid because recitation occurred in its proper place, so its ruling does not change by intention. It was not restricted to the first two rak'ahs, and there is no doubt that the last two are the place of obligatory recitation, for recitation is obligatory in two rak'ahs but not specified, though specification in the first two is wajib. And in al-Qunyah, a difference is mentioned regarding reading al-Fatiha with intention of supplication; the marginal note on Sharh Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani states that it does not substitute for recitation.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether intending supplication (du'a) while reciting Quranic verses in prayer changes the nature of the recitation. The base ruling is that recitation in prayer is for worship; supplication is a different purpose. Al-Khasi objects: if intention changes the recitation, then reciting al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs with supplication intent would invalidate the prayer's sufficiency? But scholars say it is sufficient. The answer: the place (first two rak'ahs) is the proper place for obligatory recitation, so intention does not alter it. However, if one recites in the last two rak'ahs (not the proper place) with supplication intent, it is insufficient. The text then cites al-Tanjis: reciting al-Fatiha with intent of praise (thana') is valid. The last two rak'ahs are also a place for recitation, but the obligatory recitation is not fixed to specific rak'ahs; specification in the first two is wajib. Al-Qunyah records a contrary view from Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani that such recitation does not substitute. This shows the nuanced position: the ruling depends on whether the recitation is in its proper place (first two) or not.

Key Terms
عزيمة (azimah): Intention or resolve to do something, here specifically the intention of supplication when reciting Quran.
محل القراءة (mahall al-qira'ah): The proper place for obligatory recitation in prayer, i.e., the first two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer with the intention of supplication (du'a), what is the ruling according to the preferred Hanafi view?
A) The recitation is valid and the prayer is complete.
B) The recitation does not substitute for the obligatory recitation, and the prayer is invalid unless repeated.
C) The prayer is valid but the recitation is considered supplication only.
D) The person must perform sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on recitation with supplication intention depends on whether it occurs in its proper place (first two rak'ahs); intention alone does not change the act when place is correct.

Permissibility of Reciting Qunoot in Prayer
Ruling on reciting qunoot and dhikr in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting qunoot in prayer and explain why the relied-upon opinion permits it despite Imam Muhammad's view of dislike.

Core Idea
Reciting qunoot is permissible in prayer; the fatwa allows it despite a minority view of dislike.

In this passage, we examine the Hanafi position on reciting the qunoot supplication during prayer. While some early authorities, such as Imam Muhammad, considered it disliked due to its resemblance to Quranic verses, the relied-upon opinion affirms its permissibility. Understanding this ruling clarifies a common area of confusion in the fiqh of salah and ensures the worshipper can act confidently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage discusses reciting the qunoot supplication ('Allahumma inna nasta'inuka') in prayer. First, note that all dhikr is absolutely permissible. The specific ruling from the fatwa is that qunoot is not disliked.
2
Recognize the Intra-Madhhab Difference
Imam Muhammad is reported to have disliked qunoot due to a historical suspicion that it might be Quranic, as some Companions differed on its nature. He avoided it out of caution.
3
Understand the Rebuttal
The author argues that there is definitive, absolute consensus (ijma' qat'i) that qunoot is not part of the Quran. Therefore, the precautionary avoidance is unnecessary.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) is that qunoot is not disliked and reciting it is permissible. This is the position given in fatawa works.
5
Evaluate the Practical Consequence
A Hanafi worshipper may recite qunoot in witr without any concern of karahah. It is a recommended act, but leaving it is not disliked either.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الأذكار فالمنقول إباحتها مطلقاً ويدخل فيها اللهم اهدنا إلى آخره . وأما اللهم إنا نستعينك إلى آخره» الذي دعاء القنوت عندنا فالظاهر من المذهب أنه لا يكره لهما وعليه الفتوى. كذا في الفتاوى هو الظهيرية وغيرها. وعن محمد يكره لشبهة كونه قرآناً لاختلاف الصحابة في كونه قرآناً فلا يقرأه احتياطاً. قلنا: حصل الإجماع القطعي اليقيني على أنه ليس بقرآن، ومعه توجب الاحتياط المذكور. نعم المذكور في الهداية وغيرها في باب الأذان استحباب الوضوء لذكر الله تعالى وترك المستحب لا يوجب الكراهة.
As for dhikr (remembrances), it is transmitted that they are absolutely permissible, and includes 'Allahumma ihdina...' (Guide us). As for 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka...' (O Allah, we seek Your help), which is the qunoot supplication in our school, the apparent position of the school is that it is not disliked for them, and upon it is the fatwa. Thus in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah and others. From Muhammad, it is disliked due to the suspicion that it is Quran because the Companions differed on whether it is Quran; so he does not recite it out of caution. We say: There is absolute and certain consensus that it is not Quran, and with that, the aforementioned caution is not required. Yes, it is mentioned in al-Hidayah and others in the chapter on adhan that performing wudu for the remembrance of Allah is recommended, and leaving a recommended act does not necessitate dislike.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on reciting certain supplications in prayer. The author says that general dhikr is absolutely permissible. Specifically, the qunoot supplication ('Allahumma inna nasta'inuka') is not disliked according to the relied-upon opinion (fatwa). Imam Muhammad is reported to have disliked it because some Companions thought it might be Quranic, so he avoided it out of caution. However, the author rebuts that there is definitive consensus it is not Quran, so the precaution is unnecessary. The text then notes that al-Hidayah mentions wudu for dhikr is recommended, but leaving a recommended act does not cause dislike (karahah). This indicates that while the qunoot is not disliked, it is also not obligatory; it is a recommended act.

Key Terms
دعاء القنوت (du'a al-qunut): The supplication recited in the witr prayer, beginning with 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka'.
كراهة (karahah): Dislike, a level below haram but discouraged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi opinion, what is the ruling on reciting the qunoot supplication ('Allahumma inna nasta'inuka') in prayer?
A) It is absolutely forbidden.
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It is permissible (not disliked).
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Reciting qunoot in witr is permissible (mubah) according to the relied-upon Hanafi opinion, despite a minority view of dislike.

The Linguistic and Legal Definition of Salah
Defines salah linguistically and legally, and discusses its ruling, cause, and sign.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of salah and identify its ruling, cause, and the distinction between sabab and 'alamah.

Core Idea
Salah is linguistically supplication and legally specific actions; its ruling is obligation, its cause is time, and its pillars ensure validity.

Every act of worship in the Hanafi school has a precise definition that distinguishes its linguistic origin from its legal reality. This lesson unpacks the definition of salah given by the commentator, clarifies the ruling and cause, and introduces the subtle usuli distinction between sabab and 'alamah.

Guided Path
1
Step 1: Identify the two definitions
Find the sentence that gives the linguistic and legal definitions. Note the exact Arabic terms: 'هي لغة الدعاء' and 'شرعاً الأفعال المخصوصة من القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود'.
The legal definition lists the specific actions: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration.
2
Step 2: Extract the ruling (hukm) and the cause (sabab)
Look for the sentence beginning with 'وحكمها' and 'وسببها'. The hukm is that performing salah drops the obligation and brings reward. The sabab is the time of prayer according to fuqaha.
Note the difference between sabab and 'alamah as per the usuliyyin.
3
Step 3: Distinguish sabab from 'alamah
Read the passage that explains the difference: the sabab leads to the ruling without effect, while the 'alamah indicates the ruling without dependency. Understand why usuliyyin call the times 'signs' rather than causes.
The real illah is the successive favors in the time – a deeper cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة

هي لغة الدعاء، وشرعاً الأفعال المخصوصة من القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود. وقول الشارح وفيها زيادة مع بقاء معنى فيكون تغييراً لا نقلاً فيه نظر، إذا الدعاء ليس من حقيقتها شرعاً، وإن أريد به القراءة فبعيد فالظاهر أنها منقولة كما في الغاية لا لما علل به من وجودها بدون الدعاء في الأمي بل لما ذكرناه، وسيأتي بيان أركانها وشرائطها وواجباتها. وحكمها سقوط الواجب عن ذمته بالأداء في الدنيا ونيل الثواب الموعود في الآخرة إن كان واجباً وإلا فالثاني وسببها أوقاتها عند الفقهاء، وعند الأصوليين هي علامات وليست بأسباب والفرق بينهما أن السبب هو المفضي إلى الحكم بلا تأثير، والعلامة هي الدال على الحكم من غير توقف ولا إفضاء ولا تأثير فهو علامة على الوجوب. والعلة في الحقيقة النعم المترادفة في الوقت وهو شرط صحة متعلقة بالضرورة كما يفيده كونه ظرفاً. ثم عامة مشايخنا عندنا ينابذه.

قوله : (هي لغة الدعاء) هذا ما عليه الجمهور وجزم به الجوهري وغيره. وقال الزمخشري تبعاً لأبي علي واستحسنه ابن جني أن حقيقة «صلى» حرك الصلوين لأن المصلي يفعل ذلك في ركوعه وسجوده، وقيل للداعي مصلياً تشبيهاً في تخشعه بالراكع والساجد اهـ. والصلوان بالسكون العظمان الناتئان في أعالي الفخذين اللذان عليهما الأليتان. وادعى أبو حيان أنهما عرقان. وحاصله أن «صلى» حقيقة لغوية في تحرك الصلوين مجاز لغوي في الأركان المخصوصة استعارة يعني تصريحية في الرتبة الثانية في الدعاء تشبيهاً للداعي بالراكع والساجد. وتمامه في النهر قوله: (فيكون تغييراً لا نقلاً) الفرق بينهما أن في النقل لم يبق المعنى الذي وضعه الواضع مرعياً وفي التغيير يكون باقياً لكنه زيد عليه شيء آخر. وفي النهر : اختلف الأصوليون في الألفاظ الدالة على معان شرعية كالصلاة والصوم أهي منقولة عن معانيها اللغوية إلى حقائق شرعية أم مغيرة؟ قيل بالأول قال في الغاية وهو
Book of Prayer. It (salah) is linguistically supplication, and legally the specific actions: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The statement of the commentator: 'And in it there is an addition while the meaning remains, so it is a modification (taghyir) not a transmission (naql)' is debatable, because supplication is not part of its legal reality, and if by it he means recitation, that is far; the apparent view is that it is transmitted (manqul) as stated in al-Ghayah, not for the reason given—that it exists without supplication in the case of an illiterate person—but for what we mentioned. The explanation of its pillars, conditions, and obligations will come later. Its ruling is the dropping of obligation from one's liability by performance in this world and attainment of promised reward in the hereafter if it is obligatory, otherwise the second. Its cause (sabab) is its times according to the jurists, but according to the usuliyyin they are signs ('alamat) not causes; the difference is that the cause leads to the ruling without effect, while the sign indicates the ruling without being dependent on it, leading, or effecting; it is a sign of obligation. The real cause (illah) is the successive favors in the time, and it is a condition of validity related to necessity, as is indicated by its being a container. Then most of our scholars in our view reject it. His statement: (It is linguistically supplication): This is the view of the majority, and al-Jawhari and others affirmed it. al-Zamakhshari, following Abu Ali and endorsed by Ibn Jinni, said that the reality of 'salla' is to move the two hip bones because the prayer performs that in his bowing and prostration; and it is said that the supplicant is called musalli by way of resemblance in humility to the one bowing and prostrating. The two hip bones (salwan, with sukun) are the two prominent bones at the top of the thighs upon which the buttocks lie. Abu Hayyan claimed they are two veins. The summary is that 'salla' is a linguistic reality in moving the two hip bones, and a linguistic metaphor for the specific actions, a transfer in the second rank for supplication, likening the supplicant to the one bowing and prostrating. Its completion is in al-Nahr. His statement: (So it is a modification, not a transmission): The difference between them is that in transmission the meaning placed by the coiner is no longer considered, while in modification it remains but something else is added to it. In al-Nahr: The usuliyyin differed regarding words denoting legal meanings, like salah and sawm: are they transmitted from their linguistic meanings to legal realities or modified? The first was said; in al-Ghayah it is said: and it is...
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq begins the Book of Prayer by defining salah. It first gives the two definitions: linguistically (supplication) and legally (the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration). It then engages in a technical discussion about the nature of the term: whether the Shar'iah has 'transmitted' (naql) the word from its linguistic meaning to a new legal meaning, or whether it has 'modified' (taghyir) the original meaning by adding to it while keeping the original sense. The commentator (the author of al-Bahr) notes that the claim of modification is problematic because supplication is not part of the legal reality of salah; if by supplication one means recitation (which includes supplication), that is also an imprecise identification. The apparent view, according to the author, is that it is transmitted (manqul), as supported in al-Ghayah. The passage then discusses the ruling (hukm) of salah: it causes the obligation to be dropped from the liability, and if obligatory, it brings reward. It distinguishes between sabab (cause) and 'alamah (sign) from the usul perspective: the times of prayer are causes according to fuqaha but signs according to usuliyyin. The real 'illah is the successive favors in the time. Then it delves into the linguistic analysis, presenting the majority view that 'salah' means supplication, and the alternate view of al-Zamakhshari that it means movement of the hip bones. It explains that the latter view considers the legal meaning a metaphorical extension of the original meaning of moving the hips. Finally, it introduces the usuli debate on naql vs taghyir, citing al-Nahr.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-salah): Linguistically: supplication; legally: the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration.
منقولة (manqulah): A word that has been transferred from its original linguistic meaning to a new legal meaning, with the original no longer considered.
مغيرة (mghayyarah): A word that has been modified by adding to the original meaning while the original remains.
الصلوان (al-salwan): The two hip bones; also claimed to be two veins by Abu Hayyan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Supplication
B) Any act of worship
C) Standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration
D) Movement of the hip bones

Key Takeaway
Salah is a transmitted term: its legal meaning (specific actions) completely replaces the original linguistic meaning (supplication).

Is the Term 'Salah' Transmitted or Modified? The Hanafi Position
Discusses whether the term 'salah' is transmitted (manqul) or modified (mghayyar), with Hanafi preference for transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the debate between naql and taghyir regarding legal terms and state the Hanafi view with its evidence.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds that 'salah' is manqul (transmitted) to its legal meaning; the original sense of supplication is no longer part of its legal definition.

When the Shari'ah uses words that existed in Arabic, do they retain their original meanings or take on entirely new ones? This lesson examines the classic usul debate over whether 'salah' is transmitted (manqul) or modified (mghayyar) and why the Hanafis choose transmission.

Guided Path
1
Step 1: Understand the two views
Read the passage that defines naql and taghyir. In naql, the original meaning is abandoned; in taghyir, the original remains but is added to.
The difference is crucial for interpreting legal texts.
2
Step 2: Identify the commentator's statement and the critique
The commentator claimed that the term is mghayyar. The author of al-Bahr critiques this: supplication is not part of the legal reality, so the addition does not retain the original meaning.
Note the author's reasoning: 'إذا الدعاء ليس من حقيقتها شرعاً'.
3
Step 3: Follow the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi position (from al-Ghayah) is that it is manqul. The evidence: the legal definition does not include supplication; recitation, though it may contain supplication, is not the same as the linguistic meaning.
The passage also mentions an illiterate person – but the author dismisses that reason and gives his own.
4
Step 4: Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
If the term is manqul, then 'salah' in the Quran and Sunnah refers exclusively to the legal actions. If mghayyar, one might argue that the linguistic sense also plays a role in interpretation.
This affects rulings like the validity of salah without recitation (for an illiterate) or without supplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة

هي لغة الدعاء، وشرعاً الأفعال المخصوصة من القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود. وقول الشارح وفيها زيادة مع بقاء معنى فيكون تغييراً لا نقلاً فيه نظر، إذا الدعاء ليس من حقيقتها شرعاً، وإن أريد به القراءة فبعيد فالظاهر أنها منقولة كما في الغاية لا لما علل به من وجودها بدون الدعاء في الأمي بل لما ذكرناه، وسيأتي بيان أركانها وشرائطها وواجباتها. وحكمها سقوط الواجب عن ذمته بالأداء في الدنيا ونيل الثواب الموعود في الآخرة إن كان واجباً وإلا فالثاني وسببها أوقاتها عند الفقهاء، وعند الأصوليين هي علامات وليست بأسباب والفرق بينهما أن السبب هو المفضي إلى الحكم بلا تأثير، والعلامة هي الدال على الحكم من غير توقف ولا إفضاء ولا تأثير فهو علامة على الوجوب. والعلة في الحقيقة النعم المترادفة في الوقت وهو شرط صحة متعلقة بالضرورة كما يفيده كونه ظرفاً. ثم عامة مشايخنا عندنا ينابذه.

قوله : (هي لغة الدعاء) هذا ما عليه الجمهور وجزم به الجوهري وغيره. وقال الزمخشري تبعاً لأبي علي واستحسنه ابن جني أن حقيقة «صلى» حرك الصلوين لأن المصلي يفعل ذلك في ركوعه وسجوده، وقيل للداعي مصلياً تشبيهاً في تخشعه بالراكع والساجد اهـ. والصلوان بالسكون العظمان الناتئان في أعالي الفخذين اللذان عليهما الأليتان. وادعى أبو حيان أنهما عرقان. وحاصله أن «صلى» حقيقة لغوية في تحرك الصلوين مجاز لغوي في الأركان المخصوصة استعارة يعني تصريحية في الرتبة الثانية في الدعاء تشبيهاً للداعي بالراكع والساجد. وتمامه في النهر قوله: (فيكون تغييراً لا نقلاً) الفرق بينهما أن في النقل لم يبق المعنى الذي وضعه الواضع مرعياً وفي التغيير يكون باقياً لكنه زيد عليه شيء آخر. وفي النهر : اختلف الأصوليون في الألفاظ الدالة على معان شرعية كالصلاة والصوم أهي منقولة عن معانيها اللغوية إلى حقائق شرعية أم مغيرة؟ قيل بالأول قال في الغاية وهو
Book of Prayer. It (salah) is linguistically supplication, and legally the specific actions: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The statement of the commentator: 'And in it there is an addition while the meaning remains, so it is a modification (taghyir) not a transmission (naql)' is debatable, because supplication is not part of its legal reality, and if by it he means recitation, that is far; the apparent view is that it is transmitted (manqul) as stated in al-Ghayah, not for the reason given—that it exists without supplication in the case of an illiterate person—but for what we mentioned. The explanation of its pillars, conditions, and obligations will come later. Its ruling is the dropping of obligation from one's liability by performance in this world and attainment of promised reward in the hereafter if it is obligatory, otherwise the second. Its cause (sabab) is its times according to the jurists, but according to the usuliyyin they are signs ('alamat) not causes; the difference is that the cause leads to the ruling without effect, while the sign indicates the ruling without being dependent on it, leading, or effecting; it is a sign of obligation. The real cause (illah) is the successive favors in the time, and it is a condition of validity related to necessity, as is indicated by its being a container. Then most of our scholars in our view reject it. His statement: (It is linguistically supplication): This is the view of the majority, and al-Jawhari and others affirmed it. al-Zamakhshari, following Abu Ali and endorsed by Ibn Jinni, said that the reality of 'salla' is to move the two hip bones because the prayer performs that in his bowing and prostration; and it is said that the supplicant is called musalli by way of resemblance in humility to the one bowing and prostrating. The two hip bones (salwan, with sukun) are the two prominent bones at the top of the thighs upon which the buttocks lie. Abu Hayyan claimed they are two veins. The summary is that 'salla' is a linguistic reality in moving the two hip bones, and a linguistic metaphor for the specific actions, a transfer in the second rank for supplication, likening the supplicant to the one bowing and prostrating. Its completion is in al-Nahr. His statement: (So it is a modification, not a transmission): The difference between them is that in transmission the meaning placed by the coiner is no longer considered, while in modification it remains but something else is added to it. In al-Nahr: The usuliyyin differed regarding words denoting legal meanings, like salah and sawm: are they transmitted from their linguistic meanings to legal realities or modified? The first was said; in al-Ghayah it is said: and it is...
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq begins the Book of Prayer by defining salah. It first gives the two definitions: linguistically (supplication) and legally (the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration). It then engages in a technical discussion about the nature of the term: whether the Shar'iah has 'transmitted' (naql) the word from its linguistic meaning to a new legal meaning, or whether it has 'modified' (taghyir) the original meaning by adding to it while keeping the original sense. The commentator (the author of al-Bahr) notes that the claim of modification is problematic because supplication is not part of the legal reality of salah; if by supplication one means recitation (which includes supplication), that is also an imprecise identification. The apparent view, according to the author, is that it is transmitted (manqul), as supported in al-Ghayah. The passage then discusses the ruling (hukm) of salah: it causes the obligation to be dropped from the liability, and if obligatory, it brings reward. It distinguishes between sabab (cause) and 'alamah (sign) from the usul perspective: the times of prayer are causes according to fuqaha but signs according to usuliyyin. The real 'illah is the successive favors in the time. Then it delves into the linguistic analysis, presenting the majority view that 'salah' means supplication, and the alternate view of al-Zamakhshari that it means movement of the hip bones. It explains that the latter view considers the legal meaning a metaphorical extension of the original meaning of moving the hips. Finally, it introduces the usuli debate on naql vs taghyir, citing al-Nahr.

Key Terms
الصلاة (al-salah): Linguistically: supplication; legally: the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration.
منقولة (manqulah): A word that has been transferred from its original linguistic meaning to a new legal meaning, with the original no longer considered.
مغيرة (mghayyarah): A word that has been modified by adding to the original meaning while the original remains.
الصلوان (al-salwan): The two hip bones; also claimed to be two veins by Abu Hayyan.

C) Because the term is found in the Quran
D) Because all scholars agree it is manqul

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers 'salah' a transmitted (manqul) term; its legal meaning is exclusively the specific actions, not supplication.

Definition of Salat: Linguistic vs Legal Meaning
Defining the word salat and debating whether it is a transmitted or modified legal term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of salat and explain the Hanafi position on whether the term is transmitted (manqul) or modified (mghayyar).

Core Idea
Salat is legally defined as specific actions; the term is transmitted (naql), not merely an extension of supplication.

This lesson explores the foundational definition of salat (prayer) in Hanafi fiqh. While the word originally means supplication, Islamic law redefines it to refer to the ritual acts of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The Hanafi school holds that this legal meaning is a complete transmission (naql) of the term, not a mere modification (taghyir) that retains the original meaning.

Guided Path
1
State the linguistic meaning
Identify the literal meaning of salat as du'a (supplication) according to the majority of scholars.
Al-Jawhari and others assert this.
2
State the legal definition
Identify the specific actions that constitute the legal salat: qiyam (standing), qira'ah (recitation), ruku' (bowing), and sujud (prostration).
These are the core actions; pillars and conditions will be detailed later.
3
Understand the naql vs taghyir debate
Distinguish between transmission (naql) where the original meaning is replaced, and modification (taghyir) where the original meaning remains but additions are made.
The author critiques the taghyir view because supplication is not part of the legal reality.
4
Identify the Hanafi position
The author sides with naql, citing al-Ghayah and arguing that supplication is not part of the legal definition.
The reasoning: if salat were a modification, the original meaning would still be relevant, but it is not.
5
Apply: classify other terms
Reflect on other legal terms like zakat and sawm: are they also transmitted? This illustrates consistency in Hanafi usul.
The usul principle of naql applies to many terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
هي لغة الدعاء، وشرعاً الأفعال المخصوصة من القيام والقراءة والركوع والسجود. وقول الشارح وفيها زيادة مع بقاء معنى فيكون تغييراً لا نقلاً فيه نظر، إذا الدعاء ليس من حقيقتها شرعاً، وإن أريد به القراءة فبعيد فالظاهر أنها منقولة كما في الغاية لا لما علل به من وجودها بدون الدعاء في الأمي بل لما ذكرناه، وسيأتي بيان أركانها وشرائطها وواجباتها.
قوله : (هي لغة الدعاء) هذا ما عليه الجمهور وجزم به الجوهري وغيره. وقال الزمخشري تبعاً لأبي علي واستحسنه ابن جني أن حقيقة «صلى» حرك الصلوين لأن المصلي يفعل ذلك في ركوعه وسجوده، وقيل للداعي مصلياً تشبيهاً في تخشعه بالراكع والساجد اهـ. والصلوان بالسكون العظمان الناتئان في أعالي الفخذين اللذان عليهما الأليتان. وادعى أبو حيان أنهما عرقان. وحاصله أن «صلى» حقيقة لغوية في تحرك الصلوين مجاز لغوي في الأركان المخصوصة استعارة يعني تصريحية في الرتبة الثانية في الدعاء تشبيهاً للداعي بالراكع والساجد. وتمامه في النهر قوله: (فيكون تغييراً لا نقلاً) الفرق بينهما أن في النقل لم يبق المعنى الذي وضعه الواضع مرعياً وفي التغيير يكون باقياً لكنه زيد عليه شيء آخر. وفي النهر : اختلف الأصوليون في الألفاظ الدالة على معان شرعية كالصلاة والصوم أهي منقولة عن معانيها اللغوية إلى حقائق شرعية أم مغيرة؟ قيل بالأول قال في الغاية وهو الظاهر لوجودها بدونه في الأمي وقيل بالثاني وأنه إنما زيد على الدعاء باقي الأركان المخصوصة وأطلق الجزء على الكل قوله : (بل لما ذكرناه أي من أن الدعاء ليس من حقيقتها بناء على أنه خلاف القراءة ومنعه في النهر ولم يذكر له سنداً
The Book of Prayer. Linguistically it is supplication, and legally it is the specific actions of standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. The commentator's saying: 'And there is an increase while the meaning remains, so it is a modification not a transmission' is debatable, because supplication is not part of its legal reality, and if what is meant is recitation it is far-fetched. So the apparent view is that it is transmitted, as in al-Ghayah, not because of what he reasoned that it exists without supplication in the illiterate, but because of what we mentioned. And the explanation of its pillars, conditions, and obligations will follow. His statement: '(It is linguistically supplication)' – this is what the majority hold, and al-Jawhari and others asserted it. Al-Zamakhshari followed by Abu Ali and approved by Ibn Jinni said that the reality of 'salla' is the movement of the two pelvic bones because the prayer does that in his bowing and prostration. It is said that the supplicant is called a prayer in imitation of his humility to the one bowing and prostrating. As-salwan (with sukun) are the two prominent bones on the upper thighs on which the buttocks rest. Abu Hayyan claimed they are two veins. The summary is that 'salla' is a linguistic reality for the movement of the pelvic bones, a linguistic metaphor for the specific actions, an explicit metaphor in the second degree for supplication, likening the supplicant to the one bowing and prostrating. Its completion is in al-Nahr: his statement: '(So it is a modification not a transmission)'. The difference between them is that in transmission the meaning that the originator placed is not observed, while in modification it remains but something else is added to it. In al-Nahr: The usul scholars differed about words denoting legal meanings like prayer and fasting: are they transmitted from their linguistic meanings to legal realities or modified? Some said the first; he stated in al-Ghayah that the apparent view is because it exists without it in the illiterate. And some said the second, that only the remaining specific actions were added to supplication, and the part is applied to the whole. His statement: '(But because of what we mentioned)' meaning that supplication is not part of its reality based on it being contrary to recitation, and al-Nahr rejected it and did not mention a support for it.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq defines salat (prayer) both linguistically and legally. It opens by stating that salat linguistically means supplication (du'a), and legally refers to the specific actions: standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud). The commentary then discusses whether the term was merely modified (taghyir) or transmitted (naql) from its original meaning. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq critiques the view that it is a modification because the legal meaning includes actions not part of supplication. He leans toward the transmission view, citing al-Ghayah, and argues that supplication (du'a) is not part of its legal reality; if one meant recitation, that is a stretch. The commentary then examines the linguistic origin: some say 'salla' means to move the pelvic bones (salwan) due to the motion in prayer, and that calling a supplicant a 'musalli' is metaphorical, likening his humility to a bowing and prostrating person. The debate between naql and taghyir is a key usul al-fiqh issue: whether legal terms are entirely new definitions (transmitted) or remain linked to the original meaning with added elements (modified). The author defends the transmission view.

Key Terms
صلاة (salat): Linguistically: supplication (du'a). Legally: specific actions including standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration.
نقل (naql): Transmission of a word from its original linguistic meaning to a purely legal meaning, leaving the original obsolete in the legal context.
تغيير (taghyir): Modification where the original linguistic meaning remains but additional elements are added.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Ruling, Cause, and Condition of Salat
Defining the hukm, sabab, and shart of salah with a usul distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hukm, sabab, and shart of salah according to Hanafi fiqh, and distinguish between sabab and alamah.

Core Idea
Time is a sign of obligation, not a cause; it is also a condition for validity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the foundational legal framework for salah: its ruling, its cause, and its condition. It also introduces a subtle but crucial distinction between a 'cause' (sabab) and a 'sign' (alamah) that reflects core Hanafi usul methodology. Understanding these categories is essential for properly grasping how obligations are determined in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm of salah
Read the first sentence: the hukm is the discharge of obligation and attainment of reward. Note that the text implies the five daily prayers are fard 'ayn.
The hukm is fard because it removes the liability (dhimmah).
2
Locate the sabab according to fuqaha
The text states that according to jurists (fuqaha), the cause of salah is its times (awqat).
This is the common understanding in fiqh works.
3
Distinguish sabab from alamah
The text contrasts the fuqaha view with the usul scholars: times are merely signs (alamat), not causes. A cause leads to the ruling without direct effect; a sign indicates the ruling without being conditional or leading.
This distinction is key to Hanafi usul. The real 'illa is the continuous blessings of Allah.
4
Identify the shart for validity
The text says time is a condition of validity (shart sahih) related to necessity, as it is the container (zarf) for the prayer.
A condition must be present for the act to be valid but is not part of the act itself.
5
Review the historical note
The passage ends with a brief history: the five daily prayers were made fard on the night of Mi'raj; before that only two prayers were obligatory.
This reinforces the divine origin of the obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكمها سقوط الواجب عن ذمته بالأداء في الدنيا ونيل الثواب الموعود في الآخرة إن كان واجباً وإلا فالثاني وسببها أوقاتها عند الفقهاء، وعند الأصوليين هي علامات وليست بأسباب والفرق بينهما أن السبب هو المفضي إلى الحكم بلا تأثير، والعلامة هي الدال على الحكم من غير توقف ولا إفضاء ولا تأثير فهو علامة على الوجوب. والعلة في الحقيقة النعم المترادفة في الوقت وهو شرط صحة متعلقة بالضرورة كما يفيده كونه ظرفاً. ثم عامة مشايخنا عندنا ينابذه .
على أن السبب هو الجزء الأوّل إن اتصل به الأداء، وإن لم يتصل به انتقلت كذلك إلى ما يتصل به وإلا فالسبب الجزء الأخير وبعد خروجه يضاف إلى جملته، وتمامه في كتابنا المسمى بلب الأصول. وفي شرح النقاية وكان فرض الصلوات الخمس ليلة المعراج وهي ليلة السبت لسبع عشرة ليلة خلت من رمضان قبل الهجرة بثمانية عشر شهراً من مكة إلى السماء، وكانت الصلاة قبل الإسراء صلاتين صلاة قبل طلوع الشمس وصلاة قبل غروبها قال تعالى وسبح بحمد ربك بالعشي والأبكار [غافر : ٥٥]
قوله : (المسمى بلب الأصول) هو مختصر تحرير ابن الهمام.
Its ruling is the discharge of the obligation from one's liability by performance in this world and attainment of the promised reward in the Hereafter; if it is obligatory, otherwise only the second. Its cause according to jurists is its times; according to usul scholars they are signs and not causes. The difference between them is that the cause is what leads to the ruling without any effect, and the sign is what indicates the ruling without being conditional, leading, or effective; thus it is a sign of obligation. The real effective cause is the successive blessings in time, and it is a condition of validity related to necessity as implied by its being a time. Then our general scholars with us [unclear]... That the cause is the first part if performance is connected to it, and if not connected, it transfers similarly to what is connected; otherwise the cause is the last part, and after its exit it is added to its entirety. Its completion is in our book called Lub al-Usul. In Sharh al-Niqayah: The five prayers were made fard on the night of the Miraj, which was Saturday night, seventeen nights passed from Ramadan, eighteen months before the Hijra from Mecca to the sky. Prayer before the Isra consisted of two prayers: one before sunrise and one before sunset. Allah said: 'and glorify the praises of your Lord at evening and morning' [Ghafir:55]. His statement: (called Lub al-Usul) is an abridgement of Tahrir by Ibn al-Humam.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage explains the hukm (ruling), sabab (cause), and shart (condition) of salat. The hukm of salat is that when performed, it discharges the obligation from one's liability and earns the promised reward. Its cause (sabab) according to the fuqaha is the prescribed times (awqat). However, usul scholars consider these times merely signs (alamat) that indicate obligation, not actual causes. The distinction is that a cause leads to the ruling without any direct effect, whereas a sign indicates the ruling without being a cause. The real 'illa (effective cause) is the continuous blessings from Allah during the time, but this is philosophical. The time itself is also a condition (shart) for validity, as it is the container. The author then cites that their general mashayikh say that the cause for obligation is the first part of the time if one performs the prayer, otherwise it transfers to later parts; after the time exits, the obligation relates to the entire time. The text then shifts to a historical note: the five prayers were made fard on the night of the Mi'raj, before which only two prayers were obligatory. The phrase 'called Lub al-Usul' refers to Ibn al-Humam's work on usul.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): What leads to a ruling without any effect; according to fuqaha, the time is the sabab for prayer obligation.
علامة (alamah): A sign that indicates the ruling but does not cause it; usul scholars call the prayer times signs.
شرط صحة (shart sahih): Condition of validity; the time is a condition for the prayer to be valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the usul scholars mentioned in the text, what is the time of prayer?
A) The cause of the obligation.
B) The sign of the obligation.
C) The effective cause of the obligation.
D) The condition for the obligation to be lifted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the time of prayer is a sign (alamah) of the obligation and a condition for validity, not a cause; the real cause is the command of Allah.

The Time of Fajr: Definition and Proof from the Hadith of Jibril
Explaining the order of prayer times and proof for Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the start and end of Fajr time and explain how the Hadith of Jibril proves this definition.

Core Idea
Fajr time begins at true dawn (subh sadiq) and ends at sunrise, as demonstrated by Jibril's prayer.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq explains why the author begins with prayer times before the prayers themselves – because time is the cause (sabab) for the obligation. It then addresses a famous question: how could the Prophet have missed Fajr the morning after the Isra when the prayers were ordained? The answer: he was asleep, and the sleeper is not accountable. Finally, the text presents the foundational Hadith of Jibril, which delineates the starting and ending points for each prayer time. Fajr is defined from the moment the dawn breaks (subh sadiq) until sunrise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall structure
The author first gives the rationale for ordering prayer times before the rulings, then addresses a historical objection, and finally cites the primary textual evidence (Hadith of Jibril). Follow this sequence to see how the ruling is anchored.
2
Understand the cause (sabab) vs. condition
Time is the sabab (cause) of the prayer obligation, nobler than a mere condition. This justifies beginning the chapter with times rather than with the prayer itself.
3
Resolve the apparent contradiction about Fajr
The passage answers the question: why did the Prophet not pray Fajr on the morning after Isra when the prayers were made obligatory? The answer from al-Iraqi is that he was asleep. A sleeper is not held accountable.
This shows the importance of legal capacity (taklif) and the excuse of sleep.
4
Extract the precise temporal definition
From the Hadith of Jibril, Fajr begins when the dawn breaks (bazqa al-fajr) – the true dawn (subh sadiq). The end is sunrise, explicitly stated in the matn (not fully quoted but implied).
The Hanafi school relies on this hadith to set the boundaries of prayer times.
5
Analyze the proof structure
The hadith is ahad (singular transmission) thus zanni al-thubut, but its meaning is clear and accepted by the school. It is not overridden by istihsan. Identify the phrase that carries the ruling: "صلى الفجر حين بزق الفجر".
The hadith also shows that prayer times have a range – the first instance was at the earliest time, the second at the latest (except Maghrib).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بدأ بالأوقات لتقدم السبب على المسبب، والشرط وإن كان كذلك لكن السبب أشرف منه ولكونه شرطاً أيضاً. وقدم الفجر لأنه أول النهار أو لأنه لا خلاف في أوله ولا آخره أو لأن أول من صلاها آدم عليه السلام حين أهبط من الجنة إنما قدم الظهر في الجامع الصغير لأنها أول صلاة فرضت على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى أمته . كذا في غاية البيان. وبهذا اندفع السؤال المشهور كيف ترك النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة الفجر صبيحة ليلة الإسراء التي افترض فيها الصلوات الخمس وفي الغاية : إن صلاة الفجر أول الخمس في الوجوب لأن الفجر صبيحة ليلة الإسراء فيحتاج إلى الجواب عن الفجر، وأجاب عنه العراقي أنه كان نائماً وقت الصبح والنائم غير مكلف.
.
قوله : (وقت الفجر من الصبح الصادق إلى طلوع الشمس الحديث أمامة : أتاني جبريل عند البيت مرتين فصلى بي الظهر في الأولى منهما حين كان الفيء مثل الشرك، ثم صلى العصر حين كان كل شيء مثل ظله ثم صلى المغرب حين وجبت الشمس وأفطر الصائم، ثم صلى العشاء حين غاب الشفق، ثم صلى الفجر حين بزق الفجر وحرم الطعام على الصائم. وصلى المرة الثانية الظهر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثله كوقت العصر بالأمس، ثم صلى العصر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثليه، ثم صلى المغرب لوقته الأول، ثم صلى العشاء
Then he began with the times because the cause precedes the effect, and the condition even so is like that, but the cause is nobler than it and because it is also a condition. He gave precedence to Fajr because it is the beginning of the day, or because there is no disagreement on its beginning or end, or because the first to pray it was Adam (peace be upon him) when he was descended from Paradise. He only gave precedence to Zuhr in al-Jami' al-Saghir because it was the first prayer made obligatory upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his nation. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And by this the famous question is refuted: how did the Prophet (peace be upon him) leave the Fajr prayer on the morning of the night of Isra when the five prayers were made obligatory? In al-Ghayah: The Fajr prayer is the first of the five in obligation because Fajr is the morning of the night of Isra, so an answer is needed. Al-Iraqi answered that he was asleep at the time of dawn, and the sleeper is not accountable. His statement: (The time of Fajr is from the true dawn to sunrise. The hadith [transmitted by] Imamah: Jibril came to me at the House twice and prayed with me Zuhr the first time when the shadow was like the strap, then Asr when everything was like its shadow, then Maghrib when the sun set and the fasting person breaks fast, then Isha when the twilight disappeared, then Fajr when the dawn broke and food became forbidden for the fasting person. And he prayed the second time Zuhr when the shadow of everything was like it – like the time of Asr the previous day – then Asr when the shadow of everything was twice it, then Maghrib at its first time, then Isha...
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage discusses the order in which prayer times are listed. The author begins by explaining why the times are mentioned before the prayers themselves: because the cause (time) precedes the effect (prayer). Although both the condition and cause are similar, the cause is more noble. The author then notes why Fajr is mentioned first in the list: because it is the beginning of the day, or because there is no disagreement on its beginning and end (though later commentary notes there is disagreement), or because Adam was the first to perform Fajr. Curiously, in al-Jami' al-Saghir, Zuhr is mentioned first because it was the first prayer made obligatory on the Prophet. This helps answer the question: how did the Prophet miss Fajr on the morning after the Isra when the five prayers were prescribed? Al-Iraqi answered that the Prophet was asleep, and a sleeper is not accountable. The passage then gives the hadith of Jibril defining the prayer times. Jibril led the Prophet twice at the Kaaba. In the first instance, he performed each prayer at the beginning of its time; in the second, at the end (except Maghrib). This shows the permissible range for each prayer. The Fajr time is from the breaking of true dawn (subh sadiq) until sunrise. The hadith is a key proof for the Hanafi school's timings.

Key Terms
الفجر (al-Fajr): The dawn prayer; its time from true dawn (subh sadiq) to sunrise.
الصبح الصادق (al-subh al-sadiq): True dawn: the horizontal whiteness spreading on the eastern horizon, marking start of Fajr.
الإسراء (al-Isra): The Night Journey of the Prophet from Mecca to Jerusalem, during which the five prayers were prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what marks the beginning of Fajr time?
A) The appearance of a vertical pillar of light in the east.
B) The spread of horizontal whiteness (subh sadiq).
C) The moment the sun rises.
D) The end of the night when darkness is gone.

Key Takeaway
Fajr time is defined by the hadith of Jibril as true dawn to sunrise; this is a foundational ruling with proof in the Hanafi school.

Time of Fajr: From True Dawn to Sunrise
Defining the time of Fajr prayer with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the beginning and end of Fajr prayer time according to the Hanafi school, distinguish true dawn from false dawn, and explain the evidence from the hadith of Jibril.

Core Idea
Fajr time begins with the spreading of true dawn across the horizon and ends at sunrise — the true dawn is horizontal, not vertical.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes the time of Fajr prayer with a clear ruling and prophetic evidence. It not only states the time limits but also clarifies the crucial distinction between the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) and the false dawn (al-fajr al-kadhib), which is essential for correct prayer timing. Additionally, it highlights a subtle intra-Hanafi difference of opinion on the exact moment of the beginning, ultimately favoring the view that the time starts when the whiteness spreads across the horizon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Fajr prayer; its time is from true dawn to sunrise. The ruling is that the prayer is wajib within this time.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jibril (Umm Salama narration) which defines the beginning and end times.
The hadith is a strong indicator (zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalala).
3
Analyze the key term: al-fajr al-sadiq
Distinguish true dawn from false dawn. True dawn is horizontal spreading; false dawn is vertical and follows darkness.
The false dawn appears like a wolf's tail.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars considered the first appearance (bazq) as the beginning, others the spreading. The author mentions this difference.
The disagreement is about the exact moment of the beginning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view: Fajr time begins when the whiteness spreads across the horizon (al-inbashar).
This is the view of al-Marghinani in al-Nihaya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقت الفجر من الصبح الصادق إلى طلوع الشمس الحديث أمامة : أتاني جبريل عند البيت مرتين فصلى بي الظهر في الأولى منهما حين كان الفيء مثل الشرك، ثم صلى العصر حين كان كل شيء مثل ظله ثم صلى المغرب حين وجبت الشمس وأفطر الصائم، ثم صلى العشاء حين غاب الشفق، ثم صلى الفجر حين بزق الفجر وحرم الطعام على الصائم. وصلى المرة الثانية الظهر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثله كوقت العصر بالأمس، ثم صلى العصر حين كان ظل كل شيء مثليه، ثم صلى المغرب لوقته الأول، ثم صلى العشاء الأخيرة حين ذهب ثلث الليل، ثم صلى الصبح حين أسفرت الأرض، ثم التفت جبريل فقال : يا محمد هذا وقت الأنبياء من قبلك، والوقت فيما بين هذين الوقتين. وبزق أي بزغ وهو أول طلوع وقيد بالصادق احترازاً عن الكاذب فإنه من الليل، وهو المستطيل الذي يبدو كذنب الذئب ثم يعقبه الظلام والأوّل المستطير وهو الذي ينتشر ضوءه في الأفق وهي أطراف السماء. وفي السراج الوهاج آخره قبيل طلوع الشمس. وفي المجتبى: واختلف المشايخ في أن العبرة لأوّل طلوعه أو لاستطارته أو لانتشاره .اهـ. والظاهر الأخير لتعريفهم قال في النهاية : الصادق هو البياض المنتشر في الأفق.
He said: (The time of Fajr is from the true dawn to sunrise. The hadith of Umm Salama: Jibril came to me at the House twice and prayed with me Zuhr the first time when the shadow was like the strap, then Asr when everything was like its shadow, then Maghrib when the sun set and the fasting person broke the fast, then Isha when the twilight disappeared, then Fajr when the dawn broke and food was forbidden for the fasting person. And he prayed the second time Zuhr when the shadow of everything was like it as was the time of Asr yesterday, then Asr when the shadow of everything was twice it, then Maghrib at its first time, then Isha when half the night had passed, then Fajr when the earth was bright. Then Jibril turned and said: O Muhammad, this is the time of the prophets before you, and the time is between these two times. And 'bazq' means 'bazagh', which is the first rising. And it is restricted by 'true' (sadiq) to exclude the false dawn, for it is from the night, and it is the elongated one that appears like the tail of a wolf then darkness follows. And the first is the spreading one, which is the one whose light spreads in the horizon, and that is the sides of the sky. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: its end is just before sunrise. In al-Mujtaba: The scholars differed as to whether consideration is for its first rising, its spreading, or its diffusion. The apparent is the last, based on their definition. He said in al-Nihaya: The true dawn is the whiteness that spreads in the horizon.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for the time of Fajr prayer. It begins with a clear statement: the time of Fajr is from true dawn (al-subh al-sadiq) until sunrise. The author then provides the famous hadith of Jibril (peace be upon him) in which he led the Prophet (peace be upon him) in prayer at the two times—the first time at the beginning of each prayer's time, and the second time at the end. For Fajr, the first time was when the dawn broke (bazagha al-fajr) and food became forbidden for the fasting person (indicating the start of the fast), and the second time was when the earth became bright (asfara al-ard). The Prophet was told that the prayer time is between these two times. The author then explains the term 'bazq' as the first appearance of dawn. He distinguishes between the true dawn (al-fajr al-sadiq) and the false dawn (al-fajr al-kadhib). The false dawn is a vertical light that appears like a wolf's tail and is followed by darkness; it is not the start of Fajr time. The true dawn is the horizontal light that spreads across the horizon. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars whether the criterion is the first appearance, the spreading, or the diffusion. The author favors the last, as stated in al-Nihaya: the true dawn is the whiteness that spreads. This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
الصبح الصادق (al-subh al-sadiq): The true dawn, which is the horizontal whiteness that spreads across the horizon, marking the start of Fajr time.
بزق (bazq): The first appearance of the sun or dawn; here used to mean the initial rising of the true dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the beginning of Fajr prayer time in the Hanafi school?
A) The appearance of the false dawn (vertical light)
B) The first appearance of dawn (bazq) according to all scholars
C) The spreading of true dawn (horizontal whiteness)
D) The moment when the sun rises

Key Takeaway
Fajr time begins with the horizontal spread of true dawn and ends at sunrise; the false dawn (vertical light) is not a valid indicator for prayer.

End Time of Zuhr and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Zuhr end time with tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the end of Zuhr time, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and evaluate the tarjih evidence.

Core Idea
Zuhr ends when shadow is twice the object's height excluding fay' — Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi.

The beginning of Zuhr time at zawal (sun's zenith) is agreed upon by all. However, its end time is disputed within the Hanafi school itself. This passage from Bahr al-Raiq presents the two narrations from Abu Hanifa, the view of the Sahibayn, and the detailed tarjih (preference) that establishes the relied-upon position. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to navigate intra-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed beginning
State the consensus on when Zuhr begins based on Qur'an 17:78 and the meaning of zawal.
The Qur'anic phrase 'duluk al-shams' is understood as zawal.
2
State the two positions on the end time
Explain Abu Hanifa's view (shadow twice object excluding fay') and the Sahibayn's view (shadow equal to object excluding fay').
Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration agrees with the Sahibayn.
3
Trace the narrations from Abu Hanifa
Muhammad narrated the twice-length view; Hasan narrated the equal-length view. The commentator cites multiple authorities (al-Bada'i', al-Nihayah, etc.) affirming the twice-length as the correct narration.
The twice-length view is zahir al-riwayah.
4
Follow the tarjih process
Analyze the evidence: the hadith of Jibril (prayed at first length on day one and at second length on day two) and the hadith 'Abridu bi al-Zuhr' (delay due to heat). The latter supports a longer time.
The Sahibayn's view would make the delay hadith redundant.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
Conclude that Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position. The practical effect: praying Zuhr when shadow equals object is valid but makruh according to Abu Hanifa; delaying until twice is optimal.
The fatwa follows Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة. قوله : (والظهر من الزوال إلى بلوغ الظل مثليه سوى الفيء أي وقت الظهر، أما أوّله فمجمع عليه لقوله تعالى أقم الصلاة لدلوك الشمس [الإسراء : ٧٨] أي لزوالها وقيل لغروبها، واللام للتأقيت ذكره البيضاوي. وأما آخره ففيه روايتان عن أبي حنيفة : الأولى رواها محمد عنه ما في الكتاب والثانية رواية الحسن إذا صار ظل كل شيء مثله سوى الفيء وهو قولهما، والأولى قول أبي حنيفة. قال في البدائع: إنها المذكورة في الأصل وهو الصحيح وفي النهاية : إنها ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة. وفي غاية البيان : وبها أخذ أبو حنيفة وهو المشهور عنه . وفي المحيط : والصحيح قول أبي حنيفة . وفي الينابيع : وهو الصحيح عن أبي حنيفة. وفي تصحيح القدوري للعلامة قاسم : إن برهان الشريعة المحبوبي اختاره وعول عليه النسفي ووافقه صدر الشريعة ورجح دليله وفي الغياثية وهو المختار. وفي شرح المجمع للمصنف : إنه مذهب أبي حنيفة وإختاره أصحاب المتون وارتضاه الشارحون، فثبت أنه مذهب أبي حنيفة . فقول الطحاوي وبقولهما نأخذ لا يدل على أنه المذهب ذكرناه، وما ذكره الكركي في الفيص من أنه يفتى بقولهما في العصر والعشاء مسلم في العشاء فقط على ما فيه أيضاً كما سنذكره لهما إمامة جبريل في اليوم الأول في الوقت، وله: قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «أبردوا بالظهر فإن شدة الحر من فيح جهنم» وأشد الحر في ديارهم كان في هذا الوقت وإذا تعارضت الآثار لا ينقضي الوقت بالشك. وذكر شيخ الإسلام أن الاحتياط أن لا يؤخر الظهر إلى المثل وأن لا يصلي العصر حتى يبلغ المثلين
The Book of Prayer. His statement: (And Zuhr is from zawal until the shadow becomes two times the object excluding the fay') i.e., the time of Zuhr. As for its beginning, there is consensus upon it due to His statement, the Most High: 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun' [Al-Isra: 78] meaning its zawal, and it is said its setting, and the lam is for specification, mentioned by al-Baydawi. As for its end, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: the first narrated by Muhammad from him as in the book, and the second the narration of al-Hasan: when the shadow of everything becomes equal to it excluding the fay', and that is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the first is the view of Abu Hanifa. He said in al-Bada'i': It is the one mentioned in al-Asl and it is the correct one. And in al-Nihayah: It is the apparent narration from Abu Hanifa. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: Abu Hanifa adopted it and it is the famous one from him. And in al-Muhit: The correct view is that of Abu Hanifa. And in al-Yanabi': It is the correct view from Abu Hanifa. And in Tasih al-Quduri by Allamah Qasim: Burhan al-Shari'ah al-Mahbubi chose it, al-Nasafi relied upon it, Sadr al-Shari'ah agreed with him, and his proof was preferred, and in al-Ghiyathiyyah it is the chosen view. And in Sharh al-Majma' by the author: It is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, the authors of the matn chose it, and the commentators approved it, so it is established that it is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. So the statement of al-Tahawi 'We take by the view of the two' does not indicate that it is the madhhab, as we mentioned. And what al-Karaki mentioned in al-Fays that fatwa is given by the view of the two regarding Asr and Isha is accepted only for Isha, with what is in it as well, as we will mention. For him (i.e., Abu Hanifa) is the Imamate of Jibril on the first day regarding the time, and for him is his statement, peace be upon him: 'Delay Zuhr, for the intensity of heat is from the raging of Hellfire.' The most intense heat in their lands was at this time. And when the narrations conflict, the time does not end by doubt. And Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that the precaution is not to delay Zuhr to the [shadow equal to] the like, and not to pray Asr until it reaches the two likes.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the end time of Zuhr prayer. The base matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq states that Zuhr time ends when the shadow of an object becomes twice its height, excluding the fay' (the shadow remaining at zawal). The commentator explains that the beginning of Zuhr is agreed upon by consensus (ijma) based on Qur'an 17:78. The end time, however, has two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one transmitted by Muhammad al-Shaybani (as in the book) that the end is when the shadow becomes twice the object, and another from Hasan ibn Ziyad that the end is when the shadow equals the object (like the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The commentator cites multiple authorities (al-Bada'i', al-Nihayah, etc.) affirming that the view of Abu Hanifa is the twice-length end, and this is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. He rebuts al-Tahawi's claim that fatwa is according to the disciples' view, noting that this would only apply to Isha possibly. He then provides Abu Hanifa's proofs: the Imamate of Jibril (hadith indicating Zuhr was prayed when shadow was first length, implying end is at two lengths) and the hadith 'Abridu bi al-Zuhr' (delay Zuhr due to heat), which indicates that the time extends to allow delay. The commentator concludes that precaution is to avoid delaying Zuhr to the first shadow equality and not to pray Asr early.

Key Terms
الفيء (al-fay’): The shadow that remains after zawal (afternoon shadow) as distinct from the morning shadow (zill).
الظل (al-zill): The shadow cast by an object, used generally but specifically for morning shadow in the context of prayer times.
الزوال (al-zawāl): The sun's zenith, when the sun passes its meridian and begins to decline.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, when does the time for Zuhr prayer end?
A) When the shadow of an object equals its height excluding the fay'
B) When the shadow of an object becomes twice its height excluding the fay'
C) At sunset
D) When the sun becomes yellow

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that Zuhr time ends when the shadow is twice the object's height excluding the fay'.

Definition of Fay' and Method to Determine Zawal
Definition of fay' and practical method to determine zawal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fay' and zill in Hanafi fiqh and state the practical method to determine the time of zawal.

Core Idea
Fay' is the returning shadow after zawal; zawal is found when the shadow neither shortens nor lengthens.

Knowing the precise time of zawal (solar noon) is essential for performing the Zuhr prayer at its correct time. The Hanafi school provides a clear method based on observing shadows, distinguishing between pre-zawal zill and post-zawal fay'. This lesson explains the terminology and the practical steps to identify zawal.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish fay' from zill
Identify the linguistic and legal definitions: zill is the morning shadow that decreases as the sun rises; fay' is the afternoon shadow that increases after zawal. The term fay' literally means 'return' because it returns from the west to the east.
Hanafis maintain this distinction strictly, while other schools may use them interchangeably.
2
Understand the stick method
The most authentic method: erect a straight stick on level ground and mark the tip of its shadow. If the shadow shortens, it is pre-zawal; if it lengthens, it is post-zawal; when it neither shortens nor lengthens, that is the moment of zawal.
This method is authoritative according to al-Zuhayriyyah and other primary sources.
3
Learn the stature method as a fallback
If no stick is available, one can estimate using their own height. The majority say a person's shadow at zawal is about seven feet (or six and a half feet per some scholars). These figures are reconciled by measuring from different points of the foot.
The ikhtilaf is resolved by considering the measurement from the heel (seven feet) or the toe (six and a half feet).
4
Note the exception for Makkah and Madinah
On the longest days of the year in these cities, the sun is directly overhead and all shadows disappear temporarily. Therefore, the stick method cannot be used at that moment.
This exception is recorded in al-Mabsut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المغرب: الفيء بوزن الشيء ما نسخ الشمس وذلك بالعشي والجمع أفياء ،وفيوء والظل ما نسخته الشمس وذلك بالغداة. وفي السراج الوهاج والفيء في اللغة اسم للظل بعد الزوال سمي فيأ لأنه فاء من جهة المغرب إلى جهة المشرق أي رجع وبه اندفع ما قيل إن الفيء هو الظل الذي يكون للأشياء وقت الزوال. وفي معرفة الزوال روايات أصحها أن يغرز خشبة مستوية في أرض مستوية ويجعل عند منتهى ظلها ،علامة فإن كان الظل ينقص عن العلامة فالشمس لم تزل، وإن كان الظل يطول ويجاوز الخط علم أنها زالت وإن امتنع الظل من القصر والطول فهو وقت الزوال. كذا في الظهيرية. وفي المجتبى : فإن لم يجد ما يغرزه لمعرفة الفيء والأمثال فليعتبره بقامته، وقامة كل انسان ستة أقدام ونصف بقدمه. وقال الطحاوي وعامة المشايخ : سبعة أقدام ويمكن الجمع بينهما بأن يعتبر سبعة أقدام من طرف سمت الساق، وستة ونصف من طرف الإبهام واعلم أن لكل شيء ظلاً وقت الزوال إلا بمكة والمدينة في أطول أيام السنة لأن الشمس فيها تأخذ الحيطان الأربعة. كذا في المبسوط .
And in al-Mughrib: al-fay' is, in weight like 'shay', what the sun has removed (of shadow) and that is in the afternoon. Its plural is afya' and fuyu'. And al-zill is what the sun has removed (i.e., created) and that is in the morning. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: al-fay' in language is a name for the shadow after zawal; it is called fay' because it returns (faa) from the direction of the west to the direction of the east, i.e., it returned. And by this it is refuted what was said that al-fay' is the shadow that objects have at the time of zawal. And regarding knowing zawal, the most authentic narrations are that one erects a straight stick in level ground and places a mark at the end of its shadow. If the shadow is less than the mark, the sun has not yet declined; if the shadow lengthens and exceeds the line, it is known that it has declined; and if the shadow refrains from shortening or lengthening, that is the time of zawal. This is in al-Zuhayriyyah. And in al-Mujtaba: if one does not find something to erect to know the fay' and the like, then let him estimate it by his stature; the stature of every person is six and a half feet by his foot. Al-Tahawi and the majority of mashayikh said: seven feet. And it is possible to reconcile them: that one considers seven feet from the side of the leg, and six and a half from the side of the thumb. Know that everything has a shadow at the time of zawal except in Makkah and Madinah on the longest days of the year, because the sun there takes the four walls. This is in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage provides a linguistic definition of 'fay'' (returning shadow) and a practical method for determining the time of zawal (solar noon). The commentator distinguishes between 'zill' (morning shadow that recedes) and 'fay'' (afternoon shadow that returns). The method to find zawal: erect a vertical stick on level ground, mark the tip of its shadow; if the shadow shortens, it is pre-zawal; if it lengthens, it is post-zawal; when it neither shortens nor lengthens, that is the moment of zawal. For those without a stick, the stature method is given: a person's height is approximately six and a half feet (or seven feet per al-Tahawi) and the shadow at zawal is nearly equal to the height (though this is for approximation). A unique exception: in Makkah and Madinah on the year's longest days, everything has a shadow except that the sun strikes all four walls (i.e., at zenith, no shadow).

Key Terms
الفيء (al-fay’): The shadow after zawal, called fay' because it returns from the west to the east.
الزوال (al-zawāl): The moment the sun passes its zenith; the time of zawal is when the shadow neither shortens nor lengthens.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which method is considered the most authentic to determine the time of zawal (solar noon)?
A) Watching the sun with the naked eye
B) Using a prayer timetable
C) Erecting a straight stick on level ground and observing its shadow
D) Measuring the length of one's foot

Key Takeaway
Fay' is the returning shadow after zawal; the most authentic method to determine zawal is by observing a stick's shadow when it neither shortens nor lengthens.
