Times for Asr and Maghrib Prayers
Defines Asr and Maghrib times with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for Asr and Maghrib prayer times, cite the hadith evidence, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the end of Asr.

Core Idea
Asr time extends to sunset; Maghrib ends when red twilight vanishes – both proven by authentic hadith.

Accurate knowledge of prayer times is essential for valid salah. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, a major Hanafi commentary, clearly defines the times for Asr and Maghrib prayers based on authentic hadith. It also alerts us to a minority view within the Hanafi school on when Asr ends. Understanding these rulings and their proofs will deepen your appreciation of how the school relies on textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for Asr
The matn states Asr time is 'from it until sunset' – meaning from when the shadow of an object reaches twice its height (excluding the noon fay') until sunset. Recognize that this marks the beginning and end of Asr.
The beginning of Asr is linked to the end of Zuhr; the dispute on Zuhr's end applies here.
2
Locate the hadith proof for Asr
The author cites the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' This shows the time extends until sunset. Understand how this argument (wajh al-dalalah) supports the Hanafi position.
The hadith explicitly ends Asr time at sunset, countering any earlier cutoff.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on Asr
The passage mentions that al-Hasan ibn Ziyad held that Asr ends when the sun yellows (i.e., earlier). Recognize this is a minority view; the relied-upon (mufta bihi) opinion is the one supported by the hadith.
Hasan ibn Ziyad's view is from the 'nawadir' (rare transmissions) and not adopted for fatwa.
4
Identify the ruling for Maghrib
The matn states Maghrib time is 'from it until the disappearance of the twilight.' 'Twilight' (shafaq) in the Hanafi school means the red glow after sunset. So Maghrib begins at sunset and ends when the redness vanishes.
Other schools define shafaq differently (white twilight), leading to a later end for Maghrib.
5
Examine the hadith proof for Maghrib
The author cites the hadith from Muslim: 'The time of Maghrib prayer is as long as the twilight has not vanished.' This directly sets the end point. Note the clarity of the evidence.
No substantial dispute exists within the Hanafi school on Maghrib timing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعصر منه إلى الغروب أي وقت العصر من بلوغ الظل مثليه سوى الفيء إلى غروب الشمس، والخلاف في آخر وقت الظهر جار في أول وقت العصر، وفي آخره خلاف أيضاً فإن الحسن بن زياد يقول : إذا اصفرت الشمس خرج وقت العصر. ولنا رواية الصحيحين من أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر». قوله : (والمغرب منه إلى غروب الشفق) أي وقت المغرب من غروب الشمس إلى غروب الشفق لرواية مسلم وقت صلاة المغرب ما لم يسقط نور الشفق»
His statement: (And Asr from it until sunset) i.e., the time of Asr from when the shadow reaches two times excluding the fay' until sunset. And the dispute regarding the end of Zuhr applies to the beginning of Asr. And there is also a dispute regarding its end: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad says: when the sun becomes yellow, the time of Asr exits. And for us is the narration of the two Sahihs: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught Asr.' His statement: (And Maghrib from it until the disappearance of the twilight) i.e., the time of Maghrib from sunset until the disappearance of the twilight, due to the narration of Muslim: 'The time of Maghrib prayer is as long as the twilight has not vanished.'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage states the rulings for Asr and Maghrib prayer times. For Asr: its beginning is when the shadow reaches twice the object (following the dispute on Zuhr's end), and its end is at sunset. The proof is the hadith in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim that one who catches a rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught the prayer, implying the entire time until sunset. A minority view from Hasan ibn Ziyad says Asr ends when the sun yellows. For Maghrib: the time is from sunset until the red twilight (shafaq) disappears, based on the hadith from Muslim. The text does not mention any dispute on Maghrib here, but later discussions may arise.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The red twilight after sunset, which according to Hanafis defines the end of Maghrib time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the time for Maghrib prayer end?
A) At sunset
B) When the red twilight disappears
C) When the white twilight appears
D) At midnight

Key Takeaway
Asr time extends to sunset, Maghrib ends at the vanishing of red twilight – both established by authentic hadith and relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Time of Asr Prayer: Start and End
Rules the time of Asr prayer and intra-Hanafi dispute on its end.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the start and end times of Asr prayer and apply the hadith proof to determine the end time.

Core Idea
Asr time lasts until sunset; the hadith of 'one rak'ah before sunset' is the decisive proof.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the time of Asr prayer. While the start time is clearly defined as when the shadow of an object reaches twice its height (excluding the fay' shadow), there is a dispute about the end time. The commentary uses a well-known hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim to establish that Asr time continues until sunset, contrary to the opinion of Hasan ibn Ziyad who held it ends when the sun becomes yellow. Understanding this proof is essential for the correct performance of Asr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the start condition for Asr
The start of Asr is when the shadow of an object reaches twice its height, excluding the post-zawal shadow (fay').
The fay' is the shadow at zawal (noon); only the increase beyond that counts.
2
Understand the link between Zuhr end and Asr start
The dispute about the end of Zuhr time directly affects the start of Asr; the same measurement standard applies.
The passage says 'the disagreement regarding the end time of zuhr applies to the beginning of asr.'
3
Recognize the end time dispute
Hasan ibn Ziyad says Asr ends when the sun becomes yellow; the relied-upon Hanafi position says it ends at sunset.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Asr before sunset has caught Asr' proves that the time extends to sunset, because even one rak'ah before sunset makes the prayer valid.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Conclude the operative ruling
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that Asr time lasts until sunset, based on the stronger hadith evidence.
The opinion of Hasan ibn Ziyad is considered weak (marjuh) in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعصر منه إلى الغروب أي وقت العصر من بلوغ الظل مثليه سوى الفيء إلى غروب الشمس، والخلاف في آخر وقت الظهر جار في أول وقت العصر، وفي آخره خلاف أيضاً فإن الحسن بن زياد يقول : إذا اصفرت الشمس خرج وقت العصر. ولنا رواية الصحيحين من أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدرك العصر»(۱) .
His statement: (And al-asr from it to sunset) meaning: the time of asr is from when the shadow reaches twice its length excluding the fay' until sunset. And the disagreement regarding the end time of zuhr applies to the beginning of asr. And regarding its end, there is also disagreement: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad says: when the sun becomes yellow, the time of asr departs. And we have the narration of the two Sahihs: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of asr before the sun sets has caught asr.'
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the matn line concerning the asr prayer time. The author explains that asr time begins when the shadow of an object reaches twice its length, excluding the fay' (the post-zawal shadow). This is based on the end of zuhr time; the disagreement about when zuhr ends also determines when asr begins. There is also a dispute about the end time of asr: al-Hasan ibn Ziyad holds that asr ends when the sun becomes yellow (i.e., before sunset), but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that asr time lasts until sunset, as evidenced by the hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of asr before the sun sets has caught asr.' This hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim serves as the primary proof. The matn does not resolve the ikhtilaf about the beginning of zuhr, but the commentary uses the hadith to affirm the later end time.

Key Terms
الظل مثليه (al-zill mithlayhi): The shadow becomes twice the height of the object, excluding the fay'.
سوى الفيء (siwa al-fay'): Excluding the post-zawal shadow; the fay' is subtracted before doubling.
الغروب (al-ghurub): Sunset; the moment the sun disappears below the horizon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the sun becomes yellow
B) When the shadow becomes twice the height
C) At sunset
D) At the disappearance of twilight

Key Takeaway
Asr time starts when the shadow is twice the object's height (excluding fay') and lasts until sunset, as proved by the hadith of one rak'ah before sunset.

The Shafaq Dispute: Maghrib Time in Hanafi Fiqh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shafaq definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of shafaq, identify the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and state the mufta bihi ruling with its rationale.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa: shafaq is whiteness; Sahibayn: redness — the mufta bihi is the Imam's view.

This lesson examines the famous intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the definition of shafaq (twilight) which determines the end time of maghrib prayer. The difference between redness and whiteness directly affects when isha begins. We will explore the proofs from each side and why the author ultimately prefers the Imam’s view.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what each party holds: Imam Abu Hanifa says shafaq is the whiteness (al-bayad) that remains after redness; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) say it is the redness (al-humra).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not between schools.
2
Examine the dalil of the Sahibayn
Their proof includes the practice of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, and the hadith 'The time of maghrib is as long as the light of shafaq has not fallen', interpreting shafaq as redness.
3
Examine the dalil of Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam's proof is the hadith of Ibn Fudayl: 'The end time of maghrib is when the horizon disappears.' Whiteness disappears after redness, so that marks the true end.
Also cited is the practice of many Companions like Abu Bakr, Umar, etc.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing view
The author rebuts the Sahibayn: their claim that Imam returned to their view is unconfirmed; many Companions held whiteness; the hadith of Ibn Fudayl supports whiteness.
The fatwa on Imam's view is precautionary (ahwat).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If shafaq is redness, maghrib ends earlier; if whiteness, maghrib time extends later. This directly affects the beginning of isha prayer time.
The difference can be significant, especially in summer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمغرب منه إلى غروب الشفق) أي وقت المغرب من غروب الشمس إلى غروب الشفق لرواية مسلم وقت صلاة المغرب ما لم يسقط نور الشفق»(۲) وضبطه الشمني بالثاء بعض النسخ وفي بعضها في الأصل قوله : (وأشد الحز (الخ) أصرح منه ما عن أبي ذر قال : كنا مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في سفر فأراد المؤذن أن يؤذن فقال له : أبرد . ثم أراد أن يؤذن فقال له : أبرد. ثم أراد أن يؤذن فقال له : أبرد حتى ساوى الظل التلول. فقال النبي : إن شدة الحر من فيح جهنم. رواه البخاري في باب الأذان للمسافرين. فقد صرح بأن الظل قد ساوى التلول ولا قدر يدرك لفيء الزوال ذلك الزمان في ديارهم فثبت أنه له صلى الظهر حين صار الظل مثله، ولا يظن به أ أنه صلاها في وقت العصر فكان حجة على أبي يوسف ومحمد وإن لم يكن حجة على من يجوز الجمع في السفر وتمامه في شرح المنية . قوله: (وعندهما وهو رواية عنه الخ) قال في النهر : وإليه رجع الإمام وعليه الفتوى لما (۲) رواه مسلم في كتاب المساجد حديث ١٧١- ١٧٤. وهذه الحاشية في الأصل بعد كلام الدخول. وهو البياض والعشاء والوتر منه إلى الصبح ولا يقدم على العشاء للترتيب ومن لم يجد هو الحمرة وهو المثلثة المفتوحة وهو ثوران حمرته قوله : (وهو البياض أي الشفق هو البياض عند الإمام وهو مذهب أبي بكر الصديق وعمر ومعاذ وعائشة رضي الله عنهم وعندهما وهو رواية عنه قول ابن عباس وابن عمر، وصرح في المجمع بأن عليها الفتوى. ورده المحقق في فتح القدير بأنه لا يساعده رواية ولا دراية، أما الأول فلأنه خلاف الرواية الظاهرة عنه، وأما الثاني فلما في حديث ابن فضيل وإن آخر وقتها حين يغيب الأفق» وغيبوبته بسقوط البياض الذي يعقب الحمرة وإلا كان بادياً ويجيء ما تقدم يعني إذا تعارضت الأخبار لم ينقض الوقت بالشك، ورجحه أيضاً تلميذه قاسم في تصحيح القدوري. وقال في آخره: فثبت أن قول الإمام هو الأصح .اهـ. وبهذا ظهر أنه لا يفتى ويعمل إلا بقول الإمام الأعظم، ولا يعدل عنه إلى قولهما أو قول أحدهما أو غيرهما إلا لضرورة من ضعف دليل أو تعامل بخلافه كالمزارعة وإن صرح المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قولهما كما في هذه المسألة. وفي السراج الوهاج : فقولهما أوسع للناس وقول أبي حنيفة أحوط .
His statement: (And al-maghrib from it to the disappearance of al-shafaq) meaning: the time of maghrib is from sunset to the disappearance of shafaq due to the narration of Muslim: 'The time of maghrib prayer is as long as the light of shafaq has not fallen.' And al-Shamni recorded it with tha' in some copies, and in others in the original: his statement: (wa ashaddu al-hazz) etc. More explicit than it is what is narrated from Abu Dharr who said: We were with the Prophet (peace be upon him) on a journey, and the mu'adhdhin wanted to give the adhan, so he said to him: 'Wait until it becomes cool.' Then he wanted to give the adhan, so he said: 'Wait until it becomes cool.' Then he wanted to give the adhan, so he said: 'Wait until it becomes cool' until the shadow equalled the hummocks. Then the Prophet said: 'Severe heat is from the raging of Hell.' Narrated by al-Bukhari in the chapter of adhan for travellers. He clearly stated that the shadow equalled the hummocks and there was no capacity to perceive the fay' of zawal at that time in their lands, so it is established that he prayed zuhr when the shadow became its like, and it should not be thought that he prayed it in the time of asr. So it was a proof against Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, though not a proof against those who permit combining in travel. Its completion is in Sharh al-Munya. His statement: (And according to them, and it is a narration from him) etc. He said in al-Nahr: the Imam returned to it, and the fatwa is upon it because (2) Narrated by Muslim in Kitab al-Masajid, hadith 171-174. And this marginal note is in the original after the introductory words. And it is the whiteness, and al-isha and al-witr from it to dawn, and one does not give precedence to isha for the sake of order. And whoever does not find it is the redness, and it is with the open tha', and it is the rising of its redness. His statement: (And it is the whiteness) meaning: al-shafaq is the whiteness according to the Imam, and it is the madhhab of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Umar, Mu'adh, and A'isha (may Allah be pleased with them), and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and it is a narration from him, is the saying of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. And it was stated clearly in al-Majma' that the fatwa is upon it. But the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir refuted it by saying that it is supported neither by narration nor by reasoning. As for the first, it contradicts the apparent narration from him; as for the second, because of the hadith of Ibn Fudayl: 'And the end time of it is when the horizon disappears.' And its disappearance is by the setting of the whiteness that follows the redness, otherwise it would be visible. And what came before is meant: if reports conflict, the time is not voided by doubt. And his student Qasim also gave preponderance to it in Tashih al-Quduri. And he said at its end: So it is established that the saying of the Imam is the most correct. By this it became apparent that one does not give fatwa or act except by the saying of the greatest Imam, and one does not turn away from it to their saying or the saying of one of them or others except for necessity: like weakness of proof or practice to the contrary (like muzara'ah), even if the mashayikh stated that the fatwa is upon their saying as in this case. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: Their saying is more expansive for the people, and the saying of Abu Hanifa is more precautionary.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about the definition of shafaq (twilight) and its impact on the end time of maghrib prayer. The author explains that maghrib time lasts from sunset until the shafaq disappears, citing the hadith of Muslim. Then he reports the dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that shafaq is the whiteness (al-bayad) that appears after sunset and lasts until the horizon becomes dark. His proof includes the hadith of Ibn Fudayl about the horizon disappearing. The two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that shafaq is the redness (al-humra) that appears immediately after sunset, and maghrib ends when that redness disappears. This is also a narrated view from Abu Hanifa. The author notes that many later scholars gave fatwa by the students' view (shafaq = redness) because it is more expansive for people. However, the author then examines the arguments: the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir argues that Imam's view is not supported by narration or reasoning, but the author presents counter-arguments, including that Imam's view is more precautionary (ahwat). The passage includes various authorities and sources, including the claim that Imam returned to the students' view later (ruju'), but scholars like Qasim in Tashih al-Quduri reject this return as unproven. Ultimately, the author concludes that the fatwa should be on Imam Abu Hanifa's view (whiteness) as it is the most correct, but acknowledges that many mashayikh prefer the students' view for ease. The practical implication: according to Imam, maghrib time extends until the whiteness disappears, which is later; according to them, it ends earlier with the redness. The passage also briefly mentions the isha and witr times in connection with the shafaq definition.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; disputed whether it is the redness or the whiteness that remains.
البياض (al-bayad): The whiteness that appears after the redness of sunset and remains until the horizon becomes dark.
الحمرة (al-humra): The redness that appears immediately after sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Sahibayn's view is weak and contradicted by all Companions
B) Because the hadith of Ibn Fudayl supports whiteness, and the return (ruju') of Imam is unconfirmed
C) Because the redness view has no hadith evidence
D) Because the majority of other schools also hold whiteness

Key Takeaway
The definition of shafaq in the Hanafi school is whiteness according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is the most correct view, though the students' view (redness) is often used for ease.

Time of Isha and Witr: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Sets isha and witr times with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time of witr prayer according to Imam Abu Hanifa and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with its dalil.

Core Idea
Witr time follows isha time according to Imam; the Sahibayn require witr after isha prayer.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the time for isha and witr prayers, a matter with practical consequences for daily worship. The matn states they share a time window, but the commentary reveals a key disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) about when witr actually begins. We will examine the hadith evidence that drives this difference and the underlying principle linking time to prayer status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Time
State the madhhab's ruling given in the text: isha and witr time is from the disappearance of shafaq to dawn. Note that 'shafaq' is itself disputed (redness vs. whiteness).
The matn does not define shafaq; that dispute is handled elsewhere.
2
Locate the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Find where the commentary splits: Imam Abu Hanifa says witr time is the same as isha time; the Sahibayn say witr time begins after isha prayer. Identify each position clearly.
The pronouns: 'Imam' = Abu Hanifa; 'them' = Abu Yusuf & Muhammad.
3
Trace the Dalil for Each Side
Find the hadith evidence cited. Imam's proof from Abu Dawud: 'between isha and dawn' (without 'prayer'). Sahibayn's proof from a variant: 'between isha prayer and dawn'. Note the critical word difference.
The hadith is about the excellence of witr.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
Explain how the Hanafi response reconciles or prefers Imam's version. The author argues the version without 'prayer' is more general, and the return (ruju') of Imam to Sahibayn is not established.
The response links to the fard/sunnah status of witr.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
State the thamarah al-khilaf: According to Imam, witr is valid immediately after maghrib (once isha time enters). According to Sahibayn, witr must be prayed after performing isha prayer.
This affects when a person may pray witr in congregation or individually.

Source Text

قوله : (والعشاء والوتر منه إلى الصبح) أي وقتهما من غروب الشفق على الخلاف فيه، وكون وقتهما واحداً مذهب الإمام، وعندهما وقت الوتر بعد صلاة العشاء. له حديث أبي داود «إن الله أمدكم بصلاة هي خير لكم من حمر النعم وهي الوتر فجعلها لكم فيما بين العشاء إلى طلوع الفجر » (۱) ولهما ما في بعض طرقه فجعلها لكم فيما بين صلاة العشاء إلى طلوع الفجر والخلاف فيه مبني على أنه فرض أو سنة قوله : (ولا يقدم على العشاء للترتيب) لا ثبت عنه من حمل عامة الصحابة الشفق على الحمرة وإثبات هذا الاسم للبياض قياس في اللغة وهو يجوز . كذا في شرح المجمع. وبهذا التقرير اندفع ما في الفتح من أن هذا الترجيح لا يساعده رواية ولا القوي من الدراية لأنه حيث ثبت رجوعه فقد ساعدته الرواية، ولا شك أن . سبب الرجوع قوي الدراية اهـ . لكن ذكر العلامة قاسم في تصحيحها رجوعه لم يثبت لما نقله الكافة . أن لدن الأئمة الثلاثة وإلى من الآن من حكاية القولين ودعوى حمل عامة الصحابة خلاف المنقول . قال في الاختيار : الشفق البياض قلت : ورواه عبد الرزاق عن مذهب أبي بكر الصديق ومعاذ بن جبل وعائشة رضي الله تعالى عنهم . وهو أبي هريرة وعن عمر بن عبد العزيز ولم ير والبيهقي الشفق الأحمر إلا . عن ابن عمر وتمامه فيه . قوله : (فيما بين صلاة العشاء إلى طلوع الفجر) وظاهر ما أخرج إسحق والطبراني عن عمرو بن العاص وعقبة بن عامر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن الله زادكم صلاة هي خير لكم من حمر النعم وهي لكم فيما بين صلاة العشاء إلى طلوع الفجر » (۱) فإن قلت : ينبغي حمل الرواية على هاتين الروايتين بأن يجعل لفظ صلاة الملفوظ فيهما مقدراً جمعاً بينها وبينهما قلت لقائل أن يقول لا بل الأمر بالقلب فإن العشاء محكم في (۱) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الوتر باب .١ الترمذي في كتاب الوتر باب .١ ابن ماجه في كتاب الإقامة باب ١١٤. الدارمي في كتاب الصلاة باب ۲۰۸.
His statement: (And al-isha and al-witr from it to dawn) meaning: their time is from the disappearance of shafaq, according to the disagreement about it. And that their time is one is the madhhab of the Imam (Abu Hanifa). And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the time of witr is after isha prayer. In support of him (Imam) is the hadith of Abu Dawud: 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer which is better for you than red camels, and it is al-witr, and He has made it for you between isha and dawn.' And in support of them (the two) is what is in some of its chains: 'He has made it for you between isha prayer and dawn.' And the disagreement in it is based on whether it (witr) is fard or sunnah. His statement: (And one does not give precedence to isha for the sake of order) not it is established from him who interpreted the general companions' taking shafaq as redness, and establishing this name for whiteness is qiyas in language and it is permissible. Thus in Sharh al-Majma'. And by this summary, what was in al-Fath that this tarjih is not supported by narration or strong reasoning is repelled, because when his return is established, narration supports it, and there is no doubt that the reason for return is strong reasoning. But the scholar Qasim mentioned in its correction that his return is not established, based on what the majority narrated: that from the time of the three imams until now, the two sayings are narrated, and the claim that the general companions held shafaq as redness contradicts what is transmitted. He said in al-Ikhtiyar: 'Al-shafaq is the whiteness.' I said: And Abd al-Razzaq narrated it from the madhhab of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and A'isha (may Allah be pleased with them). And it is the view of Abu Hurayra, and from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, and al-Bayhaqi regarded only red shafaq except from Ibn Umar, and its completion is therein. His statement: (Between isha prayer and dawn) and it is apparent from what Ishaq and al-Tabarani narrated from Amr ibn al-As and Uqba ibn Amir from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer which is better for you than red camels, and it is for you between isha prayer and dawn.' So if you say: The narration should be interpreted according to these two narrations by making the word 'prayer' in them suppositional, reconciling between them, then you can say: No, rather the matter is the heart, for isha is definitive in (1) Narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Witr, bab 1; al-Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Witr, bab 1; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Iqama, bab 114; al-Darimi in Kitab al-Salah, bab 208.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage deals with the times of isha and witr prayers. The matn states that isha and witr both begin from the disappearance of shafaq (twilight) and last until dawn. The commentary notes a dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that isha and witr have the same time (i.e., witr time begins immediately after isha), while the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that witr time is specifically after isha prayer (i.e., after one has prayed isha). Both sides have hadith evidence: Imam relies on a version of the hadith that says 'between isha and dawn' (without 'prayer'), while they rely on a version that says 'between isha prayer and dawn'. The author explains that this dispute is linked to whether witr is fard or sunnah; if it is fard, it might have its own distinct time. The passage then digresses into the shafaq dispute again, affirming that the Imam's view (shafaq = whiteness) is correct, and that the claim of Imam's return to the students' view is not established. It also mentions the hadith of Amr ibn al-As and Uqba ibn Amir that also refers to 'between isha prayer and dawn', but the author attempts to reconcile by textual interpretation. The footnotes provide the sources for the hadith. The practical outcome: the time for isha and witr is from the end of maghrib (as defined by shafaq) until dawn. The beginning of isha is determined by the shafaq dispute.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after isha; its status is wajib (according to Imam) or sunnah mu'akkadah (according to others).
صلاة العشاء (salat al-isha): The night prayer; its time begins after shafaq disappears.
الشفق (al-shafaq): Twilight after sunset; disputed as redness or whiteness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The Imam's version mentions 'red camels'
D) The Sahibayn's version mentions 'dawn' instead of 'fajr'

Key Takeaway
Witr time is inherently tied to isha time; the dispute is whether it begins simultaneously or after isha prayer.

Definition of Shafaq and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Isha Start Time
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of shafaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi definitions of shafaq, identify the evidence for each, and explain why the fatwa follows the Sahibayn despite Abu Hanifa's view being stronger.

Core Idea
Shafaq: Abu Hanifa says white, Sahibayn say red; the stronger proof is white, but fatwa is on red for ease.

The start time of Isha prayer depends on the disappearance of shafaq (twilight). But what exactly is shafaq? Inside the Hanafi school, Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed. This lesson unpacks their proofs and shows how later Hanafi scholars navigated between evidence and practical ease.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what each side defines shafaq as: Abu Hanifa says the white twilight (al-bayad); the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say the red twilight (al-humra).
The source also mentions Companions supporting each view.
2
Examine the proofs
Abu Hanifa's proof includes the hadith of Ibn Fudayl that the time ends when the horizon disappears, which only occurs after the white twilight is gone. He also cites the practice of many Companions. The Sahibayn rely on a linguistic interpretation of shafaq as redness and some narrations from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar.
The hadith is a dalil naqli; the linguistic argument is a dalil aqli.
3
Analyze the tarjih
The muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir and others preferred Abu Hanifa's view, calling it the most correct (asahh) in terms of transmission and reasoning.
The principle: when reports conflict, the time is not terminated by doubt.
4
Identify the fatwa practice
Despite the stronger proof, many later scholars gave fatwa on the Sahibayn's view for ease (واقع) and to accommodate people's practice, as stated in al-Majma' and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
This illustrates the concept of fatwa according to ease (taysir) within the school.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, this means Isha time starts earlier (after redness) if following the fatwa view, and later (after whiteness) if following Abu Hanifa's view. The precautionary (ahwat) approach is to follow Abu Hanifa.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view, but one may follow the Imam if cautious.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو البياض أي الشفق هو البياض عند الإمام وهو مذهب أبي بكر الصديق وعمر ومعاذ وعائشة رضي الله عنهم وعندهما وهو رواية عنه قول ابن عباس وابن عمر، وصرح في المجمع بأن عليها الفتوى. ورده المحقق في فتح القدير بأنه لا يساعده رواية ولا دراية، أما الأول فلأنه خلاف الرواية الظاهرة عنه، وأما الثاني فلما في حديث ابن فضيل وإن آخر وقتها حين يغيب الأفق» وغيبوبته بسقوط البياض الذي يعقب الحمرة وإلا كان بادياً ويجيء ما تقدم يعني إذا تعارضت الأخبار لم ينقض الوقت بالشك، ورجحه أيضاً تلميذه قاسم في تصحيح القدوري. وقال في آخره: فثبت أن قول الإمام هو الأصح .اهـ. وبهذا ظهر أنه لا يفتى ويعمل إلا بقول الإمام الأعظم، ولا يعدل عنه إلى قولهما أو قول أحدهما أو غيرهما إلا لضرورة من ضعف دليل أو تعامل بخلافه كالمزارعة وإن صرح المشايخ بأن الفتوى على قولهما كما في هذه المسألة. وفي السراج الوهاج : فقولهما أوسع للناس وقول أبي حنيفة أحوط .
And it is the whiteness, meaning the shafaq (twilight) is the whiteness according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa), and it is the madhhab of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Umar, Muadh, and Aisha (may Allah be pleased with them). And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and it is a narration from him, it is the statement of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. And it was stated in al-Majma' that the fatwa is upon it. But the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir rejected it saying that it is not supported by transmission or reasoning. As for the first, because it contradicts the apparent transmission from him; as for the second, due to the hadith of Ibn Fudayl: 'And its last time is when the horizon disappears' and its disappearance is when the whiteness that follows the redness falls, otherwise it would be visible. And what was mentioned earlier comes, meaning that when reports conflict, the time is not terminated by doubt. And his student Qasim also preferred it in Tashih al-Quduri, and said at the end: 'Thus it is established that the statement of the Imam is the most correct.' End quote. And by this it becomes apparent that fatwa and practice are only according to the statement of the greatest Imam, and one should not turn away from it to their statement or the statement of one of them or others except for necessity due to weakness of evidence or customary practice to the contrary, like muzara'ah, even if the scholars have stated that the fatwa is upon their statement as in this issue. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: 'Their statement is easier for the people, and the statement of Abu Hanifa is more precautionary.'
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of shafaq (twilight), which determines the start time of the Isha prayer. The matn states that shafaq is the whiteness (al-bayad). The commentator clarifies that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, supported by several prominent Companions. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), however, hold that shafaq is the redness (al-humra), which is also a narration from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. Although many scholars later issued fatwa based on the Sahibayn's view for practicality, the commentator leans toward Abu Hanifa's view as more correct based on hadith and reasoning. He cites the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir who insisted that the correct view is that which is supported by transmission (riwaya) and reason (diraya). The hadith of Ibn Fudayl indicates that the last time of Isha is when the horizon disappears, which occurs when the white twilight following the redness vanishes. If the white twilight were not considered, the horizon would still be visible. The commentator also mentions the principle that when transmitted reports conflict, the time is not assumed to have ended due to doubt. Thus, despite the fatwa being on the Sahibayn's view, the Imam's position is taken as the more cautious (ahwat) and correct in principle.

Key Terms
الشفق (shafaq): Twilight; the light that appears after sunset, used to mark the beginning of Isha time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The red twilight
B) The white twilight
C) The disappearance of all light
D) The first darkness after sunset

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's treatment of shafaq shows how later scholars sometimes adopt the weaker proof for practical ease while still acknowledging the stronger view.

Time of Witr and the Obligation of Tartib between Isha and Witr
Dispute on whether Witr time begins at disappearance of twilight or after Isha, and the obligation of tartib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the time of Witr and the obligation of tartib between Isha and Witr, and evaluate the evidence from the Sahibayn's differing view.

Core Idea
Witr's time and its connection to Isha: a dispute rooted in whether Witr is fard or sunnah.

The passage examines two interrelated issues: the time window for Witr and whether a specific order between Isha and Witr is obligatory. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that both Isha and Witr share the same time from twilight to dawn, while the Sahibayn say Witr's time begins only after performing Isha. This difference leads to a further question: may one pray Witr before Isha, and if done forgetfully, is it valid? The discussion also reveals that the ruling on tartib (order) depends on Witr's legal nature—whether it is fard/wajib or sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two debated issues
The passage discusses the time of Witr and the obligation of tartib (order) between Isha and Witr. Both issues are connected because the ruling on tartib hinges on whether Witr is fard or sunnah.
2
State the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa
Imam holds that the time for Witr is from the disappearance of twilight until dawn, same as Isha. He also holds that tartib is wajib, but if one forgetfully prays Witr before Isha, it is valid.
His evidence is the hadith without the word 'prayer': 'between Isha and dawn'.
3
State the positions of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn hold that Witr's time begins after the Isha prayer. They also hold that tartib is a condition for validity; if Witr is prayed before Isha even forgetfully, it must be repeated.
Their evidence is the hadith with the word 'prayer': 'between the Isha prayer and dawn'.
4
Analyze how the legal nature of Witr affects tartib
The dispute over tartib is built upon whether Witr is fard/wajib (Imam) or sunnah (Sahibayn). For Imam, since both are fard, the order is wajib but not a condition. For Sahibayn, since Witr is a sunnah tied to Isha, the order is a condition.
This explains why forgetfulness excuses it in Imam's view but not in Sahibayn's.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If someone prays Witr before Isha forgetfully, according to Imam it is valid and no repetition; according to Sahibayn, it must be repeated. The mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn for caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والعشاء والوتر منه إلى الصبح) أي وقتهما من غروب الشفق على الخلاف فيه، وكون وقتهما واحداً مذهب الإمام، وعندهما وقت الوتر بعد صلاة العشاء. له حديث أبي داود «إن الله أمدكم بصلاة هي خير لكم من حمر النعم وهي الوتر فجعلها لكم فيما بين العشاء إلى طلوع الفجر » ولهما ما في بعض طرقه فجعلها لكم فيما بين صلاة العشاء إلى طلوع الفجر والخلاف فيه مبني على أنه فرض أو سنة قوله : (ولا يقدم على العشاء للترتيب) أي لا يقدم الوتر على العشاء لوجوب الترتيب بين العشاء والوتر ولأنهما فرضان عند الإمام وإن كان أحدهما اعتقاداً والآخر عملاً فأفاد أنه عند التذكر حتى لو قدم الوتر ناسياً فإنه يجوز، وعندهما يعيده وعند النسيان أيضاً لأنه سنة العشاء تبعاً لها فلا يثبت حكمه قبلها كالركعتين بعد العشاء. وقول الشارح وعندهما لا يجوز فيه نظر لأنه سنة عندهما يجوز تركه أصلاً، وأشار إلى أن الترتيب بينه وبين غيره واجب عنده كما سيصرح به في باب الفوائت، وعندهما ليس بواجب لسنيته. وفي النهاية : ثم إنهما يوافقان أبا حنيفة في وجوب القضاء، فلو كانت سنة لما وجب القضاء كما في سائر السنن ومراده من الوجوب الثبوت لا المصطلح عليه لأن أداءه عندهما سنة فلا يكون القضاء واجباً عندهما وإلا فهو مشكل والله سبحانه أعلم. قوله : (فيما بين صلاة العشاء إلى طلوع الفجر) وظاهر ما أخرج إسحق والطبراني عن عمرو بن العاص وعقبة بن عامر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن الله زادكم صلاة هي خير لكم من حمر النعم وهي لكم فيما بين صلاة العشاء إلى طلوع الفجر » (۱) فإن قلت : ينبغي حمل الرواية على هاتين الروايتين بأن يجعل لفظ صلاة الملفوظ فيهما مقدراً جمعاً بينها وبينهما قلت لقائل أن يقول لا بل الأمر بالقلب فإن العشاء محكم في (۱) رواه أبو داود في كتاب الوتر باب .١ الترمذي في كتاب الوتر باب .١ ابن ماجه في كتاب الإقامة باب ١١٤. الدارمي في كتاب الصلاة باب ۲۰۸.
His statement: (and the Isha and the Witr are from it until dawn) meaning both their times are from the setting of the twilight according to the disagreement on it. And that their time is one is the madhhab of the Imam (Abu Hanifa), and according to them (Sahibayn) the time of Witr is after the Isha prayer. He has the hadith of Abu Dawud: 'Indeed Allah has granted you a prayer which is better for you than red camels, and it is the Witr. He has made it for you between Isha and dawn.' And they (Sahibayn) have what is in some of its chains: 'He has made it for you between the Isha prayer and dawn.' And the disagreement is built upon whether it is fard or sunnah. His statement: (And do not advance it before Isha due to order) meaning do not advance Witr before Isha due to the obligation of order between Isha and Witr, and because both are fard according to the Imam, even if one is by belief and the other by action. So it indicates that when remembering, even if one prays Witr forgetfully, it is permissible. According to them (Sahibayn), he repeats it, and also in case of forgetfulness, because it is sunnah of Isha, dependent on it, so its ruling is not established before it, like the two rak'ahs after Isha. And the statement of the commentator 'and according to them it is not permissible' requires reflection, because it is sunnah according to them and may be left entirely. And he indicated that order between it and others is obligatory according to him, as he will clarify in the chapter of missed prayers, and according to them it is not obligatory due to its sunnah nature. And in al-Nihayah: Then they (Sahibayn) agree with Abu Hanifa on the obligation of making up (qada'), for if it were sunnah, qada' would not be obligatory as in other sunnahs. And he intends by obligation the established nature, not the technical term, because performing it according to them is sunnah, so qada' would not be obligatory according to them. Otherwise it is problematic, and Allah knows best. His statement: (between the Isha prayer and dawn) and apparent from what Ishaq and al-Tabarani narrated from Amr ibn al-As and Uqba ibn Amir from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him: 'Indeed Allah has increased for you a prayer which is better for you than red camels, and it is for you between the Isha prayer and dawn.' If you say: one should interpret the narration by making the word 'prayer' in both implied, to reconcile between them, then one could say: no, rather the matter is related to the heart, for Isha is definitive in the hadith... (footnote).
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage discusses two related issues: the time of Witr prayer and the obligation of order (tartib) between Isha and Witr. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the time for both Isha and Witr begins at the disappearance of twilight (whichever definition is taken) and lasts until dawn. Thus, they share the same window. The Sahibayn hold that Witr's time begins only after the Isha prayer is performed. The proof for Imam is the hadith 'between Isha and dawn' without the word 'prayer', while the Sahibayn rely on a version that says 'between the Isha prayer and dawn'. The commentator notes that this difference is rooted in whether Witr is considered fard (Imam) or sunnah (Sahibayn). Concerning tartib, the Imam holds that Witr must not be offered before Isha because both are fard, and order between fard acts is obligatory. The Sahibayn consider Witr sunnah, so order is not obligatory, but they still require repetition if one prays Witr before Isha forgetfully, as it is connected to Isha. The commentator also clarifies that the Sahibayn agree with Imam on the obligation of qada' (making up) for Witr, which seems contradictory if it is only sunnah, but he explains that 'obligation' here means fixed/established, not the technical fard. The additional discussion on the hadith variants attempts to reconcile the wording.

Key Terms
الترتيب (tartib): The obligatory order between prayers, specifically that Witr must be performed after Isha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does the time of Witr prayer begin?
A) After the Isha prayer is performed
B) At the disappearance of the twilight
C) After midnight
D) At true dawn

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on Witr's time and tartib illustrates how differences in hadith interpretation and the legal nature of an act (fard vs sunnah) affect ritual practice.

Obligation of Isha and Witr When Their Time Is Not Found: Ruling and Grammatical Parsing
Ruling with grammatical parsing on Isha/Witr obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Isha and Witr for those in high latitudes, explain the intra-madhhab dispute, and parse the Arabic construction 'man lam yajid waqtahuma lam yajaba'.

Core Idea
Absence of the full prayer time lifts the obligation; the Arabic pronoun omission is grammatically problematic in this construction.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a rare but real fiqh problem: what if you live where night is so short that Isha time does not fully appear? The author gives the ruling and then launches into a lengthy grammatical justification of the matn's wording. This lesson will unpack both the legal ruling on the obligation of Isha and Witr and the intricate Arabic grammar behind the phrase 'man lam yajid waqtahuma lam yajaba'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and exceptional scenario
The act under consideration is the Isha and Witr prayers. The exceptional scenario is when the full time interval for these prayers does not occur recognizably, e.g., in high latitudes where dawn appears before twilight disappears.
2
State the ruling from the matn
The matn states: 'Whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory.' This means that if the complete prayer time is absent, the obligation is lifted.
3
Examine the proof and fatwa
The author cites al-Baqqali's fatwa, which draws an analogy to the case of a person missing hands: just as washing hands is dropped, so is the prayer obligation. He then cites the hadith 'Witr is a right...' to support obligation in normal circumstances.
The hadith is used to strengthen Abu Hanifa's view, but the exception remains based on absence of cause.
4
Note the intra-madhhab dispute
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir) argue that the prayers are obligatory even in such regions. The author refutes this by emphasizing the absence of the time condition.
The mufta bihi follows al-Baqqali: not obligatory.
5
Analyze the grammatical structure
The grammarian explains that the pronoun referring back to 'man' is omitted in the predicate 'lam yajaba', which is normally not allowed. He examines both possibilities for 'man' (relative pronoun or conditional) and shows why the omission is considered faulty.
This parsing exercise illustrates the importance of precise Arabic in legal texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن لم يجد وقتهما لم يجبا) أي العشاء والوتر كما لو كان في بلد يطلع فيه الفجر قبل أن يغيب الشفق كبلغارفي أو قصر ليالي السنة فيما حكاه لعدم السبب وأفتى به البقالي كما يسقط غسل اليدين من الوضوء عن مقطوعهما من المرفقين، وأفتى بعضهم بوجوبها واختاره المحقق في فتح القدير بثبوت الفرق بين عدم محل الوقت وصلاة العشاء محتمل له فإنه يقال آتيك لصلاة كذا والمراد آتيك لوقتها، فيحمل عليه كما هو القاعدة في رد المحتمل إلى المحكم عند صورة التعارض، وقد ذكر غير واحد نظير هذا فيما روي عنه أنه قال المستحاضة تتوضأ لوقت كل صلاة وأنه قال تتوضأ لكل صلاة» (۱) : ثم في هذا الحديث دلالة على ما ذهب إليه أبو حنيفة من الوجوب ويقوي ذلك قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الوتر حق فمن لم يوتر فليس منا (۲) رواه أبو داود والحاكم وصححه إلى غير ذلك. اهـ. ابن أمير حاج. قوله: ( ومن لم يجد وقتهما لم يجبا أي لم يجبا عليه فحذف العائد على من وهو لا يسوغ حذفه في مثله ، سواء كانت من موصولة أو شرطية . أم إذا كانت موصولة فلأنها مبتدأ وما بعدها صلتها ولم يجبا خبر المبتدأ، والخبر متى كان جملة فلا بد من ضمير يعود إلى المبتدأ، ولا يجوز حذفه إلا إذا كان منصوباً في الشعر كقوله : وخالد يحمد سادتنا أي يحمده أو كان مجروراً بشرط أن لا يؤدي إلى تهيئة العامل للعمل وقطعه عنه كقولهم السمن منوان بدرهم أي منه وأما إذا أدى فلا يسوغ حذفه، فلا يقال زيد مررت» وهذا منه. وإما إذا كانت شرطية فلأن اسم الشرط أو ما أضيف إليه لا بد في الجملة الواقعة جواباً له عليه فتقول من يقم أقم معه» و «غلام من تكرم أكرمه ولا يجوز من يقم أقم» ولا «غلام من تكرم أكرم فكذا هذا كذا في التبيين قوله : ( واختاره المحقق في فتح القدير الخ) أقول: رده العلامة
His statement: (And whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory) meaning Isha and Witr, as if one is in a country where dawn appears before twilight disappears, like Bulgar, or the nights are short throughout the year as reported, due to the absence of the cause, and al-Baqqali gave fatwa accordingly, just as washing the hands in ablution is dropped for one whose hands are cut off at the elbows. And some gave fatwa of their obligation, and the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir chose it, establishing the difference between the non-existence of the place of time and the Isha prayer being probable for it, for one says 'I will come to you at the prayer of such and such' meaning at its time, so it is interpreted accordingly, as is the rule of referring the probable to the definitive when there is conflict. And many have mentioned a similar case in what was narrated from him that he said: 'The mustahada performs wudu for the time of every prayer.' and that he said: 'She performs wudu for every prayer.' Then in this hadith there is evidence for what Abu Hanifa held of obligation, and that is strengthened by his saying, peace be upon him: 'Witr is a right, so whoever does not pray Witr is not of us.' Related by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim and he authenticated it, etc. End quote. Ibn Amir Hajj. His statement: (And whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory) meaning they are not obligatory on him. So the pronoun referring back to 'who' was omitted, and such omission is not permissible in this case, whether 'man' is a relative pronoun or a conditional particle. If it is a relative pronoun, then it is the subject and what follows is the relative clause, and 'they are not obligatory' is the predicate of the subject. Whenever the predicate is a sentence, there must be a pronoun returning to the subject, and its omission is not allowed unless it is accusative in poetry, like his saying: 'And Khalid is praised by our masters' meaning 'they praise him', or if it is in the genitive on condition that it does not lead to preparing the operator for action and then cutting it off, like their saying: 'Butter: two manns for a dirham' meaning 'of it'. But if it does lead to that, omission is not permissible. So one does not say 'Zaid I passed by' and this is from that. If it is a conditional particle, then the conditional noun or what is annexed to it must have a pronoun in the sentence that is its answer, so you say 'Whoever stands, I stand with him' and 'The slave of whoever you honor, I honor him.' It is not permissible to say 'Whoever stands, I stand' nor 'The slave of whoever you honor, I honor.' So this is similar, as in al-Tabyin. His statement: (and the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir chose it) I say: the scholar refuted it.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage addresses the obligation of Isha and Witr for individuals living in regions where the full time interval between twilight and dawn does not occur (e.g., very high latitudes with short nights or continuous daylight). The matn states that if a person does not 'find' the time for these prayers, they are not obligatory. The commentator gives an example: if in a country dawn appears before the twilight of the previous night has fully disappeared (like Bulgar), or if the nights are very short, then the prayers are not wajib because the causal condition (the existence of the full time) is absent. Al-Baqqali gave fatwa this way, analogizing it to the case of a person missing hands: they are not required to wash them in wudu. However, some scholars held they are obligatory, and the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir chose that view, arguing that the phrase 'prayer' can be interpreted as 'time for prayer' and thus obligation remains. The commentator cites hadith evidence for the obligation of Witr, strengthening Abu Hanifa's view. Following this legal discussion, the passage provides a detailed grammatical analysis of the Arabic construction 'man lam yajid waqtahuma lam yajaba' (whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory). The grammarian explains that the pronoun referring back to 'man' is omitted in the predicate, which is not normally permissible in Arabic. He explores both possibilities: 'man' as a relative pronoun or conditional particle, and explains why the omission occurs, referencing examples from Arabic usage and poetry. This grammatical excursus is typical of the sharh style, ensuring the student understands the precise linguistic structure of the matn.

Key Terms
لم يجد (lam yajid): To not find or perceive; here meaning the full time period for the prayer does not occur in a recognizable way.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa of al-Baqqali, what is the ruling on Isha and Witr for someone in a land where dawn appears before the twilight of the previous night disappears?
A) They must still perform them, but can combine
B) They are not obligatory
C) They are obligatory but must be delayed
D) They are optional

Key Takeaway
The existence of a valid prayer time is a necessary condition for the obligation of Isha and Witr; if it is absent, the prayers are not obligatory, following al-Baqqali's fatwa.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Obligation of Witr and Order with 'Isha
Commentary on intra-Hanafi dispute on Witr obligation and order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the obligation of Witr and the precedence order between 'Isha and Witr, and identify the evidence for each position.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, but sunnah for the Sahibayn—this determines whether order with 'Isha is required.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling on performing Witr prayer before 'Isha. The key intra-Hanafi dispute is whether Witr is wajib or sunnah, and whether the order between the two prayers is required. The commentator presents the hadith evidence and clarifies the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, along with the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act and ruling
Focus on the act of praying Witr before 'Isha. Determine what exactly is disputed: the obligation of Witr itself and the requirement of order.
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) and its proof
According to Abu Hanifa, Witr is wajib and must be performed after 'Isha. If forgotten and prayed first, it is valid. The proof is the hadith: 'Witr is a right, so whoever does not observe Witr is not from us.' The word 'haqq' indicates obligation.
3
State the Sahibayn position and their proof
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, Witr is a sunnah mu'akkadah of 'Isha, so it cannot be valid before 'Isha. They compare it to the two rak'ahs after 'Isha (which are sunnah and must follow the fard). Their reasoning: since it is a sunnah, the order is not obligatory, and praying it before 'Isha is invalid.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if someone prays Witr before 'Isha forgetfully, according to Abu Hanifa it is valid; according to the Sahibayn, he must repeat it. This difference arises from the nature of Witr: wajib vs sunnah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator supports Abu Hanifa with the hadith. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that Witr is wajib, and the order is obligatory. Hence, the forgetful case is deemed valid (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي لا يقدم الوتر على العشاء لوجوب الترتيب بين العشاء والوتر ولأنهما فرضان عند الإمام وإن كان أحدهما اعتقاداً والآخر عملاً فأفاد أنه عند التذكر حتى لو قدم الوتر ناسياً فإنه يجوز، وعندهما يعيده وعند النسيان أيضاً لأنه سنة العشاء تبعاً لها فلا يثبت حكمه قبلها كالركعتين بعد العشاء. وقول الشارح وعندهما لا يجوز فيه نظر لأنه سنة عندهما يجوز تركه أصلاً، وأشار إلى أن الترتيب بينه وبين غيره واجب عنده كما سيصرح به في باب الفوائت، وعندهما ليس بواجب لسنيته. وفي النهاية : ثم إنهما يوافقان أبا حنيفة في وجوب فلو كانت سنة لما وجب القضاء كما في سائر السنن ومراده من الوجوب الثبوت لا المصطلح عليه لأن أداءه عندهما سنة فلا يكون القضاء واجباً عندهما وإلا فهو مشكل والله سبحانه أعلم. قوله : (ومن لم يجد وقتهما لم يجبا أي العشاء والوتر كما لو كان في بلد يطلع فيه الفجر قبل أن يغيب الشفق كبلغارفي أو قصر ليالي السنة فيما حكاه لعدم السبب وأفتى به البقالي كما يسقط غسل اليدين من الوضوء عن مقطوعهما من المرفقين، وأفتى بعضهم بوجوبها واختاره المحقق في فتح القدير بثبوت الفرق بين عدم محل صاحب البلدان الوقت وصلاة العشاء محتمل له فإنه يقال آتيك لصلاة كذا والمراد آتيك لوقتها، فيحمل عليه كما هو القاعدة في رد المحتمل إلى المحكم عند صورة التعارض، وقد ذكر غير واحد نظير هذا فيما روي عنه أنه قال المستحاضة تتوضأ لوقت كل صلاة وأنه قال تتوضأ لكل صلاة» (۱) : ثم في هذا الحديث دلالة على ما ذهب إليه أبو حنيفة من الوجوب ويقوي ذلك قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم الوتر حق فمن لم يوتر فليس منا (۲) رواه أبو داود والحاكم وصححه إلى غير ذلك. اهـ. ابن أمير حاج. قوله: (ومن لم يجد وقتهما لم يجبا أي لم يجبا عليه فحذف العائد على من وهو لا يسوغ حذفه في مثله ، سواء كانت من موصولة أو شرطية . أم إذا كانت موصولة فلأنها مبتدأ وما بعدها صلتها ولم يجبا خبر المبتدأ، والخبر متى كان جملة فلا بد من ضمير يعود إلى المبتدأ، ولا يجوز حذفه إلا إذا كان منصوباً في الشعر كقوله : وخالد يحمد سادتنا أي يحمده أو كان مجروراً بشرط أن لا يؤدي إلى تهيئة العامل للعمل وقطعه عنه كقولهم السمن منوان بدرهم أي منه وأما إذا أدى فلا يسوغ حذفه، فلا يقال زيد مررت» وهذا منه. وإما إذا كانت شرطية فلأن اسم الشرط أو ما أضيف إليه لا بد في الجملة الواقعة جواباً له عليه فتقول من يقم أقم معه» و «غلام من تكرم أكرمه ولا يجوز من يقم أقم» ولا «غلام من تكرم أكرم فكذا هذا كذا في التبيين قوله : ( واختاره المحقق في فتح القدير الخ) أقول: رده العلامة يستلزم العشاء يجب الفرض وبين سببه الجعلي الذي جعل علامة على الوجوب الخفي الثابت في نفس الأمر وجواز تعدد المعرفات للشيء، فإنتفاء الوقت انتفاء المعرف وانتفاء الدليل على الشيء لا انتفاءه لجواز دليل آخر وهو ما توطأت عليه أخبار الإسراء من فرض الله الصلاة خمساً إلى آخره. والصحيح أنه لا ينوي القضاء لفقد وقت الأداء، ومن أفتى بوجوب على قوله الوتر أيضاً
He said: Do not present Witr before 'Isha due to the obligation of order between 'Isha and Witr and because both are obligatory according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] even though one is in belief and the other in action. So it indicates that it is upon remembrance, so if he presented Witr forgetfully, it is permissible. According to them (the two companions), he repeats it even in forgetfulness because it is a sunnah of 'Isha, subordinate to it, so its ruling does not take effect before it, like the two rak'ahs after 'Isha. The commentator's statement 'and according to them it is not permissible' is debatable because it is a sunnah according to them, and it is permissible to leave it entirely. He indicated that order between it and others is obligatory according to him (Abu Hanifa), as he will clarify in the chapter of missed prayers, and according to them it is not obligatory due to its being a sunnah. In al-Nihayah: Then they (the two companions) agree with Abu Hanifa on obligation, but if it were a sunnah, then qada would not be obligatory as in other sunnahs. His intention from 'obligation' is affirmation (thubut) not the technical meaning, because performing it according to them is sunnah, so qada would not be obligatory according to them, otherwise it is problematic. And Allah knows best. His statement: 'And whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory' meaning 'Isha and Witr, as if he is in a country where dawn appears before sunset (like Bulghar?) or during short nights of the year as he narrated, due to absence of cause. Al-Baqqali gave fatwa accordingly, just as washing the hands in wudu drops for one whose hands are cut off at the elbows. Some gave fatwa of their obligation, and al-Muhaqqiq (Ibn al-Humam) in Fath al-Qadir chose the existence of a difference between the absence of the place of time and the prayer of 'Isha being probable for it... etc. And in this hadith is evidence for what Abu Hanifa held of obligation, and it is strengthened by his saying: 'Witr is a right, so whoever does not observe Witr is not from us.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim and authenticated, etc. End of Ibn Amir Haj. His statement: (And whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory) meaning they are not obligatory upon him. So the pronoun referring back to 'who' is omitted, which is not permissible in such a case, whether 'man' is a relative pronoun or conditional... etc. His statement: (And al-Muhaqqiq chose in Fath al-Qadir...) I say: al-Allamah [al-Halabi] refuted him. It necessitates that 'Isha is obligatory... and between its procedural cause which is made a sign for the hidden obligation established in essence, and the permissibility of multiple identifiers for a thing. So the absence of time is the absence of the identifier, and the absence of evidence for a thing is not the absence of the thing itself because another evidence is possible, and that is what the narratives of al-Isra agreed upon of Allah making the five prayers obligatory etc. The correct view is that he does not intend qada due to lack of time for performance, and whoever gave fatwa of obligation...
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Kanz al-Daqa'iq matn regarding the obligation of 'Isha and Witr and the recommended timings. The commentator first explains that Witr must not be performed before 'Isha due to the required order between them. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, both are obligatory (one in belief, the other in action), so if one forgets and prays Witr first, it is valid but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require repetition. The Sahibayn consider Witr a sunnah of 'Isha, so it cannot be valid before 'Isha. The commentator then discusses the case of a person who lives in a region where the time for 'Isha does not occur (e.g., polar regions). The matn says: 'Whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory.' Some scholars, like al-Baqqali, give fatwa that the prayers are not obligatory due to absence of cause, while others (including Ibn al-Humam) argue they are still obligatory based on the principle that absence of evidence is not evidence of absence. The commentator presents a hadith: 'Witr is a right, so whoever does not observe Witr is not from us' as evidence for Abu Hanifa's view of obligation. The latter part of the passage is a grammatical analysis of the phrase 'man lam yajid waqtahuma lam yajiba' (whoever does not find their time, they are not obligatory), explaining the omission of the pronoun and the rules of Arabic grammar. The commentator then addresses a refutation by al-Halabi against Ibn al-Humam's choice. The passage ends with the summary that the correct view is that one does not intend qada (make-up) for the missed prayers due to the absence of time for performance, but some have given fatwa of obligation.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after 'Isha, typically three rak'ahs.
الترتيب (al-tartib): The required order between prayers, here between 'Isha and Witr.
القضاء (al-qada): Making up a missed prayer after its time has passed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone prays Witr before 'Isha forgetfully, based on the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid and no repetition is needed.
C) It is valid only if done intentionally.
D) It is invalid only if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on Witr's obligation determines whether praying it before 'Isha is valid in forgetfulness; the mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa's view of wajib, making it valid.

Recommended Delays for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr Prayers
Commentary on recommended timings for three prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended timings for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr prayers according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Delaying Fajr to isfar, Zuhr to cooler time, and Asr while sun is white are recommended, not required.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the recommended timings for three prayers: Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr. The commentary cites hadith evidence and addresses an intra-Hanafi disagreement over Fajr timing. Understanding these recommendations helps you align your practice with the sunnah while avoiding misconceptions about obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer and the recommended timing
For Fajr, the recommendation is isfar (brightness). For Zuhr in summer, it is ibrad (delaying until cooler). For Asr, it is delaying as long as the sun remains white.
Note that these are recommendations (mandub), not obligations.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The text cites several ahadith: for Fajr, 'Be bright with Fajr' (Sunan al-Arba'ah) and 'Whenever you become bright with dawn prayer' (Ibn Hibban). For Zuhr, the Prophet's practice of delaying in heat (Bukhari). For Asr, 'He would delay Asr as long as the sun was white and pure' (Abu Dawud).
All evidence is ahad, giving zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Understand the ikhtilaf on Fajr
Al-Tahawi reported a view of starting with ghalas (darkness) and ending with isfar. The commentator supports the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) of performing the entire prayer in isfar.
The mufta bihi is to begin and end with isfar.
4
Apply the ruling to special cases
The commentary notes exceptions: the pilgrim at Muzdalifah does not delay Fajr; women are recommended to pray Fajr in ghalas. For Zuhr, ibrad is recommended absolutely, not conditional on heat or congregation.
Jumu'ah follows the same ruling as Zuhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وندب) تأخير الفجر) لما رواه أصحاب السنن الأربعة وصححه الترمذي أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر » (۱) وحمله على تبين طلوعه يأباه ما في صحيح ابن حبان «كلما أصبحتم بالصبح فهو أعظم للأجر» أطلقه فشمل الابتداء والانتهاء فيستحب البداءة بالإسفار والختم به خلافاً للطحاوي فإنه نقل عن الأصحاب استحباب البداءة بالغلس والختم بالإسفار، والأول ظاهر الرواية كما في العناية. وقالوا : يسفر بها بحيث لو ظهر فساد صلاته يمكنه أن يعيدها في الوقت بقراءة مستحبة . وقيل : يؤخرها جداً لأن الفساد موهوم فلا يترك المستحب لأجله وهو ظاهر إطلاق الكتاب لكن لا يؤخرها بحيث يقع الشك في طلوع الشمس. وفي السراج الوهاج حد الإسفار أن يصلي في النصف الثاني، ولا يخفى أن الحاج بمزدلفة لا يؤخرها. وفي المبتغى بالغين المعجمة الأفضل للمرأة في الفجر الغلس، وفي غيرها الانتظار إلى فراغ الرجال عن الجماعة. قوله : وظهر الصيف) أي ندب تأخيره لرواية البخاري كان إذا اشتد البرد بكر بالصلاة، وإذا اشتد الحر أبرد بالصلاة. والمراد الظهر لأنه جواب السؤال عنها وحده أن يصلي قبل المثل. أطلقه فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين يصلي بجماعة أو لا، وبين أن يكون في بلاد حارة أو لا، وبين أن يكون في شدة الحر أو لا، ولهذا قال في المجمع ونفضل الإبراد بالظهر مطلقاً، فما في السراج الوهاج من يستحب الإبراد بثلاثة شروط ففيه نظر، بل هو مذهب الشافعي على ما قيل. والجمعة كالظهر أصلاً واستحباباً في الزمانين كذا ذكره الاسبيجابي . قوله (والعصر ما لم تتغير) أي ندب تأخيره ما لم تتغير الشمس لرواية أبي داود كان يؤخر العصر ما دامت الشمس بيضاء نقية . أطلقه فشمل الصيف والشتاء لما في ذلك من تكثير النوافل لكراهتها بعد العصر، وأراد أن
His statement: (And it is recommended) delaying Fajr, because the narrators of the four Sunan and al-Tirmidhi authenticated: 'Be bright with Fajr, for it is greater in reward.' And carrying it upon the appearance of dawn is rejected by what is in Sahih Ibn Hibban: 'Whenever you become bright with dawn prayer, it is greater in reward.' It is general, including beginning and end, so it is recommended to start with isfar and end with it, contrary to al-Tahawi who narrated from the companions the recommendation to start with darkness (ghalas) and end with isfar. The first is the apparent narration as in al-`Inayah. They said: He should make it bright such that if his prayer becomes invalid, he can repeat it in the time with recommended recitation. It is said: delay it much because invalidity is illusory, so the recommended action is not left for it, and that is the apparent general meaning of the book, but he should not delay it such that doubt arises about sunrise. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the limit of isfar is to pray in the second half, and it is clear that the pilgrim at Muzdalifah does not delay it. In al-Mubtagha, the best for a woman in Fajr is darkness (ghalas), and in other prayers she waits until the men finish the congregation. His statement: (and Zuhr of summer) meaning it is recommended to delay it due to the narration of Bukhari: 'When it was intensely cold, he would hasten with prayer, and when intensely hot, he would cool with prayer.' And the intended is Zuhr because it is the answer to the question about it alone: he should pray before the mithl. He gave an absolute statement so it indicates no difference between praying in congregation or alone, between being in a hot country or not, between being in extreme heat or not. Therefore, in al-Majma` it is said: We prefer cooling with Zuhr absolutely. So what is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj of recommending cooling with three conditions is debatable; rather it is the madhhab of al-Shafi`i as is said. And Jumu`ah is like Zuhr in essence and recommendation in both times, as al-Isbiji mentioned. His statement: (and Asr as long as it has not changed) meaning its delay is recommended as long as the sun has not changed, due to the narration of Abu Dawud: 'He would delay Asr as long as the sun was white and pure.' It is general, including summer and winter, because of the increase of voluntary prayers due to their dislike after Asr, and he intended that
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the recommended timings for Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr prayers from the Kanz al-Daqa'iq. For Fajr, it is recommended to delay it until isfar (brightness) based on the hadith 'Be bright with Fajr, for it is greater in reward.' However, al-Tahawi reported from the early scholars that it is recommended to start in darkness (ghalas) and end with brightness. The preferred view is to perform the entire prayer in isfar, indicated by the hadith in Ibn Hibban. The limit of isfar is such that if one's prayer becomes invalid, he can repeat it in time. For women, it is better to pray Fajr in darkness to avoid exposure. For Zuhr, it is recommended to delay it in summer (ibrad) based on the hadith of Bukhari. The delay is recommended generally, whether in congregation or alone, whether in a hot country or not. This is the absolute view, contrary to some who restrict it to three conditions. Jumu`ah is included in the same ruling as Zuhr. For Asr, it is recommended to delay it until the sun remains white and pure, as per the hadith of Abu Dawud. This delay allows for more voluntary prayers, as they are disliked after Asr. The passage also mentions a debate about the view of al-Halabi and others.

Key Terms
الإسفار (al-isfar): Brightness of dawn, when the light spreads.
الإبراد (al-ibrad): Delaying Zuhr prayer until the cooler part of the afternoon in summer.
الغلس (al-ghalas): The darkness before dawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended way to perform Fajr prayer according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah)?
A) Start in darkness (ghalas) and end in isfar.
B) Perform the entire prayer in isfar.
C) Delay it until just before sunrise.
D) Perform it as early as possible.

Key Takeaway
For Fajr, Zuhr, and Asr, the Hanafi school recommends specific delays (isfar, ibrad, and delaying while sun is white) based on prophetic practice—these are sunnah muakkadah, not obligatory.

Recommended Delay of Fajr Prayer (Isfar)
Ruling on recommending delay of Fajr until isfar with proof and intra-madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended time for Fajr prayer, identify the primary hadith evidence, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference with al-Tahawi regarding isfar vs ghals.

Core Idea
Delay Fajr until clear dawn (isfar) is recommended for greater reward, but women and pilgrims have exceptions.

The timing of Fajr prayer is a matter of some nuance in the Hanafi school. While the basic obligation is to pray within the dawn-to-sunrise window, the best time is a subject of evidence and scholarly preference. This lesson unpacks the proof for delaying Fajr until clear dawn (isfar), the rationale behind it, and the exceptions that apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling level
The passage rules on the recommended time for Fajr prayer. The matn says it is 'nadb' (recommended) to delay. In Hanafi fiqh, nadb is equivalent to sunnah ghayr muakkadah — a meritorious act that is not compulsory.
Note the difference between nadb/mandub and wajib/fard.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The primary dalil is the hadith: 'أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر' (Make Fajr bright, for it is greater in reward). This is narrated by the four Sunan and authenticated by Tirmidhi. The imperative 'asfiru' indicates a command, but it is interpreted as recommendation due to other factors.
The second hadith from Ibn Hibban reinforces that any clear dawn time gives greater reward.
3
Understand the interpretation and scope
The hadith is taken unrestrictedly, covering both the beginning and end of the prayer time. Thus, the recommended practice is to start and finish during isfar (clear dawn). This contradicts al-Tahawi's view, who advocated starting in ghals (darkness) and ending with isfar.
The commentator prefers the first view as 'zahir al-riwayah' (apparent narration).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Tahawi transmitted from earlier companions a preference for starting in ghals. The Hanafi response is that the explicit hadith takes precedence, and the view of starting with isfar is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school, not a cross-madhhab one.
5
Apply exceptions
Two exceptions: (1) Pilgrims at Muzdalifah do not delay Fajr. (2) For women, the best is ghals (early darkness) to avoid men. For men in normal circumstances, isfar remains recommended.
The exception for women is based on avoiding fitna, not on the general ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وندب) تأخير الفجر) لما رواه أصحاب السنن الأربعة وصححه الترمذي «أسفروا بالفجر فإنه أعظم للأجر» وحمله على تبين طلوعه يأباه ما في صحيح ابن حبان «كلما أصبحتم بالصبح فهو أعظم للأجر» أطلقه فشمل الابتداء والانتهاء فيستحب البداءة بالإسفار والختم به خلافاً للطحاوي فإنه نقل عن الأصحاب استحباب البداءة بالغلس والختم بالإسفار، والأول ظاهر الرواية كما في العناية. وقالوا : يسفر بها بحيث لو ظهر فساد صلاته يمكنه أن يعيدها في الوقت بقراءة مستحبة . وقيل : يؤخرها جداً لأن الفساد موهوم فلا يترك المستحب لأجله وهو ظاهر إطلاق الكتاب لكن لا يؤخرها بحيث يقع الشك في طلوع الشمس. وفي السراج الوهاج حد الإسفار أن يصلي في النصف الثاني، ولا يخفى أن الحاج بمزدلفة لا يؤخرها. وفي المبتغى بالغين المعجمة الأفضل للمرأة في الفجر الغلس، وفي غيرها الانتظار إلى فراغ الرجال عن الجماعة. قوله : وظهر الصيف)
His statement: '(It is recommended) to delay Fajr' due to what the authors of the four Sunan narrated and al-Tirmidhi authenticated: 'Make Fajr bright (is far), for it is greater in reward.' Interpreting it as [meaning] the clear appearance of dawn is contradicted by what is in Sahih Ibn Hibban: 'Whenever you perform the morning prayer, it is greater in reward.' He left it unrestricted, so it includes the beginning and the end. Thus, it is recommended to start with isfar and to end with it, contrary to al-Tahawi, who transmitted from the companions the recommendation of starting with ghals and ending with isfar. The first is the apparent narration, as in al-'Inayah. They said: one performs it with isfar such that if the corruption of his prayer becomes apparent, he can repeat it within the time with a recommended recitation. And it was said: delay it greatly, because corruption is unlikely, so the recommended is not abandoned for it, and this is apparent from the absolute wording of the book, but do not delay it to the point of doubt about sunrise. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the measure of isfar is to pray in the second half. It is not hidden that the pilgrim at Muzdalifah does not delay it. In al-Muntaba (with a dotted ghayn): the best for a woman in Fajr is ghals, and in other prayers she waits until the men finish congregation. His statement: 'and Zuhr in summer'
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recommended delay of the Fajr prayer. The author of al-Kanz (the matn) stated that it is recommended (mandub) to delay Fajr until isfar (clear dawn light). The commentator (al-Bahr al-Raiq) provides the evidence: the hadith narrated by the four Sunan and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi: 'Make Fajr bright, for it is greater in reward.' The word 'asfiru' implies performing the prayer when the dawn is clearly bright. However, some interpret this as delaying until the time is certain, but the commentator counters with another hadith from Ibn Hibban that removes doubt. The text then discusses intra-Hanafi differences: al-Tahawi preferred starting in darkness (ghals) and ending with isfar, but the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is to start and end with isfar. There is also discussion about the limit: some say delay until one could repeat if needed, others say delay greatly, but not to the point of doubting sunrise. Special cases: pilgrims at Muzdalifah do not delay, and women are recommended to pray in darkness at the beginning of time to avoid men.

Key Terms
إسفار (isfār): The time when dawn light becomes clearly visible on the horizon, before sunrise.
غلس (ghals): The darkness at the very beginning of dawn, just after the first light appears.
ندب (nadb): A recommendatory legal ruling, also called mandub or sunnah ghayr muakkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi zahir al-riwayah, what is the recommended time for the Fajr prayer?
A) At the earliest beginning of dawn (ghals)
B) After sunrise
C) At isfar (clear dawn light)
D) During the middle of the night

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying Fajr until isfar (clear dawn light) for greater reward, with exceptions for women (who should pray in ghals) and pilgrims at Muzdalifah (who should not delay).
