Recommended Delay of Zuhr in Summer (Ibard)
Ruling with proof on delaying Zuhr in summer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Zuhr in summer, identify the hadith proof, and explain why the recommendation is unconditional.

Core Idea
Zuhr delay in summer is recommended without condition: not limited to heat or congregation.

The timing of Zuhr prayer in hot weather may stir common questions: should we pray early or wait? The Hanafi school, drawing on prophetic practice, recommends delaying Zuhr until it cools — not only in extreme heat, but in all summer conditions. This lesson unpacks the proof and the school's confident position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is the delay of Zuhr (ibrad) in summer. The ruling is nadb (recommendation), which in Hanafi is sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites a Bukhari hadith: the Prophet would hasten prayer in cold and delay it (abrada) in heat. The context shows the question was about Zuhr, so it applies to Zuhr.
The hadith is ahad, so it gives zanni evidence; the ruling remains recommended, not wajib.
3
Analyze the unrestricted wording
The matn says 'Zuhr in summer' without limiting terms. The commentator notes that the wording is absolute, so no conditions of heat level, congregation, or region are required.
Absolute here means the recommendation applies to all summer Zuhr prayers.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafis (al-Siraj al-Wahhaj) added three conditions, like extreme heat and congregation. The commentator rejects this as actually the Shafi'i view.
The Shafi'i school restricts ibrad to certain conditions; Hanafi maintains absolute recommendation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator favors the absolute view from al-Majma', and this is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Thus, the official Hanafi ruling: recommended to delay Zuhr in all summer cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وظهر الصيف) أي ندب تأخيره لرواية البخاري «كان إذا اشتد البرد بكر بالصلاة، وإذا اشتد الحر أبرد بالصلاة» والمراد الظهر لأنه جواب السؤال عنها وحده أن يصلي قبل المثل. أطلقه فأفاد أنه لا فرق بين يصلي بجماعة أو لا، وبين أن يكون في بلاد حارة أو لا، وبين أن يكون في شدة الحر أو لا، ولهذا قال في المجمع ونفضل الإبراد بالظهر مطلقاً، فما في السراج الوهاج من يستحب الإبراد بثلاثة شروط ففيه نظر، بل هو مذهب الشافعي على ما قيل. والجمعة كالظهر أصلاً واستحباباً في الزمانين كذا ذكره الاسبيجابي . قوله (والعصر ما لم تتغير)
His statement: 'and Zuhr in summer' i.e., it is recommended to delay it due to the narration of Bukhari: 'When it was severely cold, he would hasten the prayer, and when it was severely hot, he would delay (abrada) the prayer.' And what is meant is Zuhr, because it was the answer to the question about it. Its limit is to pray before the [shadow's] equal. He left it unrestricted, so it indicates no difference between praying in congregation or not, nor between being in a hot country or not, nor between being in severe heat or not. For this reason, they said in al-Majma': 'We prefer delay (ibrad) in Zuhr absolutely.' So what is in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that delay is recommended with three conditions is subject to consideration; rather, it is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, as it is said. And Jumu'ah is like Zuhr in origin and recommendation in the two times (summer and winter). Al-Isbijabi mentioned it like this. His statement: 'and Asr as long as the sun has not changed'
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling with proof for delaying Zuhr prayer in the summer. The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) stated that it is recommended to delay Zuhr in summer. The commentator brings the hadith from Bukhari: the Prophet would hasten the prayer in extreme cold and delay it in extreme heat. The phrase 'abrada' means to pray when it cools down. The limit for Zuhr is before the shadow becomes equal to the object. The wording 'Zuhr in summer' is unrestricted, so the recommendation applies generally: whether in congregation or alone, in hot countries or not, in severe heat or not. The commentator notes that in al-Majma' it is stated 'we prefer delay absolutely,' which contrasts with al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that requires three conditions. The commentator dismisses that as likely the Shafi'i position. Jun'ah (Friday prayer) follows the same ruling as Zuhr. Then the text transitions to the next section on Asr.

Key Terms
إبراد (ibrād): The act of delaying Zuhr prayer until the cooler part of the afternoon in hot weather.
مثل (mithl): The time when an object's shadow equals its height; the end of the recommended time for Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this text, when is it recommended to delay Zuhr prayer?
A) Only in severe heat
B) Only when praying in congregation
C) Absolutely in summer, regardless of conditions
D) Only in hot countries

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends delaying Zuhr in summer unconditionally, based on the Prophet's practice and the unrestricted wording of the matn.

Recommended Delay of Asr Until the Sun Changes Color
Ruling on recommending delay of Asr prayer until the sun's color changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Asr prayer, identify the hadith evidence, and explain the time limit for the delay.

Core Idea
Delaying Asr while the sun is white is recommended; delaying after it changes is disliked.

Timing is crucial in prayer. For Asr, the Hanafi school recommends delaying it until the sun begins to turn yellow, based on a prophetic practice. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence, and the precise condition that marks the end of the recommended window.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Determine the specific act being ruled upon (delaying Asr prayer) and the hukm level (recommended = nadb).
The text explicitly states 'nadb' (recommendation).
2
Locate the Dalil
Find the proof cited: a hadith from Abu Dawud that the Prophet would delay Asr while the sun was white and pure.
Hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Analyze how the hadith indicates recommendation: the verb 'yua'akhkhir' (delay) implies preference, and the condition 'white and pure' defines the recommended timeframe.
The command form is not imperative; it describes practice.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Halabi and others restricted the delay, while Ibn al-Humam and the majority allowed it unrestricted (summer and winter).
The commentator sides with Ibn al-Humam.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Understand the preferred view: the delay is recommended until the sun changes color, after which it becomes makruh (disliked).
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والعصر ما لم تتغير) أي ندب تأخيره ما لم تتغير الشمس لرواية أبي داود «كان يؤخر العصر ما دامت الشمس بيضاء نقية» أطلقه فشمل الصيف والشتاء لما في ذلك من تكثير النوافل لكراهتها بعد العصر، وأراد أن بالحلبي شارح المنية ووافقه العلامة الباقاني في شرحه على الملتقى والشرنبلالي في إمداد الفتاح وحواشيه على الدرر والعلامة نوح أفندي في حاشية الدرر، وكذا أخو المؤلف في نهره وتابعهم الشيخ علاء الدين الحصكفي في شرحه على التنوير ولكن انتصر للمحقق ابن الهمام محشي شرح التنوير شيخ مشايخنا العلامة الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي المداري ورد كلام شارح المنية في حاشيته وكتبت في هامشه ما يدفع جوابه بأظهر وجه وأبينه فليراجع ذلك قوله : (أطلقه فأفاد الخ) قال في النهر : في عبارته في أن بالحلبي ...
His statement: '(and Asr as long as it (the sun) has not changed)' i.e., it is recommended to delay it as long as the sun has not changed (color), due to the narration of Abu Dawud: 'He would delay Asr as long as the sun was white and pure.' He left it unrestricted, so it includes summer and winter, because in that is increasing supererogatory prayers, as they are disliked after Asr. And he intended that by al-Halabi, the commentator of al-Munya, and agreed with him ... (unclear text) so refer to that. His statement: 'He left it unrestricted so it indicates...' He said in al-Nahr: in his expression...
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that it is recommended to delay the Asr prayer until the sun begins to change color (yellowness). The evidence is the hadith from Abu Dawud that the Prophet used to delay Asr while the sun was still white and pure. The commentator notes that the ruling is unrestricted: it applies in both summer and winter. The reason given is that delaying allows more sunnah and nafl prayers, since they are disliked after Asr. The text then engages with a scholarly dispute: al-Halabi (commentator of al-Munya) and others (al-Baqani, al-Shurunbulali, etc.) held a view, while Ibn al-Humam and others refuted them. The commentator advises referring to the margins for details. The key point is that the delay is recommended until the sun changes, but not after that, because delaying until change is makruh (disliked).

Key Terms
تغير الشمس (taghayyur al-shams): The change of the sun's color from white to yellow before sunset; after this it is disliked to delay Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Until when is it recommended to delay Asr prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Until the sun turns yellow
B) Until sunset
C) Until the sun is completely white and pure
D) Until the time of Maghrib

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, delaying Asr prayer is recommended while the sun remains white and pure; after it changes color, delaying becomes disliked.

Recommended Delay of Isha: Seasonal Distinction
Ruling on recommending delay of Isha with proof and seasonal reconciliation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Isha prayer and explain the seasonal reconciliation between the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Delaying Isha to one-third of the night is recommended in winter; in summer, hastening is preferred.

The Hanafi school holds that it is recommended to delay Isha prayer to one-third of the night, but this is not absolute. The source passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses an apparent conflict in the hadith evidence and reconciles it by distinguishing between winter and summer. Understanding this seasonal nuance is crucial for applying the ruling correctly in mosque timings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling from the Matn
The matn states 'and Isha until one-third' meaning it is recommended to delay Isha prayer until one-third of the night.
The term 'nadb' (recommendation) indicates it is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Tirmidhi: 'Were it not for hardship on my nation, I would have delayed Isha to one-third or half of the night.'
The conditional 'laula' shows the Prophet's desire but not obligation.
3
Recognize the Intra-Madhhab Conflict
Mukhtasar al-Quduri says 'to before one-third' based on a Bukhari narration that companions prayed between twilight and one-third, implying delay is not recommended to the limit itself.
This creates an apparent contradiction with the Tirmidhi hadith.
4
Follow the Commentator's Reconciliation
The commentator reconciles by applying the Tirmidhi hadith to winter (long nights, fear of sleep) and the Bukhari narration to summer (short nights, congregation preservation).
This distinction preserves both evidences.
5
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical effect: in summer, some scholars recommend hastening Isha to avoid loss of congregation, while in winter delay is encouraged.
The mufta bihi view adopts this seasonal distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والعشاء إلى الثلث) أي ندب تأخيرها إلى ثلث الليل لما رواه الترمذي وصححه «لولا أن أشق على أمتي لأخرت العشاء إلى ثلث الليل أو نصفه» وفي مختصر القدوري إلى ما قبل الثلث لرواية البخاري : كانوا يصلون العتمة فيما بين أن يغيب الشفق إلى ثلث الليل ومقتضاه أنه لا يستحب تأخيرها إلى الثلث بخلاف الأول. ووفق بينهما في شرح المجمع لابن الملك بحمل الأول على الشتاء والثاني على الصيف لغلبة النوم ا هـ . وأطلقه فشمل الصيف والشتاء وقيل يستحب تعجيل العشاء في الصيف لئلا تتقلل الجماعة، وأفاد أن التأخير إلى نصف الليل ليس بمستحب وقالوا: إنه مباح وإلى ما بعده مكروه . وقيل : إلى ما بعد الثلث مكروه. وروى الإمام أحمد وغيره أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يستحب أن يؤخر العشاء، وكان يكره النوم قبلها والحديث بعدها. وقيد الطحاوي كراهة النوم قبلها بمن خشي عليه فوت وقتها أو فوت الجماعة فيها وإلا فلا. وقيد البدائع المستحب هو آخر الوقت في الصيف وشرط الشافعي له شدة الحر وحرارة البلد. والصلاة في جماعة وقصد الناس لها من بعيد وبه جزم في السراج على أنه مذهب أصحابنا إلا أن قوله في المجمع ونفضل الإبراد مطلقاً وإطلاق الكتاب يأباه قوله : (فإن تأخيرها إليه مكروه لا الفعل) أي أن الكراهة في نفس التأخير لا في نفس الفعل، وسيأتي في الشرح الكلام على ذلك وترجيح كون الكراهة في كل من التأخير والأداء. قوله : (ووفق بينهما في شرح المجمع الخ) قال في النهر بعد الخانية والتحفة ومحيط رضى الدين والبدائع : تقييد التأخير إلى الثلث بالشتاء أما الصيف فيندب فيه التعجيل فيه نظر لما علمت من أنه يندب التعجيل في الصيف وكلام القدوري في التأخير ومن ثم قيده في السراج بالشتاء. ثم رأيت بعض المحققين قال : ينبغي أن تكون الغاية داخلة تحت المغيا في كلام القدوري وغير داخلة في قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لولا أن أشق على أمتي لأخرت العشاء إلى ثلث الليل» لينطبق الدليل على المدعي اهـ. وهذا أحسن ما به يحصل التوفيق وبالله تعالى التوفيق .اهـ. ولا يخفى عليك أنه لا فرق بين دخول الغاية وعدمها في كلام القدوري لأنه على كل لا يدخل الثلث لوجود لفظة قبل» على أنه تبقى المنافاة في قوله في الحديث أو نصفه كما . مر فتدبر . ووفق في الدرر بأن يكون ابتداؤها قبل آخر الثلث وانتهاؤها في آخره ولو بالتخمين.
His statement: '(and Isha until one-third)' i.e., it is recommended to delay it to one-third of the night, due to what al-Tirmidhi narrated and authenticated: 'Were it not for the hardship on my nation, I would have delayed Isha to one-third or half of the night.' And in Mukhtasar al-Quduri: 'until before one-third' due to Bukhari's narration: 'They used to pray the 'Atamah between the disappearance of the twilight and the one-third of the night.' This implies that delaying to one-third is not recommended, contrary to the first. A reconciliation was made in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik: the first is taken for winter, the second for summer, due to prevalence of sleep. The author left it unrestricted, so it includes summer and winter. It was said: it is recommended to hasten Isha in summer to avoid congregation becoming small. It indicates that delay to half the night is not recommended; they said: it is permissible, and beyond that is disliked. It was said: beyond one-third is disliked. Imam Ahmad and others narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to like to delay Isha, and disliked sleep before it and conversation after it. Al-Tahawi restricted the dislike of sleep before it to one who fears missing the time or congregation; otherwise not. Al-Bada'i' restricted the recommended to the end of time in summer; al-Shafi'i conditioned it on extreme heat, hot country, prayer in congregation, and people coming from afar. This is asserted in al-Siraj as the madhhab of our companions, except that his statement in al-Majma' 'we prefer ibrad absolutely' and the absolute wording of the book contradicts it. His statement: 'For delaying to it is disliked, not the act itself' means that the dislike is in the delay itself, not in the act of praying. Later in the commentary the discussion will come on that and the preference that the dislike is in both delay and performance. His statement: 'He reconciled between them in Sharh al-Majma'...' He said in al-Nahr after al-Khaniyyah, al-Tuhfah, Muhit radi al-Din, and al-Bada'i': Restricting delay to one-third to winter, while in summer it is recommended to hasten—this requires consideration, because it is known that it is recommended to hasten in summer and the statement of al-Quduri is about delay. Hence, it was restricted in al-Siraj to winter. Then I saw some verified scholars said: The limit (ghayah) should be included under the limited (mighya') in al-Quduri's statement and not included in the hadith 'I would have delayed Isha to one-third of the night' so that the evidence applies to the claim. That is the best reconciliation. And it is not hidden that there is no difference in including the limit or not in al-Quduri's statement because in any case the one-third is not included due to the word 'before', so the contradiction remains in the hadith's 'or half' as mentioned. So reflect. A reconciliation was made in al-Durar: the prayer should begin before the end of the first third and end in its last part, even by estimation.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on delaying Isha prayer. The matn states it is recommended to delay Isha until one-third of the night. The primary proof is the hadith in Tirmidhi: 'Were it not for hardship... to one-third or half.' However, there is apparent conflict with another narration in Bukhari that they prayed 'Atamah from twilight to one-third', implying no delay beyond the first part. The commentator discusses various reconciliations: some say the first hadith is for winter (long nights) and the second for summer (short nights, fear of sleep). The text then notes different opinions: Some recommend hastening in summer to avoid losing congregation; delay to half is permissible but beyond is makruh. Al-Tahawi restricts the dislike of sleep before Isha to those who might miss the time or congregation. The commentator also delves into a technical debate about whether the 'limit' (one-third) is included in the recommended time or not, citing various authorities like al-Nahr, al-Khaniyyah, etc. Ultimately, the relied-upon view is that delaying to one-third is recommended, but with consideration for summer/winter and congregational needs. The passage ends with a note that a reconciliation in al-Durar suggests praying such that the prayer begins before the end of the first third and ends in its last part.

Key Terms
شفق (shafaq): The twilight redness after sunset; the entry time for Isha begins when it disappears.
ثلث الليل (thulth al-layl): One-third of the night, calculated from Maghrib (sunset) to Fajr (dawn).
عتمة ('atamah): Another name for Isha prayer, referring to the darkness of the night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Summer
B) Winter
C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Delaying Isha to one-third of the night is recommended in winter; in summer, hastening is preferred to maintain congregation.

Ruling on Delaying Asr Until Yellowing
States ruling on delaying Asr until sun changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on delaying Asr until yellowing and distinguish between the karahah of the delay and the validity of the prayer.

Core Idea
Delaying Asr until yellowing is makruh, but the prayer itself remains valid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a common confusion: while it is disliked to delay the Asr prayer until the sun turns yellow, the prayer itself is not invalidated. The karahah applies to the delay, not to the act of praying. This distinction is crucial for understanding Hanafi rulings on prayer times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Delaying Asr until the sun changes color. The ruling: makruh (disliked).
The text says تأخيرها إليه مكروه.
2
Distinguish the karahah
The karahah is on the delay, not on the act of praying itself (لا الفعل). Why? Because the command to pray and the prohibition of abandoning it prevent the act from being disliked.
The phrase 'مأمور بها منهي عن تركها' is key.
3
Note the exception
If one begins the prayer before the change and prolongs it until the change, it is not disliked because avoiding the disliked time while in prayer is difficult, so it is excused.
Text: 'ولو شرع فيه قبل التغير فمده إليه لا يكره'.
4
Consider the adhan analogy
The same ruling applies to the adhan regarding expediting or delaying.
The text briefly mentions this, but it's not the focus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالتغير أن تكون الشمس بحال لا تحار فيها العيون على الصحيح فإن تأخيرها إليه مكروه لا الفعل لأنه مأمور بها منهي عن تركها فلا يكون الفعل مكروهاً. كذا في السراج. ولو شرع فيه قبل التغير فمده إليه لا يكره لأن الاحتراز عن الكراهة مع الإقبال على الصلاة متعذر فجعل عفواً. كذا في غاية البيان وحكم الأذان حكم الصلاة في الاستحباب تعجيلاً وتأخيراً صيفاً وشتاء كما سنذكره في بابه إن شاء الله تعالى
With the change that the sun is in a state where eyes cannot look at it according to the correct opinion, for delaying it until that time is disliked (makruh), not the act itself, because he is commanded to perform it and prohibited from abandoning it, so the act cannot be disliked. Thus in al-Siraj. And if he began it before the change and prolonged it until it, it is not disliked because avoiding dislike while engaging in prayer is difficult, so it is excused. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And the ruling of the adhan is like the ruling of prayer regarding recommending expediting or delaying in summer and winter as we will mention in its chapter, God willing.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on delaying the Asr prayer until the sun changes color (yellowing). The author states that on the correct opinion, delaying Asr until the sun reaches a state where the eyes cannot look at it is makruh (disliked), but the actual act of praying at that time is not makruh because the person is commanded to pray and is prohibited from abandoning the prayer, so the act itself cannot be disliked. If a person began the prayer before the change and prolonged his prayer until the time of change, it is not disliked because it would be difficult to avoid the disliked time while already engaged in prayer, so it is excused. The ruling for the adhan (call to prayer) follows the same ruling regarding recommendation of expediting or delaying in summer and winter, as will be mentioned in the proper chapter.

Key Terms
التغير (al-taghayyur): The change of the sun's color to yellow, indicating the end of the preferred time for Asr.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an act whose abandonment is rewarded but whose commission is not punished, though in the Hanafi school it can be tahrimi (near haram) or tanzihi (lightly disliked).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer becomes invalid (batil).
B) The delay is disliked (makruh), but the prayer is valid.
C) It is haram to pray at that time.
D) The prayer is recommended (mustahab) at that time.

Key Takeaway
Delaying Asr until the sun turns yellow is disliked, but the prayer itself remains valid and should not be repeated.

The Recommended Time for Isha: Delay to the Third of the Night
Ruling with proof on recommended Isha time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Isha, identify the hadith evidence, and explain the seasonal reconciliation among Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
Delaying Isha to the third of the night is recommended, not required, with seasonal adjustments to avoid hardship.

The time for Isha prayer is a matter of recommendation (nadb) in the Hanafi school. The Prophet (peace be upon him) desired to delay it until the third or half of the night but refrained due to concern for his ummah. This lesson explores the primary proof, the intra-Hanafi difference between al-Quduri and the majority, and how later scholars reconciled the views by season. Understanding this teaches us the balance between Sunnah and practical ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
Look at the text: it explicitly says 'nadb' (recommendation). The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah. Note that it is not fard or wajib.
The core statement: 'والعشاء إلى الثلث' (and Isha until the third) indicates the time of recommendation.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi: 'Were it not that I would burden my ummah, I would have delayed Isha until the third or half the night.' Identify its transmission (Sunnah ahad) and legal indication (recommendation from the conditional desire).
The hadith is zanni in both transmission and indication.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Quduri in Mukhtasar says 'until before the third' based on the practice of the Companions (al-Bukhari). The majority hold 'until the third'. Understand the apparent contradiction.
This is a difference within the madhhab, not with another school.
4
Follow the reconciliation
Ibn al-Malak in Sharh al-Majma' reconciles by attributing the longer delay to winter and the shorter to summer. This is due to longer nights in winter allowing people to sleep afterward without missing congregation. The text also mentions other reconciliations (e.g., in Durar).
The key is to avoid hardship and maintain congregation.
5
Extract ancillary rulings
The passage also covers: sleep before Isha (disliked if one fears missing time or congregation), conversation after Isha (disliked without need), and the severe dislike (makruh tahrimi) of delaying beyond half the night. Identify these from the text.
These show the comprehensive nature of the chapter on prayer times.

الخ) قال في النهر بعد الخانية والتحفة ومحيط رضى الدين والبدائع : تقييد التأخير إلى الثلث بالشتاء أما الصيف فيندب فيه التعجيل فيه نظر لما علمت من أنه يندب التعجيل في الصيف وكلام القدوري في التأخير ومن لينطبق الدليل على المدعي اهـ. وهذا أحسن ما به يحصل التوفيق وبالله تعالى التوفيق .اهـ. ولا يخفى عليك أنه لا فرق بين دخول الغاية وعدمه في كلام القدوري لأنه على كل لا يدخل الثلث لوجود لفظة قبل» على أنه والعصر إلى وقت اصفرار الشمس والمغرب إلى اشتباك النجوم يكره كراهة تحريم .
His statement: (And isha until the third) i.e., it is recommended to delay it until the third of the night due to what al-Tirmidhi narrated and authenticated: 'Were it not that I would burden my ummah, I would have delayed isha until the third of the night or half of it.' And in Mukhtasar al-Quduri: until before the third, due to al-Bukhari's narration: 'They used to pray the night prayer between the disappearance of the twilight and the third of the night.' Its implication is that it is not recommended to delay it until the third, contrary to the first. He reconciled between them in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malak by carrying the first on winter and the second on summer due to the prevalence of sleep. End. And he made it absolute, including summer and winter, and it was said that it is recommended to expedite isha in summer lest the congregation become few. And it conveyed that delay to half the night is not recommended, and they said: it is permissible, and beyond that is disliked. And it was said: beyond the third is disliked. And Imam Ahmad and others narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to like to delay isha, and he disliked sleep before it and conversation after it. Al-Tahawi restricted the dislike of sleep before it to the one who fears missing its time or missing the congregation in it, otherwise no. Al-Bada'i' restricted that the recommended is the last time in summer, and al-Shafi'i conditioned for it extreme heat and hot climate. And prayer in congregation and people's intention for it from afar, and al-Siraj affirmed it as the madhhab of our companions, except that his statement in al-Majma' 'and we prefer al-ibrad absolutely' and the general application of the book rejects it. His statement: (for delaying it until it is disliked, not the act) means that the dislike is in the delay itself, not in the act itself. And will come in the commentary speech on that and the preponderance that the dislike is in both the delay and the performance. His statement: (and he reconciled between them in Sharh al-Majma' etc.) He said in al-Nahr, after al-Khaniyya, al-Tuhfa, Muhit Radi al-Din, and al-Bada'i': restricting delay to the third to winter—as for summer, expediting is recommended—has consideration because of what you know that expediting is recommended in summer and the statement of al-Quduri on delay, hence al-Siraj restricted it to winter. Then I saw some verifiers say: it ought that the limit be included under the limited in al-Quduri's statement and not included in the Prophet's statement '...to the third of the night' so that the evidence matches the claim. End. This is the best way to achieve reconciliation, and with God Almighty is success. End. And it is not hidden from you that there is no difference between inclusion and non-inclusion of the limit in al-Quduri's statement because in any case the third is not included due to the presence of the word 'before', though there remains contradiction in his statement in the hadith 'or half' as mentioned. So reflect. And it was reconciled in al-Durar by making its beginning before the end of the third and its ending at its end, even by estimation. And he said in his transmission from the commentator: conversation after it without need is disliked, but for a need it is not, and likewise recitation of Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, and discussing fiqh and hadith with a guest. And in al-Dhahiriyya: speech after dawn is disliked, and when he prays fajr, speech is permissible for him. And in al-Quniyya: delaying isha beyond half the night, asr until the time of yellowing, and maghrib until stars cluster is disliked as a prohibition-level dislike.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the recommended time for Isha prayer. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that Isha is recommended (mandub) to be delayed until the third of the night. The sharh (commentary) provides the dalil from the hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi that the Prophet (peace be upon him) wished to delay Isha until the third or half the night but refrained out of concern for hardship. However, there is a difference within the Hanafi school: al-Quduri in Mukhtasar says the recommended delay is only until before the third, based on the practice of the Companions. The commentator reconciles this by attributing the longer delay to winter and the shorter to summer, so that people do not lose sleep or congregation. Various positions are discussed: some say expediting in summer is recommended, others say delaying beyond the third is makruh. The passage also addresses ancillary rulings: sleep before Isha is disliked only if one fears missing the time or congregation; conversation after Isha is disliked except for necessary purposes like studying fiqh hadith with a guest. The commentator later mentions that in al-Quniyya, delaying Isha beyond half the night is makruh tahrimi, indicating the severity. Overall, this passage shows the nuanced Hanafi approach balancing hadith evidence, practical hardship, and seasonal variation.

Key Terms
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; an act whose performance is rewarded but whose omission is not punished.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an act that is better to avoid. Here, delay beyond the recommended time is makruh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the Hanafi ruling on delaying Isha beyond half the night?
A) It is permissible (mubah).
B) It is recommended (sunnah).
C) It is disliked as makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
The recommended delay of Isha to the third of the night is a sunnah muakkadah, adjusted by season to preserve congregation and avoid hardship.

Time for Witr Prayer: Delay or Early?
Ruling on recommended time for Witr prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended time for witr prayer and distinguish between the conditions for delay and early prayer.

Core Idea
Delay witr if you are confident of waking; otherwise, pray early – the command is conditional.

This lesson examines the recommended timing for the witr prayer. While witr itself is considered obligatory (wajib) by Imam Abu Hanifa, the time for performing it has a recommended preference. The primary guidance from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is to make witr the last prayer of the night, but this is conditioned on the worshiper's confidence in waking. Understanding this nuance helps avoid missing the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Read the matn: delaying witr is recommended for one who is confident of waking. Identify the hukm: it is nadb (recommendation).
Confidence means one has a habit of waking up for night prayers.
2
Analyze the primary dalil
The hadith 'Make the last of your prayers witr' is a command. In Hanafi usul, a command indicates obligation unless there is a qarina. Find the qarina here: the permission to pray early for those who fear missing.
The qarina is from the Tirmidhi hadith.
3
Derive the legal implication
Combine the two hadith: one commands delay, the other allows early prayer. This shows delay is not obligatory but recommended. Apply the Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub, but qarina turns it to nadb.
4
Examine the exception for those who fear missing
If one fears not waking, it is better to pray early. The text says there is no dislike in praying early, but the better practice is lost.
This is the practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والوتر إلى آخر الليل لمن يثق بالانتباه أي وندب تأخيرة لرواية الصحيحين اجعلوا آخر صلاتكم وترأه (۱) والأمر للندب الرواية الترمذي من خشي منكم أن لا يستيقظ من آخر الليل فليوتر أوله ومن طمع منكم أن يوتر في آخر الليل فليوتر من آخر الليل فإن قراءة القرآن في آخر الليل محضورة (۲) وهي أفضل وهو دليل مفهوم قوله لمن يثق به. وإذا أوتر قبل النوم ثم استيقظ وصلى ما كتب له لا كراهة فيه ولا يعيد الوتر ولزمه ترك الأفضل المفاد بحديث الصحيحين
His statement: (And witr until the last part of the night for one who is confident of awakening) i.e., it is recommended to delay it due to the narration of the two Sahihs: 'Make the last of your prayers witr' (1) and the command is for recommendation. The narration of al-Tirmidhi: 'Whoever among you fears that he will not wake up at the end of the night, let him pray witr at its beginning; and whoever hopes to pray witr at the end of the night, let him pray witr at the end of the night, for the recitation of Quran at the end of the night is witnessed (2) and it is better.' That is the evidence for the understanding of his statement 'for one who is confident.' And if one prays witr before sleep then wakes up and prays what is decreed for him, there is no dislike in it, and he does not repeat the witr, but he has left the better (afdal) indicated by the hadith of the two Sahihs.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the preferred time for Witr prayer. The matn states that Witr is recommended to be delayed to the last part of the night for those who are confident they will wake up. The commentary provides the proof: the hadith from al-Bukhari and Muslim, 'Make the last of your prayers witr,' which is a command indicating recommendation (nadb). Another hadith from al-Tirmidhi specifies that those who fear not waking should pray witr early, but those who hope to wake should delay, as recitation at the end of the night is better. Thus, the recommended time is conditional on confidence of waking. If one prays witr before sleep and then wakes up and prays voluntary prayers, that is permissible and not disliked, but he has missed the superior practice of making witr the last prayer. He should not repeat witr.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered wajib by Abu Hanifa and sunnah muakkadah by the Sahibayn.
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; here, delaying witr is recommended for those confident of waking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only for those who are confident they will wake up before Fajr.
C) Never; it should always be prayed immediately after Isha.
D) Only in winter.

Key Takeaway
Delaying witr to the last part of the night is recommended only if one is confident of waking; otherwise, it is better to pray early.

Expediting Zuhr in Winter: Ruling and Seasonal Definitions
Ruling on expediting Zuhr in winter with seasonal definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time for Zuhr in winter and apply the Hanafi definitions of seasons to determine the ruling for spring and autumn.

Core Idea
Zuhr in winter is recommended early; in summer delayed. Season boundaries depend on persistence of cold/heat or practical needs.

This brief passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses when to pray Zuhr in winter: it is recommended (nadb) to expedite it, just as it is recommended to delay it in summer. But what counts as winter? The commentator presents two Hanafi definitions—astronomical calculation or the persistence of extreme cold—and then extends the ruling to spring and autumn by analogy, filling a gap left by earlier scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying Zuhr in winter. The ruling is that expediting it is recommended (nadb). Recognize that 'nadb' is a level of recommendation, not obligation (fard) or sunnah mu'akkadah.
In Hanafi fiqh, nadb is equivalent to mustahabb or sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah.
2
Analyze the definitions of winter
The text gives two definitions: (1) astronomical calculation, if available; (2) persistent severe cold. Also a practical definition: need for both fuel and padded clothes. Understand that these define the scope of the ruling.
The definition matters because it determines when the ruling applies in different regions.
3
Note the analogical extension to spring and autumn
The commentator applies analogy (qiyas): spring is annexed to winter (expedite), autumn to summer (delay). He admits no earlier scholar discussed this, but offers his reasoned opinion.
This is an example of ijtihad in the Hanafi tradition, applying existing rulings to new cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتعجيل ظهر الشتاء أي وندب تعجيل ظهر الشتاء لما روينا في ظهر الصيف. وفي الخلاصة : من آخر الإيمان : إن كان عندهم حساب يعرفون به الشتاء والصيف فهو على حسابهم، وإن لم يكن فالشتاء ما اشتد فيه البرد على الدوام، والصيف ما يشتد فيه الحر على الدوام، فعلى قياس هذا الربيع ما ينكسر فيه البرد على الدوام، والخريف ما ينكسر فيه الحر على الدوام. ومن مشايخنا من قال : الشتاء ما يحتاج الناس فيه إلى شيئين إلى الوقود ولبس الحشو، والصيف ما يستغنى فيه عنهما، والربيع والخريف ما يستغنى عن أحدهما اهـ. ولم أر من تكلم على حكم صلاة الظهر في الربيع والخريف، والذي يظهر أن الربيع ملحق بالشتاء في هذا الحكم والخريف ملحق بالصيف فيه
His statement: (And expediting zuhr in winter) i.e., it is recommended to expedite zuhr in winter for what we narrated regarding zuhr in summer. And in al-Khulasa: from the last of iman: if they have a calculation by which they know winter and summer, then it is according to their calculation; and if not, then winter is when the cold persistently intensifies, and summer is when the heat persistently intensifies; on this analogy, spring is when the cold breaks persistently, and autumn is when the heat breaks persistently. And some of our mashayikh said: winter is when people need two things: fuel and wearing padded clothing; summer is when they are independent of both; spring and autumn are when they are independent of one of them. End. And I have not seen anyone speak on the ruling of zuhr prayer in spring and autumn, and what appears is that spring is annexed to winter in this ruling and autumn is annexed to summer in it.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on expediting Zuhr prayer in winter. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that Zuhr should be expedited in winter, just as it is recommended to delay it in summer (for cooling). The commentary then defines the seasons according to scholars: either by astronomical calculation, or by the persistent intensity of cold/heat. Some define winter as the season when people need both fire and padded clothing. The commentator notes that he has not seen any scholar discuss the ruling for spring and autumn, but he opines that spring follows winter (expedite) and autumn follows summer (delay).

Key Terms
الشتاء (al-shita'): Winter; defined by persistent cold, or by the need for fuel and padded clothes.
ندب (nadb): Recommendation; expediting Zuhr in winter is recommended.
إبْرَاد (ibrad): Delaying Zuhr in summer until it cools; the opposite of expediting in winter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It should be expedited like winter.
B) It should be delayed like summer.
C) No ruling is given; the commentator says he has not seen anyone discuss it.
D) It should be prayed at the exact midpoint of the day.

Key Takeaway
Expediting Zuhr in winter is recommended (nadb), and the season's definition guides application; spring and autumn follow by analogy.

Expediting Maghrib Prayer: Ruling and Evidence
Ruling with proof on Maghrib timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on expediting Maghrib prayer and explain the evidence from the two Sahihs and the hadith of Ahmad.

Core Idea
Expediting Maghrib is a confirmed sunnah; delaying until stars cluster is makruh.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the timing of Maghrib prayer. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that it is recommended to pray Maghrib early, and disliked to delay it until the stars cluster. We will explore the prophetic practice and the supporting hadith, as well as a subtle discussion about the legal implication of the warning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
Read the matn statement: 'والمغرب' meaning it is recommended (ندب) to expedite Maghrib, and disliked (يكره) to delay until stars cluster.
Note that the matn gives two rulings: one positive (recommendation) and one negative (dislike).
2
Locate the primary hadith (Bukhari/Muslim)
The commentator cites the hadith from the two Sahihs: the Prophet used to pray Maghrib immediately after sunset. This establishes the sunnah (practice) as proof for recommendation.
This is a fi'li (action-based) sunnah, considered strong evidence.
3
Locate the supporting hadith from Ahmad
The hadith warns that the ummah remains in goodness as long as they do not delay Maghrib until stars cluster. This threat (wa'id) is used to derive the dislike.
The commentator raises a discussion: the threat implies recommendation (nadb) rather than dislike, because permissibility is possible.
4
Analyze the commentator's discussion
Understand the usul point: a threat (وعيد) does not automatically indicate prohibition; it may indicate recommendation if permissibility remains possible. However, the school interprets the severity of the warning as indicating makruh (dislike).
This shows the nuance in Hanafi usul: context and other evidence determine the legal value of a threat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والمغرب) أي وندب تعجيلها لحديث الصحيحين كان يصلي المغرب إذا غربت الشمس وتوارت بالحجاب. ويكره تأخيرها إلى اشتباك النجوم لرواية أحمد لا تزال أمتي بخير ما لم يؤخروا المغرب حتى تشتبك النجوم (۳) ذكره الشارح وفيه بحث إذ مقتضاه الندب لا الكراهة لجواز الإباحة.
His statement: (And maghrib) i.e., it is recommended to expedite it due to the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'He used to pray maghrib when the sun set and disappeared behind the veil.' And it is disliked to delay it until the stars cluster due to the narration of Ahmad: 'My ummah will continue in goodness as long as they do not delay maghrib until the stars cluster' (3) mentioned by the commentator. And there is discussion in it, for its implication is recommendation, not dislike, because permissibility is possible.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the time of Maghrib prayer. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq declares that it is recommended (mandub) to expedite Maghrib and disliked (makruh) to delay it until the stars appear. The commentary provides the dalil: the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim, praying immediately after sunset, and a hadith from Ahmad warning that the ummah remains in goodness as long as they do not delay Maghrib. However, the commentator notes a point of discussion: the hadith seems to imply recommendation (nadb) rather than dislike (karahah), because the absence of prohibition allows permissibility. This reflects a subtlety in Hanafi usul: a threat may indicate prohibition, but here it is interpreted as a strong recommendation.

Key Terms
اشتباك النجوم (ishtibak al-nujum): The time when stars appear clustered in the sky, i.e., fully dark after sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on delaying Maghrib prayer until stars cluster?
A) It is haram.
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It is recommended.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Maghrib should be prayed soon after sunset; delaying until stars cluster is makruh.

Harmonizing Two Narrations on Isha Timing
Resolving an intra-Hanafi textual conflict on Isha timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations on delaying Isha prayer and explain how they are reconciled in practice.

Core Idea
Two valid Hanafi narrations on Isha delay—before the third or until the third—are harmonized by season.

In Hanafi fiqh, the recommended timing for Isha prayer is subject to two transmitted narrations. This lesson explores how later scholars reconciled these views, showing that both are valid and their application depends on context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rivayat
Locate the two narrations in the passage: one recommends delaying Isha until before the third of the night, the other until the third.
Both are attributed to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the apparent contradiction
Note that the two statements seem contradictory: 'before the third' vs. 'until the third'. This is the ta'arud that needs resolution.
3
See the harmonization method
The author of al-Mubtagha al-Sharnablaliyya states that each narration is justified in al-Burhan, and the best way is to acknowledge both and reconcile by context (e.g., season).
This is a jam' approach rather than tarjih.
4
Note the practical thamarah
The practical outcome: in winter, the recommended delay is until the third; in summer, before the third. This reflects the reliability of both rivayat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المبتغى الشرنبلالية وقد ظفرت بأن في المسألة روايتين : يستحب تأخير العشاء إلى ما قبل ثلث الليل في رواية، وفي رواية إليه، ووجه كل في البرهان وهذا أحسن ما يوفق به لفك التعارض اهـ. أي التعارض بين عبارتي القدوري والكنز كما هو منشأ كلام صاحب الدرر .
And in al-Mubtagha al-Sharnablaliyya: I have found that in this issue there are two narrations: it is recommended to delay isha until before the third of the night in one narration, and until the third in another, and each is justified in al-Burhan. And this is the best way to reconcile to resolve the contradiction. End. That is, the contradiction between the statements of al-Quduri and al-Kanz, as it is the origin of the speech of the author of al-Durar.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This brief passage is a resolution of an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recommended delay for Isha prayer. The author of al-Mubtagha al-Sharnablaliyya states that there are two narrations (riwayat) within the school: one recommends delaying Isha until before the third of the night, the other until the third. Both have their proofs in al-Burhan. This is the best way to harmonize the apparent contradiction between the statement of al-Quduri (who said 'until before the third') and the matn of al-Kanz (which said 'until the third'). This issue was the source of discussion for the author of al-Durar.

Key Terms
رواية (riwayah): A transmitted opinion within the Hanafi school, often from different students of Abu Hanifa.
التعارض (al-ta'arud): Apparent contradiction between two textual evidences or opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Tracking Hanafi Rulings Across Commentaries
Sharnablali directs to Sharh al-Munya for the spring/autumn Zuhr ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace a fiqh ruling through the Hanafi commentary chain and explain why a later commentator (Sharnablali) directed readers to an earlier text (Sharh al-Munya) for details.

Core Idea
Later Hanafi commentaries often correct the impression that a ruling is undiscussed by citing earlier works.

This short passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq shows how Hanafi scholars engage with their own tradition. The original text claimed that no one had spoken on the ruling of Zuhr prayer in spring and autumn. Sharnablali, in his commentary, points out that the details are actually found in Sharh al-Munya. Understanding this reference chain is essential for navigating Hanafi fiqh literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The base text (likely a matn or earlier commentary) states: 'I have not seen anyone speak on the ruling of zuhr prayer...' This is a statement about the absence of a known discussion.
The original author may have been unaware of the relevant text.
2
Identify the rebuttal reference
Sharnablali, in his Sharh Kabir 'ala Nur al-Idah, responds by saying: 'The detail has come in Sharh al-Munya.' This directs the reader to an earlier Hanafi commentary.
Sharh al-Munya is likely a commentary by Ibn Nujaym or similar.
3
Understand the chain
This creates a chain: original claim → Sharnablali's comment → Sharh al-Munya. The student must recognize that the ruling on Zuhr in spring/autumn is addressed in that earlier work, not absent.
This is a typical example of tawthiq (documentation) in Hanafi texts.
4
Apply to practice
When researching a Hanafi ruling, if a text claims 'لا أعلم' (I do not know), check later commentaries. They often fill gaps by citing earlier sources.
Never assume a ruling is missing; always verify through the commentary tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولم أر من تكلم على حكم صلاة الظهر الخ قال الشرنبلالي في شرحه الكبير لنور الايضاح: قد جاء التفصيل في شرح المنية الخ
His statement: ('And I have not seen anyone speak on the ruling of zuhr prayer etc.') Al-Sharnablali said in his big commentary on Nur al-Idah: 'The detail has come in Sharh al-Munya, etc.'
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This brief passage is a reference to a commentary by Sharnablali on the earlier statement that 'I have not seen anyone speak on the ruling of zuhr prayer in spring and autumn'. Sharnablali indicates that the details are actually discussed in Sharh al-Munya (a Hanafi fiqh work). This shows that later scholars did address the issue, contrary to the earlier author's impression.

Key Terms
شرح المنية (Sharh al-Munya): A commentary on the Hanafi text al-Munya, likely by Ibn Nujaym or another scholar. It discusses the details of zuhr prayer timing in spring and autumn.
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): A Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Shurunbulali. Sharnablali wrote a large commentary on it.

Key Takeaway
A claim in a Hanafi text that a ruling is undiscussed should be verified by consulting later commentaries, which often provide missing references.

Rulings on Speech After Prayer and Delaying Prayers
Commentary on rulings about speech after prayer and delay of prayers to extreme times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on speaking after Fajr and Asr without need, and identify the thresholds for delaying Isha, Asr, and Maghrib that render them makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Delay of Isha, Asr, Maghrib beyond prescribed limits is makruh tahrimi.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two distinct but related issues: the permissibility of speech after certain prayers, and the gravity of delaying prayers beyond their recommended times. While speech after prayer without need is simply disliked, delaying the three mentioned prayers to extreme times is ruled makruh tahrimi—a level close to haram. Understanding these rulings helps the believer avoid acts that diminish the reward of salah and incur sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
The passage rules on two sets of actions: (1) speaking after prayer (specifically Fajr and Asr from context) without need, and (2) delaying Isha, Asr, and Maghrib beyond certain times.
The text does not specify which prayers, but the context of 'after them' refers to Fajr and Asr.
2
Determine the ruling level
For speech without need, the ruling is 'كراهة' (disliked) but not specified as tahrimi or tanzihi. For delaying prayers, the text explicitly says 'يكره كراهة تحريم' (makruh tahrimi).
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram; the act is sinful.
3
Identify the exceptions
Speaking after prayer is permitted if there is a need (للحاجة), and beneficial activities like Quran, dhikr, and discussion of fiqh are also permitted. Similarly, after performing Fajr, speaking is permissible.
The prohibition of speaking after dawn (before Fajr) is from al-Zahiriyya.
4
Note the authority
The rulings are quoted from later Hanafi works – al-Zahiriyya and al-Qunyah – not from the core Zahir al-Riwayah texts.
This is fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa literature).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشارح كراهة الحديث بعدها بغير الحاجة أما لها فلا وكذا قراءة القرآن والذكر وحكايات الصالحين ومذاكرة الفقه والحديث مع الضيف. وفي الظهيرية ويكره الكلام بعد انفجار الصبح، وإذا صلى الفجر جاز له الكلام وفي القنية : تأخير العشاء إلى ما زاد على نصف الليل والعصر إلى وقت اصفرار الشمس والمغرب إلى اشتباك النجوم يكره كراهة تحريم.
The commentator: it is disliked to speak after them (prayers) without need, but if there is need, then no. Similarly, reciting Quran, dhikr, stories of the righteous, and discussing fiqh and hadith with a guest. And in al-Zahiriyya: speaking after dawn is disliked, and when one prays Fajr, speaking is permissible for him. And in al-Qunyah: delaying Isha to beyond half the night, and Asr to the time of yellowing of the sun, and Maghrib until the intertwining of stars, is disliked with a weight of tahrim (makruh tahrimi).
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expansion (sharh) by the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq on a previous matn statement about disliked actions after prayer. It first states that it is makruh (disliked) to engage in worldly speech after certain prayers (commonly understood as Fajr and Asr) without a valid need. If there is a need, it is permissible. Permissible activities include reciting Quran, dhikr, narrating stories of the righteous, and discussing fiqh and hadith with a guest. Then, quoting al-Zahiriyya, it adds that speaking after dawn (before Fajr prayer) is also disliked, but after performing Fajr prayer, speaking becomes permissible. Finally, from al-Qunyah, it gives a ruling that delaying Isha prayer beyond half the night, Asr prayer until the sun yellows, and Maghrib prayer until the stars are fully intertwined is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). This means it is close to haram and one should avoid it. The text does not provide proof for these rulings; they are drawn from later Hanafi works.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريم (karāha taḥrīm): A level of prohibition that is close to haram; the one who does it is sinful and blameworthy, but it is not as severe as haram because the evidence is zanni.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, delaying which prayer until the stars intertwine is considered makruh tahrimi?
A) Fajr
B) Maghrib
C) Isha
D) Asr

Key Takeaway
Delaying Isha beyond half the night, Asr until yellowing, and Maghrib until stars intertwine is makruh tahrimi; speech after prayer without need is simply makruh, with exceptions for need and beneficial talk.

Expediting Zuhr in Winter and Defining Seasons
Commentary on recommendation to expedite Zuhr in winter and definition of seasons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on expediting Zuhr to winter and analogous seasons, using the definition of seasons from the Hanafi texts.

Core Idea
Expediting Zuhr is recommended in both summer and winter; spring follows winter, autumn follows summer.

The matn states that expediting Zuhr is recommended in summer. This lesson expands that ruling to winter and clarifies how the seasons are defined, especially when a fixed calendar is unavailable. The commentator further extends the ruling to spring and autumn by analogy based on the prevailing cold or heat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Recognize that the text recommends (nadb) expediting Zuhr in winter, just as in summer. This is a sunnah, not wajib.
The proof for summer is from hadith (not quoted here); the winter case is based on analogy (qiyas).
2
Understand the Definition of Seasons
Learn the two methods: astronomical calculation if available, otherwise continuous cold/heat or the need for fire and warm clothing.
Definitions are from al-Khulasa and mashayikh; they affect when the ruling applies.
3
Apply Analogy to Spring and Autumn
Using the definition of spring (when cold breaks) and autumn (when heat breaks), conclude that spring is annexed to winter (expedite) and autumn to summer (expedite).
The commentator's 'which appears' is his tarjih; no earlier text discussed spring/autumn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وتعجيل ظهر الشتاء أي وندب تعجيل ظهر الشتاء لما روينا في ظهر الصيف. وفي الخلاصة : من آخر الإيمان : إن كان عندهم حساب يعرفون به الشتاء والصيف فهو على حسابهم، وإن لم يكن فالشتاء ما اشتد فيه البرد على الدوام، والصيف ما يشتد فيه الحر على الدوام، فعلى قياس هذا الربيع ما ينكسر فيه البرد على الدوام، والخريف ما ينكسر فيه الحر على الدوام. ومن مشايخنا من قال : الشتاء ما يحتاج الناس فيه إلى شيئين إلى الوقود ولبس الحشو، والصيف ما يستغنى فيه عنهما، والربيع والخريف ما يستغنى عن أحدهما اهـ. ولم أر من تكلم على حكم صلاة الظهر في الربيع والخريف، والذي يظهر أن الربيع ملحق بالشتاء في هذا الحكم والخريف ملحق بالصيف فيه
He said: (And expediting Zuhr in winter) i.e., it is recommended to expedite Zuhr in winter as we narrated in (the case of) Zuhr in summer. And in al-Khulasa: 'From the end of faith: if they have a calculation by which they know winter and summer, then it is according to their calculation; if not, then winter is when cold is continuous, and summer is when heat is continuous. By analogy, spring is when cold breaks continuously, and autumn is when heat breaks continuously. And some of our mashayikh said: winter is when people need two things: firewood and wearing padded clothing; summer is when they are free from both; spring and autumn are when they are free from one of them.' He said: And I have not seen anyone speak about the ruling of Zuhr prayer in spring and autumn, and what appears is that spring is annexed to winter in this ruling and autumn is annexed to summer.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'وتعجيل ظهر الشتاء' (expediting Zuhr in winter). The commentator explains that it is recommended (nadb) to expedite Zuhr prayer in winter, just as it is recommended to expedite it in summer (as is known from other texts). Then he quotes from al-Khulasa a discussion defining the seasons. The definition depends on local custom: if people have a fixed calendar, they use it; otherwise, winter is when it is consistently cold, summer when consistently hot. Spring is when the cold breaks, autumn when the heat breaks. Some Hanafi mashayikh define winter as the time when people need both fire and warm clothing, summer as when they need neither, and spring/autumn as when they need one. The commentator then notes that he has not found a specific ruling for Zuhr in spring and autumn, but he opines that spring should follow the ruling of winter (expedite) and autumn should follow summer (presumably also expedite? The summer ruling is also expedite, so both seasons get expedite). This is a talil (reasoning) about the 'illa (effective cause) for expediting: the shortness of time or desire for earlier prayer.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jīl): Performing the prayer at the beginning of its time (first half).
الشتاء (al-shitā'): Winter: defined either by astronomical calculation or by continuous cold weather, or by the need for fire and warm clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By the presence of clouds
B) By continuous cold weather
C) By the length of the night
D) By the position of the sun

Key Takeaway
Expediting Zuhr is recommended in all seasons; winter and spring are treated as summer and autumn respectively based on the prevailing temperature.

Expediting Asr and Isha on Cloudy Days
Commentary on expediting two prayers on cloudy days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on expediting Asr and Isha on cloudy days and explain the rationale behind it.

Core Idea
Expedite Asr and Isha on cloudy days to avoid harm—delay is for caution, not necessity.

On a cloudy day, prayer times are uncertain, leading to different views on whether to pray early or late. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling that while Zuhr and Maghrib are delayed to confirm time entry, Asr and Isha should be expedited to protect against negative consequences. The commentary provides the legal reasoning and refutes an alternative caution-based approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is expediting Asr and Isha prayers on a cloudy day. The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah (recommended), not wajib. Understand this as a recommended practice to avoid potential harm.
The matn phrase 'عين يوم غين' refers to the early part of a cloudy day.
2
Understand the rationale (illa)
For Asr: delaying may cause it to fall into the disliked time (when the sun yellows). For Isha: delaying reduces congregation because of potential rain and mud. Both reasons aim to prevent practical harm.
These are teleological arguments (talil) based on benefits and harms.
3
Analyze the refutation of opposing view
The text refutes the narration of al-Hasan that delaying all prayers is better for caution. The author argues that caution must not lead to praying outside the time; since Zuhr and Maghrib are delayed on a cloudy day, one knows that time has entered, so expediting Asr and Isha is safe.
The key point: permissibility of performance is after time entry, not before.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
On a cloudy day: delay Zuhr and Maghrib to be certain of time entry, but expedite Asr (pray early in its time) and expedite Isha (pray soon after Maghrib time is confirmed, before congregation diminishes).
This balances caution with practical considerations of valid performance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وما فيها عين يوم غين أي وندب تعجيل كل صلاة في أولها عين يوم الغيم وهي العصر والعشاء لأن في تأخير العصر احتمال وقوعها في الوقت المكروه، وفي تأخير العشاء تقليل الجماعة على احتمال المطر والطين والغين لغة في الغيم وهو السحاب. كذا في الصحاح وليس فيه وهم الوقوع قبل الوقت لأن الظهر قد أخر في هذا اليوم، وكذا المغرب وبهذا اندفع ما رجح به في غاية البيان رواية الحسن أن التأخير أفضل في سائر الصلوات يوم الغيم بأنه أقرب إلى الاحتياط الجواز الأداء بعد الوقت لا قبله
He said: (And what is in it is the eye of a cloudy day) i.e., it is recommended to expedite every prayer at its beginning on a cloudy day, and they are Asr and Isha, because in delaying Asr there is a possibility of it falling in the disliked time, and in delaying Isha there is a reduction of the congregation due to the possibility of rain and mud. And 'ghayn' is a language variant of 'ghaym' (cloud). Thus in al-Sihah. And there is no illusion of falling before the time because Zuhr has been delayed on this day, and similarly Maghrib. And by this is refuted what is given preponderance in Ghayat al-Bayan of the narration of al-Hasan that delay is better in all prayers on a cloudy day, because it is closer to caution, but permissibility is performance after the time, not before.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'وما فيها عين يوم غين' (and what is in it on a cloudy day), referring to the ruling to expedite certain prayers when there is cloud cover. The commentator explains that it is recommended (nadb) to expedite every prayer at its beginning (first time) on a cloudy day, specifically Asr and Isha. The reason ('illa) for expediting Asr is that delaying it may cause it to fall into the time when prayer is makruh (when the sun yellows). For Isha, delaying may reduce the congregation because people might be hindered by rain or mud. The word 'ghayn' is a dialectical variant of 'ghaym' (cloud). Then the commentator addresses a potential concern: there is no fear of praying before the time because on a cloudy day, Zuhr has already been delayed (as per a previous ruling), so one knows that Asr time has entered by the delay of Zuhr. Similarly, Maghrib is delayed to confirm sunset. This refutes the view of al-Hasan that delaying all prayers on a cloudy day is better, because that caution might lead to praying after the time, whereas the original ruling is to pray within the time.

Key Terms
عين اليوم ('ayn al-yawm): The beginning of the daytime, i.e., the earliest part of the prayer time.
الغين (al-ghayn): A dialectical variant of 'غيم' (cloud), used in the text as a synonym.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Isha expedited on a cloudy day according to the passage?
A) To avoid the disliked time
B) To increase the congregation size
C) Because it is always recommended
D) To prevent confusion with Maghrib

Key Takeaway
On a cloudy day, expedite Asr to avoid the disliked time and expedite Isha to preserve congregation, while delaying Zuhr and Maghrib to confirm time entry.

Delaying Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib on Cloudy Days: The Ruling and Reason
Commentary on delaying Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib on cloudy days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi recommendation to delay Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib on cloudy days and explain the reason for delaying Maghrib.

Core Idea
Delay Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib on cloudy days to ensure correct timing; Maghrib delay avoids praying before sunset.

On a cloudy day, determining precise prayer times becomes difficult due to reduced visibility. The Hanafi school addresses this by recommending that three specific prayers—Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib—be delayed, while others are expedited. This lesson unpacks the passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the reasoning behind each delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayers to delay
From the text, state that Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib should be delayed on a cloudy day. These are the prayers 'other than those whose beginning is the eye of a cloudy day' (i.e., not expedited).
The expedited prayers (Asr and Isha) are mentioned elsewhere in the matn.
2
Understand the reason for Fajr and Zuhr
The commentator explains that Fajr and Zuhr have no disliked period in their time, so delaying them does not cause harm. This contrasts with Asr and Isha, which have disliked times later.
The 'illa for Fajr and Zuhr is the absence of karahah in their time windows.
3
Understand the reason for Maghrib
Maghrib is delayed out of fear that it might be performed before the actual sunset due to the severe confusion (iltibas) caused by clouds. This ensures the prayer is offered after true sunset.
The 'illa for Maghrib is the risk of praying outside the time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ويؤخر غيره فيه) أي يؤخر غير ما في أوله عين يوم غين وهي الفجر والظهر والمغرب لأن الفجر والظهر لا كراهة في وقتهما فلا يضر التأخير، والمغرب يخاف وقوعها قبل الغروب لشدة الالتباس .
He said: (And other prayers are delayed on it) i.e., other than those whose beginning is the eye of a cloudy day are delayed, and they are Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib, because Fajr and Zuhr have no dislike in their times, so delay does not harm; and Maghrib is feared to occur before sunset due to severe confusion.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'ويؤخر غيره فيه' (and other than them are delayed on it). The commentator explains that on a cloudy day, the prayers that are not expedited (i.e., Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib) should be delayed. The reason ('illa): For Fajr and Zuhr, their times (after dawn and after zenith) have no disliked period within them, so delaying them is not problematic. For Maghrib, if it were prayed immediately at the calculated sunset, there is a risk of praying before actual sunset due to the heaviness of the cloud cover causing confusion. Therefore, it is recommended to delay Maghrib slightly to ensure sunset has occurred. This is in contrast to the expedited prayers (Asr and Isha) which are advanced to avoid later dislike.

Key Terms
الالتباس (al-iltibās): Confusion or uncertainty, here referring to the difficulty in determining the exact time when the sun has set due to clouds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To avoid makruh time.
B) Because of fear of praying before sunset due to confusion.
C) To combine with Isha.
D) Because it is wajib.

Key Takeaway
On cloudy days, delay Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib to avoid uncertainty about correct timing.

Prohibited Times for Prayer and the Asr Exception
Commentary citing hadith to justify a fiqh ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited times for supererogatory prayers, and apply the exception for Asr prayer of that day when the obligation is about to expire.

Core Idea
Three times when nafl prayer is forbidden; only the current Asr may be prayed at sunset.

The Hanafi school prohibits certain supererogatory prayers during three specific times of the day: sunrise, zenith, and sunset. This ruling is firmly established by hadith. However, there is a critical exception: if the Asr prayer of that day has not yet been performed, it is permissible to pray it at sunset because it is an obligatory act with a fixed time that cannot be delayed. This lesson examines the textual proof and the legal reasoning behind the prohibition and its exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
From the matn and hadith, list the three times when the Prophet forbade prayer and burial of the dead.
These are: sunrise until it rises high, zenith until the sun declines, and sunset until it sets.
2
State the prohibited acts
According to the matn, the prohibition covers prayer (nafl), sajda tilawa, and janaza prayer. The hadith adds burial of the dead.
Burial is included in the hadith but is not the focus of this fiqh ruling.
3
Note the exception for Asr
The matn adds 'except the Asr of that day'. This means if one has not yet performed the current day's Asr prayer, it is allowed at sunset because it is an obligatory prayer whose time is about to expire.
This exception is derived from other proofs that obligatory prayers must be performed within their extended time.
4
Locate the hadith proof
The commentator cites the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir (narrated by the group except Bukhari). Read the Arabic carefully to see the exact wording of the three times.
The hadith uses 'qā'im al-ẓahīra' for zenith.
5
Understand the legal derivation (wajh al-dalalah)
The explicit prohibition (نهى) in the hadith indicates tahrim (prohibition) for supererogatory acts. The exception for Asr is based on the principle that an obligatory duty cannot be left due to a time prohibition when its time is expiring.
This is a dalala zanni but accepted by all schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ( ومنع عن الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة عند الطلوع والاستواء والغروب إلا عصر يومه) لما روى الجماعة إلا البخاري من حديث عقبة بن عامر الجهني رضي الله عنه قال : ثلاث ساعات كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ينهانا أن نصلي فيهن أو أن نقبر فيهن موتانا : حين تطلع الشمس حتى ترتفع، وحين يقوم قائم الظهيرة حتى تزول، وحين تضيف الشمس للغروب حتى تغرب
He said: (And prohibition of prayer, sajda tilawa, and janaza prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset, except the Asr of that day) because the group except al-Bukhari narrated from the hadith of Uqba ibn Amir al-Juhani, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'There are three times when the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم forbade us to pray or to bury our dead: when the sun rises until it rises high, when the sun is at its zenith until it declines, and when the sun inclines for sunset until it sets.'
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'ومنع عن الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة عند الطلوع والاستواء والغروب إلا عصر يومه' (and prohibition of prayer, sajda tilawa, and janaza prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset, except the Asr of that day). The commentator provides the proof: a hadith from Uqba ibn Amir narrated by the authors of the collections (except al-Bukhari) that the Prophet forbade prayer and burying the dead at three times: sunrise until it rises high, midday until it passes the zenith, and sunset until it sets. The exception for Asr of that day means that if one has not yet prayed Asr, it is permissible to pray it at sunset because it is an obligatory prayer that must be performed within its time, and the prohibition is for supererogatory prayers.

Key Terms
الاستواء (al-istiwā'): The time when the sun is at its zenith (midday) before it begins to decline.
قائم الظهيرة (qā'im al-ẓahīra): The time when the sun is directly overhead and shadows are at their shortest, just before midday.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) When the sun is at the meridian until it passes
C) When the sun is directly overhead until it moves
D) When the day is at its hottest until afternoon

Key Takeaway
The three prohibited times for supererogatory prayers are sunrise, zenith, and sunset, but the current day's Asr prayer is excepted at sunset because it is obligatory and its time is expiring.
