Prayer Timings on Cloudy Days: Hastening and Delay
Hanafi commentary on rulings for prayer timing on cloudy days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on which prayers are hastened and which are delayed on a cloudy day, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding delaying Maghrib.

Core Idea
On a cloudy day, hasten Asr and Isha; delay Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib; a small delay of Maghrib with an excuse is not disliked.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rules for prayer timings on cloudy days, when it is difficult to determine exact times due to overcast skies. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, commented upon by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, provides specific guidance on which prayers should be hastened or delayed. It also addresses an intra-Hanafi difference regarding the delay of Maghrib prayer, offering a nuanced position that balances precaution with practical need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five daily prayers and the general principle
First, recall the five daily prayers. The text divides them into two groups on a cloudy day: those that are hastened (ta'jil) and those that are delayed (takhir). Understand the rationale: hastening avoids falling into disliked times or losing congregation; delaying avoids performing before the time due to confusion.
The prayers are Fajr, Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha.
2
Distinguish between hastened and delayed prayers with reasoning
Asr and Isha are hastened. For Asr, delaying risks falling into the disliked time (makruh time). For Isha, delaying reduces the congregation due to potential rain and mud. Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib are delayed: Fajr and Zuhr have no disliked time in their beginnings, so delay does not harm; Maghrib is delayed to avoid performing before sunset due to confusion.
The reasoning is based on the probability of missing the optimal time or committing a disliked act.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on delaying Maghrib
The text mentions an intra-Hanafi dispute: one narration says delaying Maghrib is makruh (disliked), another says it is not makruh unless the twilight (shafaq) disappears. The preferred view (asahh) is that a small delay due to an excuse (e.g., travel, meal, cloudy day itself) is not makruh. This is supported by the hadith of Ibn Umar who delayed until a star appeared.
The excuse factor is critical. The hadith of Ibn Umar is a key proof for the permissibility of a small delay.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a traveler on a cloudy day who arrives at a rest stop just after sunset. Should he pray Maghrib immediately or may he delay it slightly? According to the preferred view, since travel is a valid excuse, a small delay (e.g., to rest briefly) is not makruh. However, if he delays without excuse or for a long time, it may become makruh.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that a person with an excuse does not commit a sin by a slight delay.
5
Recognize definitions of ta'jil and takhir from the commentary
The commentary defines ta'jil (hastening) as performing the prayer in the first half of its time, or not separating adhan and iqama except briefly. Takhir (delaying) is the opposite. Delaying prayer specifically to perform two rak'ahs (e.g., nafl before Maghrib) is considered makruh, but a small delay for a valid reason is not.
These definitions help clarify what constitutes significant delay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤخر غيره فيه ومنع عن الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة عند الطلوع والاستواء والغروب الأول إلا من هو بالمهملة: ويكره تأخير المغرب في رواية، وفي أخرى لا ما لم يغب الشفق. الأصح هو عذر كالسفر ونحوه أو يكون قليلاً، وفي الكراهة بتطويل القراءة خلاف اهـ. وفي الإسرار : تعجيل الصلاة أداؤها في النصف الأول من وقتها. وفي فتح القدير: تعجيلها أن لا يفصل بین الأذان والإقامة إلا بجلسة خفيفة أو سكتة على الخلاف الذي سيأتي، وتأخيرها لصلاة ركعتين مكروهة، وما روى الأصحاب عن ابن عمر أنه أخرها حتى بدا نجم فأعتق رقبة يقتضي أن ذلك القليل الذي لا يتعلق به كراهة هو ما قبل ظهور النجم وفي المنية : لا يكره للسفر وللمائدة أو كان يوم غيم. وذكر الاسبيجابي إذا جيء بجنازة بغد الغروب بدؤوا بالمغرب ثم بها ثم بسنة المغرب .اهـ. وقد تقدم أن كراهة تأخيرها تحريمية قوله (وما فيها عين يوم (فين أي وندب تعجيل كل صلاة في أولها عين يوم الغيم وهي العصر والعشاء لأن في تأخير العصر احتمال وقوعها في الوقت المكروه، وفي تأخير العشاء تقليل الجماعة على احتمال المطر والطين والغين لغة في الغيم وهو السحاب. كذا في الصحاح وليس فيه وهم الوقوع قبل الوقت لأن الظهر قد أخر في هذا اليوم، وكذا المغرب وبهذا اندفع ما رجح به في غاية البيان رواية الحسن أن التأخير أفضل في سائر الصلوات يوم الغيم بأنه أقرب إلى الاحتياط الجواز الأداء بعد الوقت لا قبله قوله ( ويؤخر غيره فيه) أي يؤخر غير ما في أوله عين يوم غين وهي الفجر والظهر والمغرب لأن الفجر والظهر لا كراهة في وقتهما فلا يضر التأخير، والمغرب يخاف وقوعها قبل الغروب لشدة الالتباس .
And he delays other than it in it, and it is prohibited from prayer, prostration of recitation, and funeral prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset except the Asr of that day. The correct view: it is disliked to delay Maghrib in one narration, and in another no, as long as the twilight has not disappeared. The soundest is if there is an excuse like travel or similar, or it is little. And in the dislike of lengthening recitation, there is disagreement. And in al-Israr: hastening prayer is performing it in the first half of its time. And in Fath al-Qadir: hastening it is that one does not separate between the adhan and iqama except with a light sitting or silence according to the difference to come. And delaying it for two rak'ahs is disliked. And what the associates narrated from Ibn Umar that he delayed it until a star appeared and then freed a slave indicates that the small amount that is not associated with dislike is before the appearance of the star. And in al-Munya: it is not disliked for travel, for a meal, or if it is a cloudy day. And al-Isbijabi mentioned: if a funeral is brought after sunset, they begin with Maghrib, then with it, then with the sunnah of Maghrib. And it has preceded that the dislike of delaying it is prohibition (tahrim). His statement: 'and what in it is the eye of the day of cloud' meaning it is recommended to hasten every prayer at its beginning on a cloudy day, which are Asr and Isha because delaying Asr risks its falling into the disliked time, and delaying Isha reduces the congregation due to the possibility of rain and mud. 'Ghayn' is a variant of 'ghaym' meaning cloud. Thus in al-Sihah. And there is no fear of falling before the time because Zuhr has been delayed on this day, and similarly Maghrib. And by this is repelled what was preferred in Ghayat al-Bayan of the narration of Hasan that delay is better in all prayers on a cloudy day because it is closer to precaution, since performance after the time is permissible, not before. His statement: 'and he delays other than it in it' means he delays other than what is at its beginning on a cloudy day, which are Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib because there is no dislike in their times, so delay does not harm, and Maghrib is feared to fall before sunset due to severe confusion.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the rulings on delaying prayers on cloudy days. The matn states: 'And he delays other than it in it, and it is prohibited from prayer...' The commentary first addresses the ruling on delaying Maghrib prayer, noting an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: one narration considers it makruh, another does not unless the twilight disappears. The soundest view is that a small delay due to an excuse like travel is not makruh. The commentary then defines hastening and delaying, citing Fath al-Qadir that hastening means not separating adhan and iqama except briefly. Delaying prayer to pray two rak'ahs (such as the nafl before Maghrib) is considered makruh, but a small delay is excused based on the hadith of Ibn Umar who delayed until a star appeared and then freed a slave. On a cloudy day, it is recommended to hasten Asr and Isha because delaying them risks missing the optimal time or reducing the congregation. As for Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib, they are recommended to be delayed on a cloudy day because there is no harm in delaying Fajr and Zuhr, and Maghrib is delayed to ensure it is after sunset due to confusion. The commentary refutes the view that delay is better for all prayers on a cloudy day, arguing that the precaution is to perform after the time, not before. Key terms include 'يوم الغيم' (cloudy day), 'تعجيل' (hastening), 'تأخير' (delaying), and 'كراهة تحريمية' (prohibitive dislike).

Key Terms
يوم الغيم (yawm al-ghaym): A cloudy day; the text discusses special rulings for prayer timings on such days.
تعجيل (ta'jil): Hastening or performing a prayer early in its time.
كراهة تحريمية (karahah tahrimiyyah): Dislike close to prohibition; an action that is prohibited but with a less severe status than haram when based on a zanni evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
On cloudy days, hasten Asr and Isha; delay Fajr, Zuhr, and Maghrib; a small delay of Maghrib with a valid excuse is not disliked.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Prayers in the Three Prohibited Times
Explains the three disliked times and the rulings for obligatory and voluntary prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing obligatory and voluntary prayers during the three prohibited times and explain the legal basis (dalil) for the ruling.

Core Idea
A prayer offered during sunrise, zenith, or sunset is either invalid (fard/wajib) or valid but makruh tahrimi (nafl) due to resemblance to disbelievers.

The Prophet ﷺ forbade prayer at three specific times of the day: sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The Hanafi school analyzes this prohibition to determine whether the prayer is valid or invalid, depending on its type. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the reasoning, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times and the hadith evidence
The passage cites a hadith from 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir forbidding prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset. A second hadith from Malik explains the reason: the sun rises between the horns of Shaytan.
The prohibition includes funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) as well.
2
Determine the level of prohibition
The hadith is zanni al-thubut (probable transmission), so it indicates karaha tahrimiyya (dislike approaching prohibition), not outright haram. Karaha tahrimiyya is in the rank of wajib.
3
Distinguish between fard/wajib and nafl prayers
For fard or wajib prayers, performing them in these times renders them invalid (ghayr sahih) due to a deficiency in the pillars (arkan). For nafl prayers, they are valid but makruh tahrimi, and the worshipper must cut them if started and make them up later.
4
Understand the reason: deficiency in the pillars
The deficiency is not in the time itself but in the arkan because of the resemblance to the worship of disbelievers. This is derived from the hadith about the sun and Shaytan.
Unlike leaving a wajib, which does not affect the arkan, performing the arkan in these times introduces deficiency.
5
Apply the ruling to related acts (witr, nadhr, tawaf rak'ahs)
Witr, vowed prayers (nadhr), and the two rak'ahs of tawaf are considered wajib for this ruling; thus they are invalid in these times.

كتاب الصلاة
ثلاث ساعات كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ينهانا أن نصلي فيهن وأن نقبر فيهن موتانا : حين تطلع الشمس بازغة حتى ترتفع، وحين يقوم قائم الظهيرة حتى تميل وحين تضيف للغروب حتى تغرب . ومعنى تضيف تميل وهو بالمثناة الفوقية المفتوحة فالضاد المعجمة المفتوحة فالمثناة التحتية المشددة، وأصله تتضيف حذف منه إحدى التاءين. والمراد بقوله وإن نقبر» صلاة الجنازة كناية لأنها ذكر الرديف وإرادة المردوف إذا الدفن غير مكروه خلافاً لأبي داود لما رواه ابن دقيق العيد في الإمام عن عقبة قال : نهانا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن نصلي على موتانا عند طلوع الشمس . أطلق الصلاة فشمل فرضها ونفلها لأن الكل ممنوع فإن المكروه من قبيل الممنوع لأنها تحريمية لما عرف من أن النهي الظني الثبوت غير المصروف عن مقتضاه يفيد كراهة التحريم، وإن كان قطعية أفاد التحريم، فالتحريم في مقابلة الفرض في الرتبة، وكراهة التحريم في رتبة الواجب، والتنزيه في رتبة المندوب، والنهي في حديث عقبة من الأول فكان الثابت به كراهة التحريم. فإن كانت الصلاة فرضاً أو واجبة فهي غير صحيحة لأنها لنقصان في الوقت بسبب الأداء فيه تشبيهاً بعبادة الكفار المستفاد من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «إن الشمس تطلع بين قرني شيطان إذا ارتفعت فارقها، ثم إذا استوت ،قارنها فإذا زالت فارقها، فإذا دنت للغروب ،قارنها، وإذا غربت فارقها ونهى عن الصلاة في تلك الساعات» رواه مالك في الموطأ. وهذا هو المراد بنقصان الوقت وإلا فالوقت لا نقص فيه نفسه بل هو وقت كسائر الأوقات إنما النقص في الأركان فلا يتأدى بها ما كاملاً، فخرج الجواب عما قيل لو ترك بعض الواجبات صحت الصلاة أنها ناقصة يتأدى بها الكامل لأن ترك الواجب لا يدخل النقص في الأركان التي هي المقومة للحقيقة بخلاف فعل الأركان في هذه الأوقات وإنما جاز القضاء في أرض الغير وإن كان النهي ثم لمعنى في غيره أيضاً لأن النهي ثم ورد للمكان وهنا للزمان، واتصال الفعل بالزمان أكثر لأنه داخل في ماهيته ولهذا فسد صوم يوم النحر وإن ورد النهي فيه لمعنى في غيره لأن النهي فيه باعتبار الوقت، والصوم يقوم به ويطول بطوله ويقصر بقصره لأنه معياره فازداد الأثر فصار فاسداً. وإن كانت الصلاة نفلاً فهي صحيحة مكروهة حتى وجب قضاؤه إذا قطعه ويجب قطعه وقضاؤه في غير مكروه في ظاهر الرواية، ولو أتمه خرج عن عهدة ما لزمه بذلك الشروع. وفي المبسوط : القطع أفضل والأول هو مقتضى الدليل والوتر داخل في الفرض لأنه فرض عملي أو في الواجب فلا يصح في هذه الأوقات كما في الكافي والمنذور المطلق الذي لم يقيد بوقت الكراهة داخل فيه أيضاً كما صرح به الاسبيجابي والنفل إذا شرع فيه في وقت مستحب ثم أفسده داخل فيه أيضاً فلا يصح في هذه الأوقات كما في المحيط بخلاف ما لو قضى في وقت مكروه ما قطعه من النفل المشروع فيه في وقت مكروه حيث يخرجه عن العهدة وإن كان آثماً لأن وجوبه ضرورة صيانة المؤدي عن البطلان ليس غير والصون عن البطلان يحصل مع النقصان كما لو نذر إن يصلي في الوقت المكروه فأدى فيه يصح ويأثم، ويجب أن يصلي في غيره. وقول الشارح فيهما والأفضل أن يصلي في غيره ضعيف كما قدمناه . ويدخل في الواجب ركعتا الطواف فلا تصح في هذه الأوقات الثلاثة، اعتبرت واجبة في حق هذا الحكم ونفلاً في كراهتها بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر احتياطاً فيهما. وعبارة الكتاب أولى من عبارة أصله الوافي حيث قال : لا تصح صلاة إلى آخره لما علمت أن الصحة إنما هن في الفرائض والواجبات لا في النوافل بخلاف المنع فإنه يعم الكل.
The Book of Prayer. Three hours during which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us from praying and from burying our dead: when the sun rises until it ascends, when the sun is at its zenith until it inclines, and when it inclines towards setting until it sets. The meaning of 'tadif' is 'tamil' (inclines). It is spelt with an open above-the-line (fatha), then a full-point (dad), then an open above-the-line (fatha), then a double-under-the-line (shadda). Its original is 'tatadif' with one of the two ta's elided. By his saying 'and that we bury' is meant funeral prayer as a metonymy, because it mentions the associate and intends the associated, as burial is not disliked, contrary to Abu Dawud due to what Ibn Daqiq al-'Id narrated in al-Imam from 'Uqbah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us from praying over our dead at sunrise. He (the narrator) made the prayer absolute, so it includes obligatory and voluntary, because all are prohibited. Indeed, the disliked is of the type of prohibited because it is haram (tahrimiyya), as it is known that a prohibition that is zanni in transmission and not diverted from its apparent meaning indicates karaha tahrimiyya (disliked of prohibition), and if it were qat'i, it would indicate tahrim (prohibition). So tahrim is opposite of fard in rank, karaha tahrimiyya is in the rank of wajib, and karaha tanzihiyya is in the rank of mandub. The prohibition in the hadith of 'Uqbah is of the first type, so what is established by it is karaha tahrimiyya. If the prayer is fard or wajib, it is invalid, because of a deficiency in the time due to performing it therein, resembling the worship of the disbelievers, derived from his saying (peace be upon him): 'The sun rises between the two horns of shaitan; when it ascends, it separates from it; when it is at zenith, it accompanies it; when it declines, it separates; and when it approaches setting, it accompanies it; and when it sets, it separates; and he forbade prayer in these hours' - narrated by Malik in al-Muwatta. This is what is meant by deficiency of time, otherwise time itself has no deficiency, rather it is like other times; the deficiency is in the pillars (arkan), so the complete (prayer) is not fulfilled by them. This is the answer to what was said: if one leaves some wajibat, the prayer is valid but deficient, and the complete is fulfilled by it, because leaving wajib does not bring deficiency into the pillars which constitute the reality, unlike performing the pillars in these times. And it is permissible to make up (qada) on someone else's land even though the prohibition was there for another meaning because the prohibition there was for the place, and here for the time. The connection of the act to time is greater because it is part of its essence, and for this reason the fast on the day of sacrifice (yawm al-nahr) is invalid even though the prohibition was for another meaning, because the prohibition therein is with regard to the time, and fasting stands by it and lengthens with its length and shortens with its shortness because it is its measure, so the effect increases and it becomes invalid. If the prayer is voluntary (nafl), it is valid but disliked (makruh), such that it becomes necessary to make it up if he cuts it, and he must cut it and make it up in a non-disliked time in the apparent narration. If he completes it, he is discharged from the obligation that became incumbent by that commencement. In al-Mabsut: cutting is better, and the first is the result of the evidence. Witr is included in fard because it is practical (amali) fard, or in wajib, so it is not valid in these times, as in al-Kafi. The absolute nadhr (vow) that is not restricted to a disliked time is also included in it, as stated by al-Isbijabi. And an optional prayer that one begins in a recommended time then invalidates it is also included, so it is not valid in these times, as in al-Muhit. Contrary to if one makes up in a disliked time the part he cut from an optional prayer he began in a disliked time - he is discharged from responsibility although it is sinful, because its obligation is a necessity to protect the performer from invalidity and nothing else. Protection from invalidity is achieved with deficiency, just as if he vowed to pray in a disliked time and performed it therein, it is valid and he is sinful, and he must pray in other than it. The statement of the commentator (sharh) that 'the better is to pray in other than it' is weak as we have mentioned. And included in wajib are the two rak'ahs of tawaf, so they are not valid in these three times. They are considered wajib with respect to this ruling, and nafl with respect to their dislike after fajr and 'asr, as a precaution in both. And the wording of the book (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) is better than the wording of its original al-Wafi where it said: 'prayer is not valid' etc., because you know that validity is only in fard and wajib prayers, not in nafl, unlike prohibition which includes all.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on prayers during the three prohibited times: sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The author begins by citing a hadith from the Prophet (ﷺ) forbidding prayer and burial of the dead in these times. He clarifies that the prohibition includes all prayers, both obligatory and voluntary, and that the underlying reason is to avoid resembling the worship of disbelievers, as the sun is associated with shaitan during these moments. He then distinguishes between the types of prohibition: the hadith is zanni al-thubut (probable transmission), so it establishes karaha tahrimiyya (dislike approaching prohibition), not outright tahrim. For obligatory prayers (fard or wajib), performing them in these times renders them invalid (ghayr sahih) because of a deficiency in the time that affects the pillars (arkan) of prayer, unlike missing a wajib which does not invalidate. For voluntary prayers, they are valid but makruh tahrimi; if one begins a nafl in these times, it is wajib to cut it and make it up in a non-disliked time. The passage also includes witr (considered fard or wajib according to different views), nadhr (vowed prayers), and the two rak'ahs of tawaf, all treated as wajib and thus invalid in these times. The author prefers the wording of Kanz al-Daqa'iq which distinguishes between validity (sihha) for obligatory prayers and prohibition (man') for all, over the wording of al-Wafi which says 'prayer is not valid' without distinction.

Key Terms
كراهة التحريم (karāha taḥrīmiyya): A disliked action that is close to prohibition, established by a zanni evidence. It is in the rank of wajib; its omission does not invalidate the act but requires compensation.
النقصان (al-nuqṣān): Deficiency in the time that affects the pillars of prayer, making the prayer incomplete. Here it refers to the spiritual deficiency due to resemblance to worship of disbelievers, not a literal deficiency of time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing the two rak'ahs of tawaf during sunrise according to the Hanafi school?
A) They are valid and recommended.
B) They are invalid (not valid).
C) They are valid but makruh tanzihi.
D) They are makruh tahrimi and must be cut.

Key Takeaway
Performing obligatory prayers during the three prohibited times renders them invalid; voluntary prayers are valid but disliked and must be cut.

Salah — Prayer

The Hanafi Position on Missed Prayers (Fawa'it) During Prohibited Times
Inter-madhhab dispute on fawa'it in prohibited times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it) are included in the prohibition of prayer during the three hated times and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.'

Core Idea
A specific prohibition (hadith of 'Uqbah) overrides a general command to make up missed prayers, so qada is also prohibited in the three times.

Having established the three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset) and the general prohibition of prayer therein, the author now addresses a critical inter-madhhab dispute: does this prohibition apply to missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it) as well? The Shafi'i school, relying on the well-known hadith commanding immediate makeup of missed prayers, argues that fawa'it are exempt. The Hanafi school, however, employs a fundamental usul principle—that a specific text (khas) only limits a general text ('amm) if it is concurrent (muqaran) in its revelation—to maintain that the prohibition covers all prayers, including missed ones. This lesson dissects the arguments and traces the practical ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting texts
One text is the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir which specifically prohibits prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The other is the hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, then let him pray it when he remembers it,' which commands makeup of missed prayers at any time.
These are the primary dalil in the dispute.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i considers the makeup command as a specific exception (khas) to the general prohibition, because it is addressed specifically to those who missed a prayer. Thus, fawa'it are not subject to the prohibition.
The Shafi'i school prioritizes the specific command over the general prohibition.
3
State the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that for a khas to limit an 'amm, it must be muqaran—concurrent in revelation. The makeup hadith was revealed independently and is not concurrent with the prohibition. Moreover, even if it were, the prohibition is itself specific to the three times, so it limits the general time scope of the makeup command.
This is based on Hanafi usul: 'Al-khas al-muqaran yusharrif al-amm'.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule of precedence
Since the prohibition (hadith of 'Uqbah) is a muharram (prohibitory) text, it takes precedence over an ibaha (permissive) command. Therefore, the prohibition remains effective for all prayers, including fawa'it.
The principle 'al-muharram yuqaddam 'ala al-mubah' applies.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: A person with a missed prayer cannot make it up during the three prohibited times; if he does, it is invalid. Shafi'i: He can pray it at any time, even during these times.
This is the concrete outcome that affects a Muslim's daily practice.

وأراد بسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة ما وجبت قبل هذه الأوقات، أما إذا تلاها فيها أو حضرت الجنازة فيها فأداها فإنه يصح من غير كراهة إذ الوجوب بالتلاوة والحضور لكن الأفضل التأخير فيهما. وفي التحفة الأفضل أن يصلي على الجنازة إذا حضرت في الأوقات الثلاثة ولا يؤخرها بخلاف الفرائض وظاهر التسوية بين صلاة الجنازة وسجدة التلاوة أنه لو حضرت الجنازة في غير مكروه فأخرها حتى صلى في الوقت المكروه فإنها لا تصح وتجب إعادتها كسجود التلاوة. وذكر الاسبيجابي : لو صلى صلاة الجنازة فإنه يجوز مع الكراهة ولا يعيد، ولو سجد سجدة التلاوة ينظر ؛ إن قرأها في هذا الوقت تجوز مع الكراهة وتسقط عن ذمته، وإن قرأها قبل ذلك ثم سجدها في هذا الوقت لا يجوز ويعيد اهـ. وسجدة السهو كسجدة التلاوة . كذا في المحيط - حتى لو دخل وقت الكراهة بعد السلام وعليه سهو فإنه لا يسجد لسهوه وسقط عنه لأنه لجبر النقصان المتمكن في الصلاة فجرى ذلك مجرى القضاء وقد ذلك كاملاً فلا يتأدى بالناقص . كذا في شرح المنية. وذكر في الأصل ما لم ترتفع الشمس قدر رمح فهي في حكم الطلوع واختار الفضلي أن الأنسان ما دام يقدر على النظر إلى قرص الشمس في الطلوع فلا تحل الصلاة، فإذا عجز عن النظر حلت وهو مناسب لتفسير التغير المصحح كما قدمناه وأراد بالغروب التغير كما صرح به قاضيخان في فتاواه حيث قال : وعند احمرار الشمس إلى أن تغيب والشافعي رحمه الله أخرج من النهي في حديث عقبة الفوائت عملاً بقوله عليه السلام من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فيصلها إذا ذكرها متفق عليه . والجواب عنه أن كونه مخصصاً لعموم النهي متوقف على المقارنة، فلما لم تثبت فهو معارض في بعض الأفراد فيقدم حديث عقبة لأنه محرم، ولو تنزلنا إلى طريقهم في كون الخاص مخصصاً كيفما كان فهو خاص في الصلاة عام في الأوقات، فإن وجب تخصيص عموم الصلاة في حديث عقبة وجب تخصيص حديث عقبة عموم الوقت لأنه خاص في الوقت، وتخصيص العشاء فينتفي وهم الوقوع قبل الوقت إذ التعجيل في العصر والعشاء يكون بعد التأخير في الظهر
And he intended by the prostration of recitation (sajda tilawa) and the funeral prayer (salat al-janaza) what was obligatory before these times. As for if he recites it (the verse) in them or the funeral prayer occurs in them and he performs it, then it is valid without dislike, because obligation is due to recitation and presence. But it is better to delay in both. In al-Tuhfa, it is better to pray the funeral prayer if it occurs in the three times and not to delay it, contrary to the obligatory prayers. And the apparent equality between funeral prayer and prostration of recitation is that if the funeral prayer occurs in a non-disliked time and he delays it until he prays in the disliked time, then it is not valid and must be repeated, like the prostration of recitation. Al-Isbijabi mentioned: If he prays the funeral prayer, it is permissible with dislike and he does not repeat; but if he prostrates a prostration of recitation, he considers: if he recited it in this time, it is permissible with dislike and his responsibility is discharged; if he recited it before then prostrated in this time, it is not permissible and he must repeat. The prostration of forgetfulness (sajda sahw) is like prostration of recitation. Thus in al-Muhit - even if the time of dislike enters after the salutation and he has a forgetfulness (sahw), he does not prostrate for his forgetfulness and it is dropped from him, because it is to compensate the deficiency that has settled in the prayer, so it runs the course of making up (qada), and that (the deficiency) is complete, so it is not fulfilled by the deficient. Thus in Sharh al-Munyah. And it is mentioned in al-Asl that as long as the sun has not risen the height of a spear, it is in the ruling of sunrise. Al-Fadli chose that as long as a person is able to look at the disc of the sun at sunrise, prayer is not permissible; when he is unable to look at it, it becomes permissible. And this is appropriate for the interpretation of the change (taghayyur) that validates, as we have mentioned. And he intended by sunset the change, as Qadikhan stated in his Fatawa: 'And at the reddening of the sun until it sets.' And al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) excluded the missed prayers (fawa'it) from the prohibition in the hadith of 'Uqbah, acting upon his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, then let him pray it when he remembers it' - agreed upon (muttafaq 'alayh). The answer to it is that its being a specific (khas) limiting the generality of the prohibition is dependent on concurrence (muqarana). Since it is not established, it is conflicting in some individuals, so the hadith of 'Uqbah is given precedence because it is a prohibition (muharram). And if we descend to their way that a specific limits generality in any case, then it (the hadith about missing) is specific to prayer and general to times: if it is necessary to limit the generality of prayer in the hadith of 'Uqbah, then it is necessary to limit the generality of the hadith of 'Uqbah over the generality of time because it is specific to time. And the specific (khas) of the 'isha' prayer [makes] the assumption of occurrence before time cease, for hastening in 'asr and 'isha' comes after delaying in zuhr.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of prayers in the three prohibited times, focusing on specific acts: prostration of recitation (sajda tilawa), funeral prayer (salat al-janaza), and prostration of forgetfulness (sajda sahw). The author explains that if these acts become obligatory before the disliked time, then performing them in the disliked time is valid but disliked; however, if they become obligatory during the disliked time (e.g., reciting a verse of sajda or the funeral occurring), then performing them immediately is valid without dislike, though delaying is better for sajda tilawa but not for funeral prayer. There is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: al-Isbijabi distinguishes between sajda tilawa that is recited in the disliked time (valid) and one recited earlier (invalid if postponed). The passage also clarifies the definition of the beginning and end of the prohibited times: sunrise is until the sun rises a spear's height (according to al-Asl), and the preferred view of al-Fadli is that prayer is impermissible as long as one can still see the sun's disc. For sunset, the time is from the reddening of the sun until it sets, as per Qadikhan. The final part addresses an inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i, who exempts missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it) from the prohibition, citing the hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.' The Hanafi response argues that the hadith of 'Uqbah (prohibiting prayer in these times) takes precedence because it is a specific prohibition, and the general command to make up missed prayers is general in time but specific in prayer (only for missed prayers), while the prohibition is specific to the three times. Therefore, the prohibition overrides the command for making up missed prayers in those times, meaning qada of missed prayers is also prohibited in the three disliked times.

Key Terms
الفوائت (al-fawā'it): Missed obligatory prayers that were not performed on time and must be made up.
المقارنة (al-muqārana): Concurrence or coincidence of the general and specific in terms of timing or subject matter, necessary for a specific to limit a general.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is prohibited and invalid.
C) It is valid but makruh tanzihi.
D) It is permissible but must be cut immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school includes missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it) in the prohibition of prayer during sunrise, zenith, and sunset, based on the precedence of a specific prohibition over a general command, a principle grounded in Hanafi usul.

Salah — Prayer

Prayers in Disliked Times: Validity, Sin, and Repetition
Explains ruling and conditions for prayers in disliked times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings for obligatory and supererogatory prayers in disliked times and apply the Hanafi position to special cases like tawaf and funeral prayer.

Core Idea
Obligatory prayers in disliked times are valid but sinful; supererogatory are invalid.

In the Hanafi school, the times of sunrise, noon zenith, and sunset are considered makruh tahrimi for prayer. But not all prayers are treated equally: an obligatory prayer performed during these times is technically valid yet sinful, requiring a repeat, while a supererogatory prayer is completely invalid. This lesson unpacks the general principle and examines special cases such as the two rak'ahs of tawaf, sajdat al-tilawa, and the funeral prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify the hukm for obligatory prayers in a disliked time: valid (sahih) but sinful (athim), and must be repeated (yajib an yusalliya fi ghayrihi). Contrast with supererogatory: not valid at all.
This is the foundational rule from which special cases branch.
2
Apply to the two rak'ahs of tawaf
The two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib. In the three disliked times they are invalid, because for validity they are treated as obligatory, even though for the ruling of dislike after Fajr and 'Asr they are considered nafil.
Note the double categorization: wajib for validity, nafil for dislike.
3
Analyze sajdat al-tilawa and funeral prayer
If the obligation for sajdat al-tilawa or funeral prayer arose before the disliked time, performing them during the disliked time is valid but disliked. However, if the cause (recitation or death) occurs in the disliked time, they may be performed without dislike, though delaying is better.
Al-Isbijabi’s difference: funeral prayer once performed is not repeated, but sajdat al-tilawa may require repetition if the cause was before the time.
4
Examine sajdat al-sahw
Sajdat al-sahw is like sajdat al-tilawa: if the disliked time enters after salam, the prostration is dropped because it is compensatory and cannot be performed incomplete.
The reasoning: it makes up for deficiency; a deficient act cannot be completed by an incomplete prostration.
5
Define the boundaries of disliked times
The passage defines sunrise as until the sun has risen a spear’s length (approximately 2-3 minutes after disk appears) and sunset as from the reddening of the sun until it disappears. Within these, prayer is not permissible.
Al-Fadli’s criterion: inability to look at the sun's disk marks the end of sunrise prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن يصلي في الوقت المكروه فأدى فيه يصح ويأثم، ويجب أن يصلي في غيره. وقول الشارح فيهما والأفضل أن يصلي في غيره ضعيف كما قدمناه . ويدخل في الواجب ركعتا الطواف فلا تصح في هذه الأوقات الثلاثة، اعتبرت واجبة في حق هذا الحكم ونفلاً في كراهتها بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر احتياطاً فيهما. وعبارة الكتاب أولى من عبارة أصله الوافي حيث قال : لا تصح صلاة إلى آخره لما علمت أن الصحة إنما هن في الفرائض والواجبات لا في النوافل بخلاف المنع فإنه يعم الكل. وأراد بسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة ما وجبت قبل هذه الأوقات، أما إذا تلاها فيها أو حضرت الجنازة فيها فأداها فإنه يصح من غير كراهة إذ الوجوب بالتلاوة والحضور لكن الأفضل التأخير فيهما. وفي التحفة الأفضل أن يصلي على الجنازة إذا حضرت في الأوقات الثلاثة ولا يؤخرها بخلاف الفرائض وظاهر التسوية بين صلاة الجنازة وسجدة التلاوة أنه لو حضرت الجنازة في غير مكروه فأخرها حتى صلى في الوقت المكروه فإنها لا تصح وتجب إعادتها كسجود التلاوة. وذكر الاسبيجابي : لو صلى صلاة الجنازة فإنه يجوز مع الكراهة ولا يعيد، ولو سجد سجدة التلاوة ينظر ؛ إن قرأها في هذا الوقت تجوز مع الكراهة وتسقط عن ذمته، وإن قرأها قبل ذلك ثم سجدها في هذا الوقت لا يجوز ويعيد اهـ. وسجدة السهو كسجدة التلاوة . كذا في المحيط - حتى لو دخل وقت الكراهة بعد السلام وعليه سهو فإنه لا يسجد لسهوه وسقط عنه لأنه لجبر النقصان المتمكن في الصلاة فجرى ذلك مجرى القضاء وقد ذلك كاملاً فلا يتأدى بالناقص . كذا في شرح المنية. وذكر في الأصل ما لم ترتفع الشمس قدر رمح فهي في حكم الطلوع واختار الفضلي أن الأنسان ما دام يقدر على النظر إلى قرص الشمس في الطلوع فلا تحل الصلاة، فإذا عجز عن النظر حلت وهو مناسب لتفسير التغير المصحح كما قدمناه وأراد بالغروب التغير كما صرح به قاضيخان في فتاواه حيث قال : وعند احمرار الشمس إلى أن تغيب
If he prays in the disliked time and performs it therein, it is valid and he sins, and he must pray in another time. The statement of the commentator regarding both that it is better to pray in another time is weak as we have mentioned. Included in the obligatory are the two rak'ahs of tawaf; they are not valid in these three times. They are considered obligatory for this ruling and supererogatory regarding their dislike after Fajr and 'Asr prayer as a precaution in both. The expression of the book is better than the expression of its original al-Wafi where he said: 'No prayer is valid' etc., because you know that validity applies only to obligatory and needed prayers, not to supererogatory ones, unlike prohibition which includes all. With sajdat al-tilawa and funeral prayer, he meant that which became obligatory before these times. As for if he recites in them or the funeral occurs and he performs it therein, it is valid without dislike, since obligation is by recitation and presence, but delaying is better in both. In al-Tuhfah: It is better to pray over the funeral if it occurs in the three times and not delay it, unlike the obligatory prayers. The apparent equality between funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawa is that if the funeral occurs without dislike and he delays it until he prays in the disliked time, it is not valid and must be repeated like sajdat al-tilawa. Al-Isbijabi mentioned: If he prays the funeral prayer, it is permissible with dislike and he does not repeat; if he prostrates sajdat al-tilawa, consider: if he recited it in this time, it is permissible with dislike and his obligation is fulfilled; if he recited it before and then prostrated it in this time, it is not valid and he repeats. Sajdat al-sahw is like sajdat al-tilawa. So in al-Muhit: Even if the disliked time enters after the salutation and he owes a sahw, he does not prostrate for his sahw and it is dropped from him because it is to compensate for deficiency occurring in the prayer, so it runs as qada', and since that is complete, it is not performed by the incomplete. So in Sharh al-Munyah. In al-Asl: As long as the sun has not risen a spear's length, it is in the ruling of sunrise; al-Fadli chose that as long as a person can look at the disk of the sun at sunrise, prayer is not permissible; when he cannot look, it is permissible, and this is suitable for the interpretation of the verified change as we mentioned. He meant by sunset the change as Qadikhan declared in his Fatawa: 'At the reddening of the sun until it sets.'
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on the rules of disliked times for prayer. The author begins by stating the general principle: if a person prays an obligatory prayer during a disliked time, the prayer is valid but they sin, and they must repeat it in another time. He then critiques a previous commentator who said it is better to pray in another time, calling that weak. He then discusses specific types of prayers: the two rak'ahs of tawaf are considered obligatory for the ruling of validity in these times, so they are invalid in the three disliked times; however, for the ruling of dislike after Fajr and 'Asr, they are considered supererogatory out of precaution. The author prefers the wording of the current book over its source al-Wafi. Next, he explains that sajdat al-tilawa and funeral prayer are only disliked if they became obligatory before the disliked time; if the recitation or funeral occurs during the disliked time, performing them is valid without dislike, but delaying is better. He notes a difference of opinion from al-Isbijabi regarding whether the prayer or prostration needs to be repeated. Sajdat al-sahw is treated like sajdat al-tilawa. Finally, he discusses the definition of sunrise and sunset based on the ability to see the sun, aligning with earlier interpretations.

Key Terms
الوقت المكروه (al-waqt al-makruh): The time during which prayer is disliked, specifically the three times: sunrise, noon until zenith, and sunset.
ركعتا الطواف (rak'ata al-tawaf): Two rak'ahs prayed after completing tawaf around the Ka'bah; considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janaza): The funeral prayer performed for a deceased Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Invalid and must be repeated.
C) Valid and not disliked because they are wajib.
D) Invalid but no repetition needed.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory prayers in disliked times are valid but sinful and require repetition; supererogatory prayers are invalid; special cases follow nuanced rules based on when the obligation arose.

Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Prayers in Disliked Times
Hanafi rebuttals to Shafi'i proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument for praying missed prayers in disliked times, applying the principle that a prohibitive specific text overrides a permissive general text.

Core Idea
A prohibitive specific text overrides a permissive general text.

This lesson delves into one of the classic inter-madhhab debates: whether prayers are permissible during the three disliked times (sunrise, noon zenith, sunset). The Shafi'i school argues for exceptions based on general hadiths, while the Hanafi school insists on the primacy of the specific prohibitive hadith of 'Uqbah. Through usul al-fiqh reasoning, we will see how the Hanafis defend their position and refute the Shafi'i proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the exact legal question being debated? Determine the act (prayer in disliked times) and the disputed exceptions (missed prayers, Makkah, Friday).
2
State the Hanafi position and its primary dalil
The Hanafi school holds that prayer in these times is prohibited. Their main evidence is the hadith of 'Uqbah. Understand its text and authority.
Hadith of 'Uqbah prohibits prayer at sunrise, noon, and sunset.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proofs and the Hanafi response for missed prayers
The Shafi'is use the hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer...' to argue that missed prayers are exempt. The Hanafis respond by analyzing the generality and specificity of both texts, concluding that the prohibitive text should prevail.
Key usul principle: al-khas yuqaddam 'ala al-'amm (the specific overrides the general).
4
Examine the other Shafi'i exceptions and Hanafi refutations
The Shafi'is also cite a hadith allowing prayer in Makkah at any time, and a report from Abu Yusuf about Friday noon prayer. The Hanafis refute both, either by contesting the authenticity or by showing they are general and overridden.
For Friday, the report is considered weak or incorrectly interpreted.
5
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
What does this dispute mean for a person? A Hanafi would not pray any prayer during these times except 'Asr of the same day, while a Shafi'i would allow missed and supererogatory prayers.
The mufta bihi opinion is the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشافعي رحمه الله أخرج من النهي في حديث عقبة الفوائت عملا بقوله عليه السلام من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فيصلها إذا ذكرها متفق عليه. والجواب عنه أن كونه مخصصاً لعموم النهي متوقف على المقارنة، فلما لم تثبت فهو معارض في بعض الأفراد فيقدم حديث عقبة لأنه محرم، ولو تنزلنا إلى طريقهم في كون الخاص مخصصاً كيفما كان فهو خاص في الصلاة عام في الأوقات، فإن وجب تخصيص عموم الصلاة في حديث عقبة وجب تخصيص حديث عقبة عموم الوقت لأنه خاص في الوقت، وتخصيص العشاء فينتفي وهم الوقوع قبل الوقت إذ التعجيل في العصر والعشاء يكون بعد التأخير في الظهر. عموم الوقت هو إخراجه الأوقات الثلاثة من عموم وقت التذكر في حق الصلاة الفائتة كما أن تخصيص الآخر هو إخراج الفوائت عن عموم منع الصلاة في الأوقات الثلاثة، وحينئذ الفائتة فيتعارضان في الأوقات المكروهة إذ تخصيص حديث عقبة يقتضي إخراجها عن الحل في الثلاثة، وتخصيص حديث التذكر للفائتة من عموم الصلاة يقتضي حلها فيها، ويكون إخراج حديث عقبة أولى لأنه محرم. وأخرج أيضاً النوافل بمكة لعموم قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم يا بني عبد مناف لا تمنعوا أحداً طاف بهذا البيت وصلى أية ساعة شاء من ليل أو نهار وجوابه أنه عام في الصلاة والوقت فيتعارض عمومهما في الصلاة، ويقدم حديث عقبة لما قلنا. وكذا يتعارضان في الوقت إذ الخاص يعارض العام عندنا وعلى أصولهم يجب أن يخص منه حديث عقبة في الأوقات الثلاثة لأنه خاص فيها. وأخرج أبو يوسف منه النفل يوم الجمعة وقت الزوال لما رواه الشافعي في مسنده : نهى عن الصلاة نصف النهار حتى تزول الشمس إلا الجمعة. وجوابه أن الاستثناء عندنا تكلم بالباقي فيكون حاصله نهياً مقيداً يوم بكونه بغير يوم الجمعة فيقدم عليه حديث عقبة المعارض له فيه لأنه محرم، وبحث فيه المحقق ابن الهمام بأنه يحمل المطلق على المقيد لاتحادهما حكماً وحادثة ولم يجب عنه، فظاهر ترجيح قول أبي يوسف فلذا قال في الحاوي: وعليه الفتوى كما عزاه له ابن أمير حاج في شرح المنية . وفي العناية: أن حديث أبي يوسف منقطع أو معناه ولا يوم الجمعة، واستثنى المصنف من المنع عصر يومه فأفاد أنه لا يكره أداؤه وقت التغير، وقد قدمنا أن المكروه إنما تأخيره لا أداؤه لأنه أداه كما وجب لأن سبب الوجوب آخر الوقت إن لم يؤد قبله وإلا فالجزء المتصل بالأداء وإلا فجميع الوقت. وعلل المصنف في كافيه بأنه لا يستقيم إثبات الكراهة للشيء لأنه مأمور به وقيل الأداء مكروه أيضاً .اهـ. وعلى هذا مشى في شرح هو صرح به والمغرب تأمل اهـ. قوله : (فإن وجب تخصيص عموم (الصلاة تخصيص الأول مصدر مضاف لمفعوله والأصل تخصيصه كما هو عبارة الفتح والضمير الحديث التذكر، وتخصيص الثاني مضاف لفاعله. والحاصل أن في كل من الحديثين خصوصاً وعموماً، فإن وجب تخصيص أحدهما لعموم الآخر وجب في الثاني كذلك. بقي أن كون حديث التذكر عاماً فيه خفاء بل الظاهر أنه مطلق كما في العناية، ويمكن استفادة العموم من إضافة الظرف إلى ما بعده فإن الإضافة تأتي لما تأتي له الألف واللام. قوله: (وأخرج أيضاً الخ) أي الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى قوله: (وفي العناية الخ) عبارته والجواب عن الثاني أن هذه الزيادة لم تثبت لأنها شاذة أو أن معناه ولا بمكة كما في قوله تعالى إلا
And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, excluded from the prohibition in the hadith of 'Uqbah the missed prayers, acting upon his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, then let him pray it when he remembers it' (agreed upon). The response to this is that its specification of the general prohibition depends on comparison (muqarana), and since it is not established, it is opposing in some individuals, so the hadith of 'Uqbah is preferred because it is prohibitive. And if we descend to their method that a specific is specifying however it is, it is specific regarding prayer and general regarding times. If specification of the general of prayer in the hadith of 'Uqbah is required, then specification of the hadith of 'Uqbah regarding the general of time is required because it is specific to time, and specifying the 'Isha' dispels the notion of occurrence before time, since hastening in 'Asr and 'Isha' comes after delaying in Zuhr. Generality of time is excluding the three times from the general time of remembrance regarding the missed prayer, just as the other specification is excluding the missed prayers from the general prohibition of prayer in the three times. Then the missed prayer conflicts in the disliked times, for the specification of the hadith of 'Uqbah requires excluding it from permissibility in the three, and the specification of the hadith of remembrance for the missed prayer from the general prayer requires its permissibility therein. And the exclusion by the hadith of 'Uqbah is more appropriate because it is prohibitive. He also excluded supererogatory prayers in Makkah due to the generality of his statement (peace be upon him): 'O sons of 'Abd Manaf, do not prevent anyone from circumambulating this House and praying at any hour he wishes, by night or day.' The response is that it is general regarding prayer and time, so their generalities conflict regarding prayer, and the hadith of 'Uqbah is preferred for what we said. Likewise, they conflict regarding time, for the specific opposes the general according to us, and according to their principles, the hadith of 'Uqbah must specify from it in the three times because it is specific to them. And Abu Yusuf excluded from it the supererogatory on Friday at the time of zenith based on what al-Shafi'i narrated in his Musnad: 'He forbade prayer at noon until the sun declines except on Friday.' The response is that the exception according to us speaks of the remaining, so its outcome is a prohibition restrictively on a day, being other than Friday, so the hadith of 'Uqbah which opposes it therein is preferred because it is prohibitive. The investigator Ibn al-Humam discussed that the absolute should be carried upon the restricted due to their unity in ruling and case, and he did not answer it, so the apparent preponderance is the statement of Abu Yusuf. Hence al-Hawi said: 'And upon it is the fatwa,' as attributed to him by Ibn Amir Hajj in Sharh al-Munyah. And in al-'Inayah: The hadith of Abu Yusuf is munqati' (disconnected) or its meaning is 'and not on Friday'. The author excepted from the prohibition the 'Asr of that day, so it indicates that performing it at the time of change is not disliked. We have already mentioned that the disliked is its delay, not its performance, because he performs it as required, since the cause of obligation is the end of time if not performed before; otherwise, the part connected to the performance; otherwise, all of the time. The author explained in his Kafi that it is not valid to establish dislike for something that is commanded, and it is said that performance is also disliked. Upon this he proceeded in the commentary... His statement: (For if specification of the generality of prayer is required) the first specification is a masdar added to its object, and the original is its specification as is the expression of al-Fath, and the pronoun refers to the hadith of remembrance, and the second specification is added to its subject. The summary is that in each of the two hadiths there is specificity and generality, so if specification of one for the generality of the other is required, then specification of the second likewise is required. Remaining is that the hadith of remembrance being general is obscure; rather, the apparent is that it is absolute as in al-'Inayah, and generality can be derived from the addition of the adverb to what follows, for the addition comes for what the definite article comes for. His statement: (He also excluded...) i.e., al-Shafi'i. His statement: (In al-'Inayah...) its expression, and the response to the second is that this increase is not established because it is anomalous, or its meaning is 'and not in Makkah' as in the verse 'except'.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the permissibility of praying in disliked times. The Shafi'is argue that missed prayers (fawa'it) are exempt from the prohibition based on the hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, then let him pray it when he remembers it.' The Hanafis respond by arguing that the hadith of 'Uqbah (which prohibits prayer at sunrise, noon, and sunset) is more specific and prohibitive, so it takes precedence. They engage in a usul al-fiqh discussion about general and specific texts, showing that both hadiths have aspects of generality and specificity. They conclude that the hadith of 'Uqbah is stronger because it is prohibitive. Then they address two further Shafi'i exceptions: supererogatory prayers in Makkah based on a hadith allowing prayer at any time, and supererogatory prayers on Friday at noon based on a narration from Abu Yusuf. The Hanafis refute both, arguing that the general hadith of 'Uqbah overrides these exceptions. They also discuss the opinion of Abu Yusuf and the position of Ibn al-Humam, ultimately stating that the fatwa is according to the Hanafi view that prayers are generally prohibited in these times, except for 'Asr of the same day which is not disliked. The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq explained that the dislike is for delaying, not performing, the prayer. The passage ends with a grammatical analysis of the phrase 'فإن وجب تخصيص عموم الصلاة' clarifying the grammatical roles.

Key Terms
حديث عقبة (hadith 'Uqbah): The hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amr which prohibits prayer at sunrise, noon until the sun declines, and sunset.
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Missed prayers that are made up later (qada').
خاص (khas): Specific; a text that applies to a specific set of individuals or circumstances.
عام ('amm): General; a text that applies to all individuals or circumstances without restriction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding prayers in disliked times, what is the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument using the hadith of 'Uqbah about missed prayers?
A) The hadith of 'Uqbah is fabricated.
B) The hadith of 'Uqbah is specific to missed prayers and cannot override the general prohibition of disliked times.
C) The hadith of 'Uqbah is general and applies to all times, so it abrogates the prohibition.
D) The hadith of 'Uqbah only applies to Makkah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the specific and prohibitive hadith of 'Uqbah takes precedence over general permissions for prayer in the three disliked times, emphasizing the importance of avoiding sin in worship.

Conflict of General and Specific Texts on Prayer in Prohibited Times
Explaining conflict between two hadiths and Hanafi preference for specific prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school gives precedence to a specific prohibition over a general permission in the case of prayer at prohibited times.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a specific text (khas) indicating prohibition overrides a general text (amm) permitting prayer at all times.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a classic usul al-fiqh tension: two hadiths appear to conflict, one prohibiting prayer at three specific times, another permitting missed prayers and tawaf prayers at any time. The Hanafi school resolves this by prioritizing the specific prohibition, applying the principle that the specific (khas) takes precedence over the general (amm). We will trace this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: prayer at three times (sunrise, zenith, sunset) is makruh tahrimi. The specific hadith of Uqba is the primary proof.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i and others argue that general hadiths (e.g., 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers') or the tawaf hadith allow prayer at any time, including those three.
The opposing school uses these general texts as evidence.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi response: the hadith of Uqba is specific (khas) to those times and indicates prohibition (tahrim). In Hanafi usul, a specific text overrides a general one.
The principle is 'al-khas yuqaddam 'ala al-amm'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the general hadith
The general hadiths are general in both prayer and time. They conflict with the specific prohibition. Since the specific is stronger (being a prohibition), it prevails.
For tawaf prayers, the hadith is also general, so the specific prohibition still dominates.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis prohibit any voluntary or missed prayer at these times (except exceptions like funeral prayer), while Shafi'is permit tawaf prayers and consider the prohibition only for non-tawaf prayers.
This affects daily practice for a Hanafi following the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عموم الوقت هو إخراجه الأوقات الثلاثة من عموم وقت التذكر في حق الصلاة الفائتة كما أن تخصيص الآخر هو إخراج الفوائت عن عموم منع الصلاة في الأوقات الثلاثة، وحينئذ الفائتة فيتعارضان في الأوقات المكروهة إذ تخصيص حديث عقبة يقتضي إخراجها عن الحل في الثلاثة، وتخصيص حديث التذكر للفائتة من عموم الصلاة يقتضي حلها فيها، ويكون إخراج حديث عقبة أولى لأنه محرم. وأخرج أيضاً النوافل بمكة لعموم قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم يا بني عبد مناف لا تمنعوا أحداً طاف بهذا البيت وصلى أية ساعة شاء من ليل أو نهار» وجوابه أنه عام في الصلاة والوقت فيتعارض عمومهما في الصلاة، ويقدم حديث عقبة لما قلنا. وكذا يتعارضان في الوقت إذ الخاص يعارض العام عندنا وعلى أصولهم يجب أن يخص منه حديث عقبة في الأوقات الثلاثة لأنه خاص فيها.
The generality of time is to exclude the three times from the generality of the time of remembrance regarding the missed prayer, just as the other specification is to exclude the missed prayers from the generality of the prohibition of prayer in the three times. Then the missed prayer... they conflict regarding the disliked times, since the specification of the hadith of Uqba necessitates excluding them from permissibility in the three [times], and the specification of the hadith of remembrance for the missed prayer from the generality of prayer necessitates their permissibility in them. And the exclusion by the hadith of Uqba is more appropriate because it is [indicating] prohibition. And also he excluded supererogatory prayers in Makkah due to the generality of his statement, peace be upon him: 'O sons of Abd Manaf, do not prevent anyone from circumambulating this House and praying at any hour he wishes, night or day.' The response is that it is general regarding prayer and time, so their generalities conflict regarding prayer, and the hadith of Uqba is given precedence for what we said. Likewise they conflict regarding time, since the specific opposes the general according to us, and according to their principles, the hadith of Uqba must be specified to the three times because it is specific to them.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage addresses a key usul al-fiqh issue: how to resolve apparent conflict between two hadiths. The first hadith (from Uqba) prohibits prayer at three specific times (sunrise, zenith, sunset). The second hadith (about remembrance/tadhakkur) seems to allow praying missed prayers at any time, including those times. The Hanafi approach is to treat the prohibition as specific and thus stronger. The text also discusses the exception for tawaf prayers in Makkah based on a general hadith, but argues that the prohibition still takes precedence because it is specific and indicates prohibition (tahrim). The author follows the Hanafi method of giving priority to the specific over the general.

Key Terms
العموم (al-umum): The general applicability of a text to all individuals or times it covers.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): The act of specifying a general text by a specific text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the hadith of Uqba is more authentic.
B) Because the hadith of Uqba is specific and indicates prohibition.
C) Because tawaf prayers are not considered valid prayers.
D) Because the general hadith is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a specific text (khas) indicating prohibition overrides a general text (amm) permitting an act, as seen in the ruling on prayer at the three disliked times.

Abu Yusuf's Exception for Friday Supererogatory Prayer at Zawal
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Friday zawal nafl prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Yusuf's view on supererogatory prayer at zawal on Friday and explain the Hanafi tarjih based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf exempts Friday supererogatory prayer at zawal; the majority prohibits but fatwa may follow Abu Yusuf.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the prohibition of supererogatory prayer at zawal (midday) on Friday. Abu Yusuf holds an exception based on a hadith, while the majority maintain the prohibition. We will analyze the evidence and the tarjih to understand which view is operative for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the two positions
Determine who holds the exception and who holds the general prohibition. Abu Yusuf allows nafl at zawal on Friday; the majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, etc.) prohibit it.
The dispute is recorded in al-Bahr al-Raiq.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's dalil
Abu Yusuf relies on a hadith narrated by al-Shafi'i that prohibits prayer at midday except on Friday. Identify the source and its classification.
The hadith is from al-Shafi'i's Musnad.
3
Examine the majority's objection
The majority responds that the exception phrase 'except Friday' does not override the stronger prohibition from the hadith of Uqba, which prohibits prayer at zawal generally. Understand the reasoning behind giving precedence to the hadith of Uqba.
The hadith of Uqba is considered stronger in indicating prohibition.
4
Analyze Ibn al-Humam's argument for harmonization
Ibn al-Humam argues that the absolute (general prohibition) should be carried to the restricted (exception for Friday) because they share the same ruling and incident. Understand why this would support Abu Yusuf.
This is a usul al-fiqh principle of haml al-mutlaq 'ala al-muqayyad.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
According to al-Hawi, the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. However, al-Inayah criticizes the hadith as disconnected (munqati') or interprets it differently. Recognize that the tarjih is contested.
The fatwa authority is al-Hawi, but other sources favor the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخرج أبو يوسف منه النفل يوم الجمعة وقت الزوال لما رواه الشافعي في مسنده : نهى عن الصلاة نصف النهار حتى تزول الشمس إلا الجمعة. وجوابه أن الاستثناء عندنا تكلم بالباقي فيكون حاصله نهياً مقيداً يوم بكونه بغير يوم الجمعة فيقدم عليه حديث عقبة المعارض له فيه لأنه محرم، وبحث فيه المحقق ابن الهمام بأنه يحمل المطلق على المقيد لاتحادهما حكماً وحادثة ولم يجب عنه، فظاهر ترجيح قول أبي يوسف فلذا قال في الحاوي: وعليه الفتوى كما عزاه له ابن أمير حاج في شرح المنية . وفي العناية: أن حديث أبي يوسف منقطع أو معناه ولا يوم الجمعة
And Abu Yusuf excluded from it the supererogatory [prayer] on Friday at the time of zawal, based on what al-Shafi'i narrated in his Musnad: 'He prohibited prayer at midday until the sun declines, except on Friday.' The response is that the exception according to us is speech about the remainder, so its result is a restriction that it is restricted to other than Friday, so the hadith of Uqba which opposes it in that matter is given precedence because it is [indicating] prohibition. And the investigator Ibn al-Humam discussed it, that the absolute is carried upon the restricted due to their unity in ruling and incident, and he did not answer it. So apparently the opinion of Abu Yusuf is preponderant, hence it was said in al-Hawi: And the fatwa is upon it, as cited by Ibn Amir Hajj in his commentary on al-Munyah. And in al-Inayah: that the hadith of Abu Yusuf is disconnected (munqati') or its meaning is 'and not on Friday'.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Yusuf holds that the prohibition of prayer at zawal (midday) does not apply on Friday for supererogatory prayers, based on a hadith that exempts Friday. The majority of Hanafis respond that even with this exception, the prohibition (from the hadith of Uqba) still applies because it is stronger, as it indicates tahrim. However, Ibn al-Humam argued for combining the two by carrying the absolute to the restricted, which would support Abu Yusuf. The author notes that al-Hawi gives fatwa according to Abu Yusuf, but al-Inayah criticizes the hadith as disconnected or interprets it differently. Thus, the matter is debated, but the text suggests that the fatwa in al-Hawi follows Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary prayers.
الزوال (al-zawal): The moment when the sun passes the meridian (midday).
منقطع (munqati'): A hadith with a broken chain of transmission (disconnected).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is munkar (rejected) due to a weak narrator.
D) It is mutawatir (mass-transmitted) but abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on Friday zawal nafl, with Abu Yusuf's view being relied upon in some fatwa sources despite majority opposition.

Ruling on 'Asr Prayer at the Time of Change
Explaining that 'Asr of the current day is not disliked at the time of change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that 'Asr prayer performed near sunset is not disliked, and identify the correct proof.

Core Idea
Performing 'Asr near sunset is valid because the obligation is fulfilled at the end of its time; the dislike is for delay, not for the act.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on performing 'Asr prayer during the 'time of change' – the period near sunset when the sun's color turns yellow. Many assume that all prayers at that time are disliked, but the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq makes an exception for the 'Asr of the current day. Let's explore the reasoning and the proof behind this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Performing 'Asr prayer at the time of change. The ruling: it is not makruh (disliked).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author reasons that the cause of obligation (sabab al-wujub) is the end of the time if one has not prayed earlier. Thus, performing it at that time is fulfilling the command, so it cannot be disliked.
This is a t'alil (reasoning) based on the nature of obligation.
3
Distinguish between delay and performance
The disliked aspect is only in delaying the prayer earlier in the time, not in the act of praying itself at the end.
This distinction is key to understanding the Hanafi position.
4
Address the counter-claim
Some said performance is also disliked. The author refutes this by noting that the prayer is commanded, so dislike cannot be established.
The strength of the command (amr) overrides any notion of karahah.
5
Note the usul discussion
The passage also examines conflicting hadiths and explains that the hadith about refraining at sunrise does not apply to 'Asr at sunset due to differences in time and ruling.
This shows the rigorous method of reconciling texts.

واستثنى المصنف من المنع عصر يومه فأفاد أنه لا يكره أداؤه وقت التغير، وقد قدمنا أن المكروه إنما تأخيره لا أداؤه لأنه أداه كما وجب لأن سبب الوجوب آخر الوقت إن لم يؤد قبله وإلا فالجزء المتصل بالأداء وإلا فجميع الوقت. وعلل المصنف في كافيه بأنه لا يستقيم إثبات الكراهة للشيء لأنه مأمور به وقيل الأداء مكروه أيضاً .اهـ. وعلى هذا مشى في شرح هو صرح به والمغرب تأمل اهـ. قوله : (فإن وجب تخصيص عموم (الصلاة تخصيص الأول مصدر مضاف لمفعوله والأصل تخصيصه كما هو عبارة الفتح والضمير الحديث التذكر، وتخصيص الثاني مضاف لفاعله. والحاصل أن في كل من الحديثين خصوصاً وعموماً، فإن وجب تخصيص أحدهما لعموم الآخر وجب في الثاني كذلك. بقي أن كون حديث التذكر عاماً فيه خفاء بل الظاهر أنه مطلق كما في العناية، ويمكن استفادة العموم من إضافة الظرف إلى ما بعده فإن الإضافة تأتي لما تأتي له الألف واللام. قوله: (وأخرج أيضاً الخ) أي الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى قوله: (وفي العناية الخ) عبارته والجواب عن الثاني أن هذه الزيادة لم تثبت لأنها شاذة أو أن معناه ولا بمكة كما في قوله تعالى إلا خطأ) [النساء : ٩٢] أي ولا خطأ .اهـ. زاد في معراج الدراية أو يحمل ذلك على أنه قبل النهي اهـ. قوله : (لأنه مأمور به أقول : عبارة المصنف في كافيه الأمر به . قوله: (فيثبت في ذمته الخ) قال في النهر : وبهذا التقرير علمت أنه لو صلى العصر ثم استمر حتى غربت أنها تفسد كما بحثه بعض الطلبة وهو متجه وذلك لأنها وإن فاتت إلا أنها تقررت في ذمته كاملة فلا تؤدي بالناقص ..اهـ. أقول : هذا البحث مشهور وقد ذكره صاحب البحر في شرحه على المنار وذكر جوابه وعبارته في الجواب : وأجيب بأن الشرع جعل الوقت متسعاً وجعل له شغل كل الوقت فالفساد الذي يعترض حالة البقاء جعل عذراً لأن الاحتراز عنه في الإقبال على الصلاة متعذر اهـ. وقال أيضاً: لكن قال في التنقيح هذا يشكل بالفجر وأجاب عنه في التلويح بأن العصر يخرج إلى ما هو وقت لصلاة في الجملة بخلاف الفجر أو بأن في الطلوع دخولاً في الكراهة وفي الغروب خروجاً عنهما اهـ. قوله : (أجيب الخ) وفي إمداد الفتاح بعد نقله ذلك: وروى ابن عمر أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: «إذا طلعت الشمس فأمسك عن الصلاة فإنها تطلع بين قرني شيطان» رواه مسلم. وروي أيضاً ووقت صلاة الصبح من طلوع الفجر ما لم تطلع الشمس، فإذا طلعت الشمس فأمسك الصلاة عن
And the author excluded from the prohibition the 'Asr of its day, so he indicated that performing it at the time of change is not disliked. And we have previously stated that the disliked is only its delaying, not its performance, because he performs it as obliged, because the cause of obligation is the end of the time if he did not perform it before, otherwise the part connected to the performance, otherwise all the time. And the author reasoned in his Kafi that it is not correct to establish dislike for something because it is commanded, and it was said that the performance is also disliked. End. And upon this he proceeded in the commentary... Then he said: (If the specification of the generality of prayer is required...) The first specification is a verbal noun with a passive object, originally 'its specification' as in al-Fath, and the pronoun refers to the hadith of remembrance, and the second specification is with an active subject. The result is that each of the two hadiths has a specific and a general; if it is necessary to specify one due to the generality of the other, it is also necessary in the second. It remains that the hadith of remembrance being general is obscure, rather it appears absolute as in al-Inayah, and generality can be inferred from the addition of the adverb to what follows, because addition comes for what the definite article comes for. Then his statement: (And he also excluded) i.e., al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. Then his statement: (And in al-Inayah...) his expression and the answer to the second is that this addition is not established because it is irregular, or its meaning is 'and not in Makkah' as in the verse 'except a mistake' [4:92] i.e., 'and no mistake'. End. And in Ma'raj al-Diraya it was added that it is carried on that it was before the prohibition. End. Then his statement: (Because it is commanded) I say: the expression of the author in his Kafi is 'the command with it'. Then his statement: (Thus it is established in his responsibility...) He said in al-Nahr: By this explanation you have learned that if he prays 'Asr and then continues until sunset, it becomes invalid, as some students researched, and it is consistent, because although it is missed, it is established in his responsibility as complete, so it cannot be performed imperfectly. End. I say: This research is famous and has been mentioned by the author of al-Bahr in his commentary on al-Manar, and he mentioned its answer, and his expression in the answer: It is answered that the Law made the time spacious and made it occupy all the time, so the invalidity that occurs in the state of remaining is made an excuse because it is difficult to avoid it when beginning the prayer. End. And he also said: But in al-Tanqih it is problematic with Fajr, and it was answered in al-Talwih that 'Asr exits to what is a time for prayer in general, unlike Fajr, or that in the rising there is entry into dislike and in the setting there is exit from both. End. Then his statement: (It was answered...) And in Imdad al-Fattah after quoting that: And Ibn 'Umar narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'When the sun rises, then refrain from prayer, for it rises between the horns of a devil' narrated by Muslim. And it is also narrated: 'The time of Fajr prayer is from dawn until the sun rises, so when the sun rises, then refrain from prayer.'
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on performing 'Asr prayer near sunset (the time of change). The author makes an exception for 'Asr of the current day: it is not makruh to perform it at that time, even though the time is generally disliked. The reasoning is that the obligation of 'Asr becomes due at the end of its time, and if one delays it until then, he is performing it as obligated. The disliked aspect applies only to delaying, not to the act itself. The text then delves into a detailed usul analysis of the conflicting hadiths, emphasizing that the hadith of remembrance is absolute rather than general. It discusses the distinction between 'Asr and Fajr: Fajr is invalidated by sunrise because its entire time is complete, while 'Asr's time ends with sunset, and the last part is deficient, so performing it then is valid. The hadith about catching a rak'ah is reconciled by preferring qiyas when texts conflict. The passage concludes with a hadith about refraining from prayer at sunrise.

Key Terms
وقت التغير (waqt al-taghayyur): The time when the sun changes color (yellowing) near sunset, which is generally disliked for prayer except for 'Asr of that day.
المكروه (al-makruh): In this context, 'disliked' refers to delaying the prayer, not performing it at that time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because it is a supererogatory prayer.
D) Because the time of change is not actually disliked.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that performing 'Asr at the time of change is valid and not disliked, because the obligation is fulfilled at the end of the time.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Asr at the End of Its Time and Difference with Fajr
Commentary resolving hadith conflict with prohibition of prayer at sunrise/sunset.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Asr prayer at the end of its time, explain the difference from Fajr, and apply the hadith of catching a rak'ah to resolve the apparent conflict with prohibition hadiths.

Core Idea
Asr at sunset is valid (deficiency in time); Fajr at sunrise is invalid (time complete).

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that Asr prayer performed at the very end of its time (near sunset) is valid, even though it coincides with a generally prohibited time. The key lies in understanding that the deficiency is in the time itself, not the prayer. We will also see why Fajr is treated differently—its time is complete, so if the sun rises during prayer, it becomes invalid. The apparent conflict between the hadith of catching a rak'ah and the prohibition of prayer at those times is resolved through a nuanced application of textual evidence and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The Hanafi school holds that performing Asr prayer at the end of its time (when the sun begins to change) is valid. This is an exception to the general prohibition of prayer at sunset. What is the ruling for Fajr? It becomes invalid if the sun rises during the prayer.
The difference hinges on whether the time itself is deficient or complete.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Abu Hurairah (Sahih Muslim): 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught it...' This is the proof for Asr's validity.
The hadith also mentions Fajr, but the Hanafis treat it differently due to other evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'فقد أدركها' (has caught it) indicates that even if only one rak'ah is completed before sunset, the entire prayer is valid. This establishes that the time of Asr extends until sunset, and the prohibition is overridden for this obligatory prayer.
The wajh al-dalalah is the explicit wording that validates the prayer despite the end of the time.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an apparent contradiction between this hadith and the general prohibition hadiths such as 'لا صلاة بعد العصر حتى تغرب الشمس'. How is this resolved?
Some schools may apply the prohibition uniformly; the Hanafis use a specific reconciliation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafis resolve the conflict by applying the hadith to Asr (making it an exception) and the prohibition to Fajr. The reason: For Asr, the time at the end is deficient (the sun changes), so the prayer is valid as it was obligated. For Fajr, the time from dawn to sunrise is entirely complete, so if the sun rises, the prayer becomes invalid because it extended into a prohibited time.
This tarjih is based on the nature of the times and the principle that the prohibition is for nafl, not for obligatory prayers like Asr.

كتاب الصلاة
الطحاوي. والتحفة والبدائع والحاوي وغيرها على أنه المذهب من غير حكاية خلاف وهو الأوجه للحديث السابق الثابت في صحيح مسلم وغيره. وقيد بعصر يومه لأن أمسه عصر لا يجوز وقت التغير لأن الأجزاء الصحيحة أكثر فيجب القضاء كاملاً ترجيحاً للأكثر الصحيح على الأقل الفاسد وأورد عليه أن من بلغ أو أسلم في الجزء الناقص لا يصح منه في ناقص غيره مع تعذر الإضافة في حقه إلى الكل لعدم الأهلية. وأجيب بأن لا رواية فيها فتلتزم الصحة، والصحيح أن النقص لازم الأداء في ذلك الجزء، وأما الجزء فلا نقص فيه غير أن تحمل ذلك النقص لو أدى فيه العصر ضروري لأنه مأمور بالأداء فيه، فإذا لم يؤد لم يوجد النقص الضروري وهو في نفسه كامل فيثبت في ذمته كذلك فلا يخرج عن عهدته إلا بكامل وبهذا اندفع ما ذكره السراج الهندي في شرح المغني من أن السبب لما كان ناقصاً في الأصل كان ما ثبت في الذمة ناقصاً أيضاً، فعند مضي الوقت لا يتصف بالكمال لما علمت أنه لا نقص في الوقت أصلاً. وأشار إلى أن فجر يومه يبطل بالطلوع والفرق بينهما أن السبب في العصر آخر الوقت وهو وقت التغير وهو ناقص فإذا أداها فيه أداها كما وجبت ووقت الفجر كله كامل فوجبت كاملة فتبطل بطرق الطلوع الذي وقت فساد لعدم الملائمة بينهما فإن قيل : روى الجماعة عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من أدرك ركعة من العصر قبل أن تغرب الشمس فقد أدركها ومن أدرك ركعة من الصبح قبل أن تطلع الشمس فقد أدرك الصبح أجيب بأن التعارض لما وقع بين هذا الحديث وبين النهي عن الصلاة في الأوقات الثلاثة في الفجر رجعنا إلى القياس كما

إلا عصر يومه وعن التنفل بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر لا قضاء فائته
