عند
هو حكم التعارض فرجحنا حكم هذا الحديث في صلاة العصر وحكم النهي في صلاة الفجر. كذا في شرح النقاية وظاهره أن ترجيح المحرم على المبيح إنما هو عدم القياس، أما عنده فالترجيح له وفي القنية : كسالى العوام إذا صلوا الفجر وقت الطلوع لا ينكر عليهم لأنهم لو منعوا يتركونها أصلاً ظاهراً، ولو صلوها تجوز عند أصحاب الحديث، والأداء الجائز عند البعض أولى من الترك أصلاً. وفي البغية الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة والدعاء والتسبيح أفضل من قراءة القرآن اهـ. ولعله لأن القراءة ركن الصلاة وهي مكروهة فالأولى ترك ما كان ركناً لها والتعبير بالاستواء أولى من التعبير بوقت الزوال لأن وقت الزوال لا تكره فيه الصلاة إجماعاً. كذا في شرح منية المصلي .
Book of Prayer. Al-Tahawi, al-Tuhfa, al-Bada'i', al-Hawi, and others agree that it is the madhhab without any dispute, and it is the most appropriate due to the previous hadith established in Sahih Muslim and others. It was restricted to the Asr of his day because yesterday's Asr is not permissible at the time of change (of the sun) because the sound parts are more, so it must be made up fully, preferring the more sound over the less corrupt. It was objected that one who reaches puberty or accepts Islam in the deficient part cannot perform it in another deficient part due to the impossibility of adding to it in his case because of lack of capacity. The answer is that there is no narration in it, so valid is adhered to. The correct view is that the deficiency is necessary for performance in that part, but as for the part, there is no deficiency in it except that bearing that deficiency if he performs Asr in it is necessary because he is commanded to perform it in it. If he does not perform, the necessary deficiency does not exist, and it (the prayer) is complete in itself, so it is established in his liability as such, and he is not free from liability except with a complete one. By this, what al-Siraj al-Hindi mentioned in Sharh al-Mughni is refuted: that since the cause was originally deficient, what is established in the liability is also deficient, so when the time passes it is not described as complete, because you know there is no deficiency in the time at all. And he pointed out that the Fajr of his day becomes invalid at sunrise, and the difference between them is that the cause in Asr is the end of the time which is the time of change and it is deficient, so if he performs it in it, he performs it as it was obligated. The time of Fajr is entirely complete, so it is obligated completely, so it becomes invalid at the occurrence of sunrise, which is the time of corruption, due to lack of compatibility. If it is said: The group narrated from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Asr before the sun sets has caught it, and whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught the morning prayer.' The answer is that when conflict occurred between this hadith and the prohibition of prayer in the three times for Fajr, we resort to analogy. ... (The text continues with further commentary and citations.)
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the exception of 'Asr of that day' from the prohibition of prayer during the three prohibited times (sunrise, sunset, and zenith). The author begins by stating that the Hanafi school unanimously holds that the prohibition is restricted to supererogatory prayers, and obligatory prayers like Asr are allowed at the end of their time. The hadith of Abu Hurairah (peace be upon him) about catching a rak'ah is cited. The objection is raised that this seems to conflict with the prohibition of prayer at those times. The answer is that the conflict is resolved by preferring the hadith for Asr and the prohibition for Fajr. The reasoning is that for Asr, the deficiency is in the time (the sun changing) not in the prayer itself, so it is valid. For Fajr, the time is complete (from dawn to sunrise), so if the sun rises, the prayer becomes invalid because it was performed in a time that became prohibited. The commentary also includes discussions from various sources like Sharh al-Niqayah, al-Qunyah, and al-Bughyah, emphasizing that the prohibition applies to nafl, not to obligatory prayers like qada', sajdat al-tilawah, or janazah.

Key Terms
عصر يومه (ʿaṣr yawmih): The Asr prayer of the current day, which is exempt from the prohibition of prayer during the third (end) of the time.
الجزء الناقص (al-juzʾ al-nāqiṣ): The deficient part of the time, i.e., the end of Asr time when the sun changes, which necessitates compensation if missed.
النهي عن الصلاة في الأوقات الثلاثة (al-nahy ʿan al-ṣalāt fī al-awqāt al-thalātha): The prohibition of prayer at three times: sunrise, sunset, and zenith. This passage discusses how it applies to Fajr and Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is Asr prayer valid when performed at the end of its time, while Fajr prayer becomes invalid if the sun rises during it?
A) Because the hadith of catching a rak'ah applies only to Asr, not Fajr.
B) Because the deficiency in Asr time is in the time itself, while Fajr time is complete, so the prayer must be complete.
C) Because the prohibition of prayer at sunrise is stronger than at sunset.
D) Because the Hanafi school has a different narration for Fajr.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates Asr at the end of its time due to deficiency in the time, while invalidating Fajr at sunrise because the time was complete.

Exceptions to the Prohibition of Prayer After Fajr and Asr
Commentary on the matn's list of exempted prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three exceptions to the prohibition of prayer after Fajr and Asr in the Hanafi school and explain the reasoning that differentiates them from supererogatory prayers.

Core Idea
The prohibition after Fajr and Asr targets only supererogatory prayers; obligatory prayers, prostration, and funeral prayer are exempt.

The hadith 'No prayer after Asr until the sun sets' appears to prohibit all prayers. However, the Hanafi school applies a nuanced understanding: the prohibition is specific to supererogatory (nafl) prayers. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the three exceptions – qada' (making up missed prayers), sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation), and salat al-janazah (funeral prayer) – and addresses the intra-Hanafi debate regarding witr prayer.

Guided Path
1
List the exceptions
Identify the three types of prayer that the matn explicitly exempts from the prohibition after Fajr and Asr.
They are qada' fā'ita, sajdat tilāwa, and salāt janāza.
2
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith
Examine the general hadith 'لا صلاة بعد الفجر...' and see how the Hanafi school restricts it to nafl using a contextual meaning (ma'na) based on the time being 'occupied' with the obligation.
This is a form of takhsis al-amm by meaning.
3
Follow the critique by Ibn al-Humam
Understand Ibn al-Humam's objection that this restriction lacks clear textual evidence and effectively opposes the general prohibition.
This represents a stricter textual approach within the Hanafi school.
4
Address the witr dispute
Consider the intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa (wajib) allows qada' after dawn; Sahibayn (sunnah) do not, but al-Qunyah reports consensus that witr is performed after dawn.
The mufta bihi is permissibility.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
State the relied-upon position: qada', sajda, and janazah are permitted; witr qada' is also permitted by consensus.
The prohibition is strictly for nafl prayers.

قوله (وعن التنفل بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر لا عن قضاء فائتة وسجدة تلاوة وصلاة جنازة) أي منع عن النتفل في هذين الوقتين قصداً لا عن غيره لرواية الصحيحين إلا صلاة بعد صلاة العصر حتى تغرب الشمس، ولا صلاة بعد صلاة الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس» وهو بعمومه متناول للفرائض فأخرجوها منه بالمعنى وهو أن الكراهة كانت لحق الفرض ليصير الوقت كالمشغول به لا بمعنى في الوقت فلم يظهر في حق الفرائض، وقد بحث فيه المحقق ابن الهمام بأن هذا الاعتبار لا دليل عليه . ثم النظر إليه يستلزم نقيض قولهم العبرة في المنصوص عليه لعين النص لا لمعنى النص لأنه يستلزم معارضة النص بالمعنى، والنظر إلى القضاء تقديماً للنهي العام على حديث التذكر. نعم يمكن إخراج صلاة الجنازة وسجدة التلاوة بأنهما ليسا بصلاة مطلقة، ويكفي في إخراج القضاء من الفساد العلم بأن النهي ليس بمعنى في الوقت، وذلك هو الموجب للفساد، وأما من الكراهة ففيه ما سبق اهـ. والحاصل إن الدليل يقتضي ثبوت الكراهة في كل صلاة وتخصيصه بلا مخصص شرعي لا يجوز. أطلق في الفائتة فشملت الوتر لأنه واجب على قوله وأما على قولهما فهو سنة فينبغي أن لا يقضي بعد طلوع الفجر لكراهة التنفل فيه، لكن في القنية : الوتر يقضي بعد طلوع الفجر بالإجماع بخلاف سائر السنن .اهـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه واقتصر على الثلاثة ليفيد أن

على أنه ذكر في الأسرار أن النهي عنها متأخر لأنه أبداً يطرأ على الأصل الثابت، ولأن الصحابة عملت به فعلم أنه لاحق بل قال الطحاوي: إنها كلها منسوخة بالنصوص الناهية وإلا يلزم العمل ببعض الحديث وترك بعضه بمجرد قولنا طرأ ناقص على كامل في الفجر بخلاف عصر يومه أن النقص قارن العصر ابتداء والفجر بقاء فيبطل في العصر كالفجر . قوله : (واقتصر على الثلاثة الخ) قال في النهر أقول : التحقيق أن يقال لما كان التقييد بالنفل يفهم الجواز فيما عداه وليس بالواقع نص الجائز ليعلم عدم الجواز فيما عداه من غير النفل ولولا هذه النكتة لما احتيج إلى ما ذكر

هو
His saying: (And regarding supererogatory prayer after Fajr and Asr, not regarding the making up of a missed prayer, and the prostration of recitation, and the funeral prayer) i.e., the prohibition is about supererogatory prayer in these two times specifically, not about other prayers, due to the narration of the two Sahihs: 'No prayer after Asr until the sun sets, and no prayer after Fajr until the sun rises.' Its generality includes obligatory prayers, so they excluded them from it by meaning, which is that the dislike was due to the right of the obligatory prayer so that the time becomes as if occupied, not in the sense of the time itself; therefore it does not appear regarding obligatory prayers. The investigator Ibn al-Humam discussed this, saying this consideration has no evidence. Then considering it necessitates the opposite of their statement that the criterion in the text is for the text itself, not for the meaning of the text, because it necessitates opposing the text with meaning, and considering the making up (qada') is giving precedence to the general prohibition over the hadith of remembrance. Yes, it is possible to exclude funeral prayer and prostration of recitation since they are not absolute prayers, and it suffices for excluding qada' from invalidity that the prohibition is not in the sense of the time, and that is what necessitates invalidity. As for dislike, what preceded suffices. The conclusion is that the evidence necessitates the existence of dislike for every prayer, and specifying it without a valid legal specification is not permissible. He made the missed prayer general, so it includes witr because it is obligatory according to him (Abu Hanifa), and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is sunnah, so it should not be performed after dawn due to dislike of supererogation therein, but in al-Qunyah: Witr is performed after dawn by consensus unlike other sunan. It is not hidden what is in it. He limited it to three to indicate that the texts indicate prohibition... As he mentioned in al-Asrar that the prohibition about them is later, because it always occurs on the established original, and because the Companions acted upon it, so it is known that it is later. Rather, al-Tahawi said: All of them are abrogated by the prohibiting texts, otherwise it would necessitate acting on some hadith and leaving some merely by our saying a deficient occurred on a complete in Fajr, unlike Asr of his day because deficiency accompanied Asr from the beginning and Fajr at the end, so it becomes invalid in Asr like Fajr. His saying: (He limited to three, etc.) said in al-Nahr: I say: The investigation is that since the restriction to supererogatory implies permissibility in what is other than it, and there is no text of permissibility to indicate the lack of permissibility in what is other than supererogatory, and without this nuance, there would be no need for what was mentioned.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage explains the matn's phrase that the prohibition of prayer after Fajr and Asr applies specifically to supererogatory (nafl) prayers, not to making up missed prayers (qada'), performing the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah), or funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The author discusses the reasoning: the hadith 'No prayer after Fajr until the sun rises' is general, but the fuqaha' excluded these by considering the 'illa: the prohibition is meant to avoid occupying time that is like being occupied with the obligation, which does not apply to obligations. Some scholars, like Ibn al-Humam, criticized this reasoning as lacking clear textual basis. The passage also addresses witr prayer: according to Abu Hanifa it is wajib, so it can be made up after dawn; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is sunnah, so it should not be made up then due to dislike of nafl. However, al-Qunyah reports consensus that witr can be made up after dawn. Finally, the author notes that the matn limited the exceptions to three (qada', sajda, janazah) to indicate that only these are permitted, and discussions about abrogation of earlier permissions by later prohibitions.

Key Terms
قضاء فائتة (qaḍāʾ fāʾita): Making up a missed obligatory prayer.
سجدة تلاوة (sajdat tilāwa): Prostration of recitation when reciting certain Quranic verses.
صلاة جنازة (ṣalāt janāza): Funeral prayer, considered a collective obligation (fard kifayah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following prayers is NOT allowed after Fajr prayer?
A) Making up a missed Zuhr prayer
B) Performing sajdat al-tilawah
C) Performing the janazah prayer
D) Performing a two-rak'ah sunnah prayer with intention of nafl

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the prohibition of prayer after Fajr and Asr only applies to supererogatory prayers; making up missed obligatory prayers, prostration of recitation, and funeral prayer are permitted, with witr being allowed by consensus.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Prohibited Times for Voluntary Prayers and Exceptions
Commentary on prohibited times for voluntary prayer with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr, identify the three exceptions, and explain the reasoning for each exception.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer is makruh tahrimi after Fajr and Asr, but make-up prayers, sajdat al-tilawah, and janazah prayer are exempt.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the prohibition of tanafful at specific times. Understanding the exceptions is crucial for correct practice in daily prayer routines. The Hanafi school balances the general hadith with reasoned exceptions to ensure obligatory acts are not hindered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited times
Locate the two specific times mentioned: after Fajr (until sunrise) and after Asr (until sunset). Note that the prohibition is for voluntary prayers only.
The times are defined by the completion of the obligatory prayer, not by the beginning of the time window.
2
State the general ruling
State that performing voluntary prayers (tanafful) during these times is makruh tahrimi (prohibited) according to the Hanafi school.
This ruling is based on the hadith and does not apply to obligatory or necessary prayers.
3
List the three exceptions
Identify the three types of prayers that are exempt: making up missed obligatory prayers (qada' fai'tah), prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah), and funeral prayer (salat al-janazah).
These are not considered 'tanafful' in the Hanafi definition.
4
Explain the dalil and its interpretation
The hadith 'La salata ba'da al-Asr...' is general, but Hanafi scholars interpret it as applying to voluntary prayers due to the underlying reason (illah): the time is symbolically occupied by the obligatory prayer.
This interpretation is based on istihsan and avoids contradicting the obligation of make-up prayers.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on witr
Abu Hanifa considers witr wajib and allows its make-up after dawn, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it sunnah and thus its make-up is disliked, except by consensus for witr itself.
The mufta bihi position follows the consensus that witr can be made up after dawn.

كتاب الصلاة
عن إلا عصر يومه وعن التنفل بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر لا قضاء فائته وسجدة تلاوة وصلاة جنازة. عند هو حكم التعارض فرجحنا حكم هذا الحديث في صلاة العصر وحكم النهي في صلاة الفجر. كذا في شرح النقاية وظاهره أن ترجيح المحرم على المبيح إنما هو عدم القياس، أما عنده فالترجيح له وفي القنية : كسالى العوام إذا صلوا الفجر وقت الطلوع لا ينكر عليهم لأنهم لو منعوا يتركونها أصلاً ظاهراً، ولو صلوها تجوز عند أصحاب الحديث، والأداء الجائز عند البعض أولى من الترك أصلاً. وفي البغية الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة والدعاء والتسبيح أفضل من قراءة القرآن اهـ. ولعله لأن القراءة ركن الصلاة وهي مكروهة فالأولى ترك ما كان ركناً لها والتعبير بالاستواء أولى من التعبير بوقت الزوال لأن وقت الزوال لا تكره فيه الصلاة إجماعاً. كذا في شرح منية المصلي .
قوله (وعن التنفل بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر لا عن قضاء فائتة وسجدة تلاوة وصلاة جنازة) أي منع عن التنفل في هذين الوقتين قصداً لا عن غيره لرواية الصحيحين «لا صلاة بعد صلاة العصر حتى تغرب الشمس، ولا صلاة بعد صلاة الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس» وهو بعمومه متناول للفرائض فأخرجوها منه بالمعنى وهو أن الكراهة كانت لحق الفرض ليصير الوقت كالمشغول به لا بمعنى في الوقت فلم يظهر في حق الفرائض، وقد بحث فيه المحقق ابن الهمام بأن هذا الاعتبار لا دليل عليه . ثم النظر إليه يستلزم نقيض قولهم العبرة في المنصوص عليه لعين النص لا لمعنى النص لأنه يستلزم معارضة النص بالمعنى، والنظر إلى القضاء تقديماً للنهي العام على حديث التذكر. نعم يمكن إخراج صلاة الجنازة وسجدة التلاوة بأنهما ليسا بصلاة مطلقة، ويكفي في إخراج القضاء من الفساد العلم بأن النهي ليس بمعنى في الوقت، وذلك هو الموجب للفساد، وأما من الكراهة ففيه ما سبق اهـ. والحاصل إن الدليل يقتضي ثبوت الكراهة في كل صلاة وتخصيصه بلا مخصص شرعي لا يجوز. أطلق في الفائتة فشملت الوتر لأنه واجب على قوله وأما على قولهما فهو سنة فينبغي أن لا يقضي بعد طلوع الفجر لكراهة التنفل فيه، لكن في القنية : الوتر يقضي بعد طلوع الفجر بالإجماع بخلاف سائر السنن .اهـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه واقتصر على الثلاثة ليفيد أن النصوص يفيد منع مع على أنه ذكر في الأسرار أن النهي عنها متأخر لأنه أبداً يطرأ على الأصل الثابت، ولأن الصحابة عملت به فعلم أنه لاحق بل قال الطحاوي: إنها كلها منسوخة بالنصوص الناهية وإلا يلزم العمل ببعض الحديث وترك بعضه بمجرد قولنا طرأ ناقص على كامل في الفجر بخلاف عصر يومه أن النقص قارن العصر ابتداء والفجر بقاء فيبطل في العصر كالفجر . قوله : (واقتصر على الثلاثة الخ) قال في النهر أقول : التحقيق أن يقال لما كان التقييد بالنفل يفهم الجواز فيما عداه وليس بالواقع نص الجائز ليعلم عدم الجواز فيما عداه من غير النفل ولولا هذه النكتة لما احتيج إلى ما ذكر
على ما .
هو
وصلاة جنازة وبعد طلوع الفجر بأكثر من سنة الفجر وقبل المغرب ووقت الخطبة وعن الجمع بين الصلاتين في وقت بعذر .
سبب بقية الواجبات من الصلاة داخل في النفل فيكره فيهما كالمنذور خلافاً لأبي يوسف، وما شرع فيه من النفل ثم أفسده وركعتي الطواف لأن ما التزمه بالنذر نفل لأن النذر سبب موضوع لالتزامه بخلاف سجود التلاوة لأنها ليست بنفل لأن التنفل بالسجدة غير مشروع فيكون واجباً بإيجاب الله تعالى، ولأنه تعلق وجوب النذر بسبب من جهته وسجدة التلاوة بإيجابه تعالى وإن كانت التلاوة فعله كجمع المال فعله ووجوب الزكاة بإيجاب الشرع. وفي فتح القدير : وقد يقال : وجوب السجدة في التحقيق متعلق بالسماع لا بالاستماع ولا التلاوة، وذلك ليس فعلاً من المكلف بل وصف خلق فيه بخلاف النذر والطواف والشروع فعله ولولاه لكانت الصلاة نفلاً اهـ. وهو قاصر على السامع للتلاوة لأن السبب في حقه السماع على خلاف فيه، وأما التالي فاتفقوا على أن السبب في حقه إنما هو التلاوة لا السماع وأطلق في التنفل فشمل ماله وما ليس له، فتكره تحية المسجد فيهما للعموم وهو مقدم على عموم قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من دخل المسجد فليركع ركعتين» لأنه . مبيح وذلك حاظر . وأشار إلى أنه لو شرع في النفل في وقت مستحب ثم قضاه فيهما فإنه لا يسقط عن ذمته كما في المحيط، وإلى أنه لو أفسد سنة الفجر ثم قضاها بعد صلاة الفجر فإنه لا يجوز على الأصح . وقيل يجوز والأحسن أن يشرع في السنة ثم يكبر بالفريضة فلا يكون مفسداً للعمل ويكون منتقلاً من عمل إلى عمل. كذا في الظهيرية وفيه نظر، لأنه إذا كبر للفريضة فقد أفسد السنة كما صرحوا به في باب ما يفسد الصلاة. وفي شرح المجمع لابن الملك : ما قاله بعض الفقهاء من أنه إذا أقيم للفجر وخاف رجل فوت الفرض يشرع في السنة فيقطعها فيقضيها قبل الطلوع مردود لكراهة قضاء التنفل الذي أفسده فيه على أن الأمر بالشروع للقطع قبيح شرعاً، وإلى أنه لا يكره التنفل قبل صلاة العصر في وقته، وإلى أن لصلاة العصر مدخلاً في كراهة النوافل فينشأ عنه كراهة التطوع بعد العصر المجموعة إلى الظهر في وقت الظهر بعرفات فيما يظهر، ولم أقف على التصريح به لأحد من أهل المذهب. كذا في شرح منية المصلي. واعلم أن قضاء الفائتة وما معها لا تكره بعد صلاة العصر إلى غاية التغير لا إلى الغروب كما هو ظاهر كلامه .
قوله (وبعد طلوع الفجر بأكثر من سنة الفجر) أي ومنع عن التنفل بعد طلوع الفجر إذ التقييد بالتنفل يغني عنه، وهذا دقيق جداً فتدبره إذ به يستغنى عن إخراج النفل عن معناه الشرعي لأنهم قد عرفوه بأنه فعل ليس بفرض ولا واجب ولا مسنون قوله : (وأشار الخ) الإشارة غير ظاهرة تأمل. قوله : ( ولم أقف على التصريح به لأحد الخ قال في النهر : هذا عجيب ففي فتح القدير ما لفظه : وذكر بعضهم لا يتنفل بعد صلاة الجمع بعرفة ،والمزدلفة وعزاه في المعراج إلى المجتبى، وفي القنية لمجد الأئمة الترجماني وظهير الدين المرغيناني قوله : (واعلم أن قضاء الفائتة الخ) يخالفه ما
Book of Prayer. Except the Asr of his day and about voluntary prayer after Fajr and Asr, not missed prayer, prostration of recitation, and funeral prayer. Regarding it is the rule of contradiction, so we gave preference to this hadith in Asr prayer and the rule of prohibition in Fajr prayer. Thus in Sharh al-Niqaya, and its apparent meaning is that preferring the prohibitory over the permissive is only due to lack of analogy, but according to him, the preference is for it. In al-Qunyah: The lazy commoners if they pray Fajr at sunrise, they are not rebuked, because if they were prevented, they would leave it entirely apparently, and if they pray it, it is permissible according to the hadith scholars, and performing an action that is permissible according to some is better than leaving it entirely. In al-Bughyah: Sending blessings upon the Prophet (PBUH) in times when prayer is disliked, and supplication and glorification are better than reciting Qur'an. Perhaps because recitation is a pillar of prayer and it is disliked, so it is better to leave what is a pillar of it, and expressing with 'equivalence' is better than expressing with 'time of zawal' because prayer at the time of zawal is not disliked by consensus. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. His statement (And about voluntary prayer after Fajr and Asr, not about missed prayer, prostration of recitation, and funeral prayer): meaning prohibition of voluntary prayer in these two times intentionally, not other than that, due to the narration of the two Sahihs: 'No prayer after Asr until the sun sets, and no prayer after Fajr until the sun rises.' In its generality it includes obligatory prayers, so they excluded them from it by meaning: that the dislike was for the sake of the obligatory prayer to make the time as if occupied by it, not a meaning in the time itself, so it did not apply to obligatory prayers. The investigator Ibn al-Humam discussed this, saying that this consideration has no evidence. Then looking at it entails a contradiction of their statement that the criterion in what is textual is the text itself, not the meaning of the text, because it entails opposing the text by meaning, and considering the make-up prayer is giving priority to a general prohibition over the hadith of remembering. Yes, it is possible to exclude funeral prayer and prostration of recitation because they are not absolute prayers, and it is sufficient to exclude make-up prayer from invalidation by knowing that the prohibition is not a meaning in the time itself, and that is what causes invalidation. As for dislike, what preceded suffices. The conclusion: the evidence requires establishing dislike in every prayer, and specifying it without a legal specific is not permissible. He made the missed prayer absolute, so it included witr because it is obligatory according to him, but according to them it is sunnah, so it should not be made up after dawn due to dislike of voluntary prayer in it, but in al-Qunyah: Witr is made up after dawn by consensus, unlike other sunnahs. It is not hidden what is in it. He restricted to three to indicate that the texts indicate prohibition. Along with that, it is mentioned in al-Asrar that the prohibition is later because it always comes upon the established principle, and because the Companions acted upon it, so it is known that it is later. Rather, al-Tahawi said: All of them are abrogated by the prohibitory texts, otherwise it would entail acting upon part of the hadith and leaving part merely by our saying that an inferior came upon a superior in Fajr, unlike the Asr of his day that the inferior accompanied the Asr from the beginning and Fajr in continuance, so it is invalidated in Asr like Fajr. His statement (And he restricted to three etc.) He said in al-Nahr: I say: The verification is that since the restriction to voluntary prayer implies permissibility of what is other than it, and the reality is not that the text permits with it, so that non-permissibility of other than it from non-voluntary might be known. Without this subtlety, there would be no need for what was mentioned about what it is. And funeral prayer, and after dawn by more than the sunnah of Fajr, and before Maghrib, and the time of the sermon, and about combining two prayers in one time due to an excuse. The reason: the rest of the obligatory prayers are included in voluntary, so they are disliked in those times, like vowed prayers, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And what one started of voluntary and then nullified, and the two rak'ahs of circumambulation, because what one committed to by vow is voluntary, because the vow is a cause established for committing, unlike prostration of recitation because it is not voluntary, since voluntary prostration is not legislated, so it is obligatory by Allah's command. And because the obligation of the vow is attached to a cause from his side, while prostration of recitation is by His command, even though recitation is his action, like collecting wealth is his action and the obligation of zakat is by the command of sharia. In Fath al-Qadir: It could be said that the obligation of prostration is truly attached to hearing, not to listening or recitation, and that is not an action of the responsible person but rather a quality created in him, unlike the vow and circumambulation and beginning, which are his actions, and were it not for that, they would be voluntary prayer. It is confined to the one who hears the recitation, because the cause for him is hearing, with a difference of opinion. As for the reciter, they agreed that the cause for him is recitation, not hearing. He made voluntary absolute, so it includes what is for him and what is not for him. Thus greeting the mosque is disliked in those two times due to the generality, and it is given precedence over the generality of his statement (PBUH): 'Whoever enters the mosque, let him pray two rak'ahs' because it is permissive while that is prohibitory. He pointed out that if one started a voluntary prayer in a preferred time and then makes it up in these times, it does not fall from his responsibility, as in al-Muhit. And if one nullified the sunnah of Fajr and then makes it up after Fajr prayer, it is not permissible according to the most correct view. And it is said permissible, and the best is that he start the sunnah and then say takbir for the obligatory prayer, so he is not nullifying the action and is transferring from one action to another. Thus in al-Zahhiriyyah, and there is a problem in it, because if he says takbir for the obligatory prayer, he has nullified the sunnah, as they explicitly stated in the chapter on what nullifies prayer. In Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik: What some jurists said that if the iqamah for Fajr is made and a man fears missing the obligatory prayer, he starts the sunnah and then cuts it and makes it up before sunrise, is rejected due to the dislike of making up the voluntary prayer that he nullified in it, and because the command to start for cutting is legally ugly. And that it is not disliked to perform voluntary prayer before Asr in its time. And that the Asr prayer has a role in the dislike of nawafil, so arises dislike of voluntary prayer after Asr combined with Zuhr at the time of Zuhr at Arafat, as appears. I have not come across an explicit statement on this from anyone of the madhhab. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. Know that making up missed prayer and what is with it is not disliked after Asr until the change of color, not until sunset, as is apparent from his words. His statement (And after dawn by more than the sunnah of Fajr): meaning prohibition of voluntary prayer after dawn, since the restriction to voluntary suffices for it, and this is very subtle, so contemplate it, for by it one dispenses with removing voluntary from its legal meaning because they defined it as an action that is not obligatory (fard), not necessary (wajib), and not recommended (sunnah). His statement (And he pointed out etc.) The indication is not apparent, ponder. His statement (And I have not come across an explicit statement from anyone etc.) He said in al-Nahr: This is strange, for in Fath al-Qadir there is a text: And some mentioned that one does not perform voluntary prayer after the combined prayer at Arafah and Muzdalifah, and it was attributed in al-Mi'raj to al-Mujtaba, and in al-Qunyah by Majd al-A'imma al-Tarjumani and Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani. His statement (And know that making up missed prayer etc.) Contradicts what.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the rules of prohibited times for prayer. The author explains that voluntary prayers (تطوع) are forbidden after Fajr and Asr based on the hadith in Sahih Bukhari and Muslim: 'No prayer after Asr until the sun sets, and no prayer after Fajr until the sun rises.' However, the Hanafi school makes exceptions for three types of prayers: make-up prayers (قضاء فائتة), prostration of recitation (سجدة تلاوة), and funeral prayer (صلاة جنازة). The reasoning is that the prohibition is not intrinsic to the time itself but rather to ensure that the time is not occupied with supererogatory acts that could distract from obligatory prayers. Therefore, obligatory or necessary prayers are not included in the prohibition. The passage also discusses a difference of opinion regarding witr prayer: according to Abu Hanifa it is wajib and thus can be made up after dawn, while according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is sunnah and should not be made up due to dislike of voluntary prayers at that time, but there is an exception by consensus for witr. The commentary further addresses other prohibited times: after dawn by more than the sunnah of Fajr, before Maghrib, during the khutbah (sermon), and the issue of combining prayers at Arafat due to an excuse. It also covers the ruling of making up an intentionally broken voluntary prayer in these times, concluding that it is not permissible on the most authentic view, and that the better approach is to start the sunnah and then transition to the fard without breaking the sunnah. Importantly, the passage clarifies that making up missed obligatory prayers is not disliked after Asr until the sun begins to change color, not until sunset, which is the correct ruling.

Key Terms
تنفل (tanafful): Voluntary, supererogatory prayer that is not obligatory or necessary.
فائتة (fā'itah): A missed obligatory prayer that is being made up (qada').
سجدة تلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): Prostration of recitation performed upon reciting specific verses of the Quran.
صلاة جنازة (ṣalāt al-janāzah): Funeral prayer, which is fard kifayah but not a formal prayer with ruku' and sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the three exceptions to the prohibition of prayer after Fajr and Asr?
A) Make-up prayer (qada' fai'tah)
B) Prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah)
C) Funeral prayer (salat al-janazah)
D) Greeting the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid)

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of prayer after Fajr and Asr applies only to voluntary prayers, not to make-up prayers, prostration of recitation, or funeral prayer.

Prohibition of Combining Prayers Except at Arafat and Muzdalifah
Inter-madhhab dispute on combining prayers with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining prayers, explain the Shafi'i position, and identify the conditions required by the Shafi'i school for valid joining.

Core Idea
Combining prayers is prohibited except at Arafat and Muzdalifah; advance joining invalidates, delay joining is prohibited but valid.

Combining two obligatory prayers into one time is a matter of significant difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. In this passage, Ibn Nujaym presents the Hanafi prohibition based on explicit hadith, then outlines the Shafi'i conditions for permissibility, warning against casual practice without proper conditions. This lesson will guide you through the evidence and the practical consequences of each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on combining prayers: prohibited except at Arafat (Zuhr and Asr) and Muzdalifah (Maghrib and Isha). Distinguish between advance joining (invalidates) and delay joining (prohibited but valid).
The term 'جمع' here refers to combining two prayers in one time.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
The Shafi'i school allows combining for travelers between Zuhr and Asr, and between Maghrib and Isha, with specific conditions.
The passage mentions that many people, especially Hajj pilgrims, follow this without adhering to the conditions.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on narrations where the Prophet joined prayers, interpreting them as genuine joining at one time.
They do not see a contradiction with the fixed times because they consider travel an excuse.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response interprets those narrations as 'suri jam'' (formal joining by praying at the end of the first time and start of the second) or metaphorical use of 'time' for nearness. The definitive hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is prioritized.
The author provides the Hanafi response of interpreting narrations as metaphorical or actual nearness.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis must pray each prayer in its own time, while Shafi'is can combine when traveling, but must fulfill conditions like intention, order, and continuity.
This difference affects daily practice, especially during travel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن الجمع بين الصلاتين في وقت بعذر) أي منع عن الجمع بينهما في وقت واحد بسبب العذر للنصوص القطعية بتعيين الأوقات فلا يجوز تركه إلا بدليل مثله ولرواية الصحيحين قال عبد الله بن مسعود: والذي لا إله غيره ما صلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلاة قط إلا لوقتها إلا صلاتين جمع بين الظهر والعصر بعرفة، وبين المغرب والعشاء بجمع وأما ما روي من الجمع بينهما فمحمول على الجمع فعلاً بأن صلى الأولى في آخر وقتها، والثانية في أول وقتها. ويحمل تصريح الراوي بالوقت على المجاز القربه منه، والمنع عن الجمع المذكور عندنا مقتض للفساد إن كان جمع تقديم، وللحرمة إن كان جمع تأخير مع الصحة كما لا يخفى. وذهب الشافعي وغيره من الأئمة إلى جواز الجمع للمسافر بين الظهر والعصر وبين المغرب والعشاء، وقد شاهدت كثيراً من الناس في الأسفار خصوصاً في سفر الحج ماشين على هذا تقليداً للإمام الشافعي في ذلك إلا أنهم يخلون بما ذكرت الشافعية في كتبهم من الشروط له فأحببت إيرادها إبانة لفعله على وجهه لمريده اعلم أنهم بعد أن اتفقوا على أن فعل كل صلاة في وقتها أفضل إلا للحاج في الظهر والعصر بعرفة وفي حق المغرب والعشاء بمزدلفة قالوا: شروط التقديم ثلاثة : البداءة بالأولى ونية الجمع بينهما ومحل هذه النية عند مسلم إذ الظاهر أن ذلك على سبيل الوجوب لتعليلهم بأن المغرب فرض عين والجنازة فرض كفاية، ولأن الغالب في كلامهم في مثله إرادة الوجوب تأمل اهـ .. قوله : (أو كسوف) فيه أن خطبة الكسوف مذهب الشافعي رحمه الله لا مذهبنا تأمل . وأما خطبة الاستسقاء فهي على قول الصاحبين . ولو نوى مع السلام منها جاز على الأصح والموالاة بأن لا يطول بينهما فصل، فإن طال وجب تأخير الثانية إلى وقتها. ولا يضر فصل يسير. وما عده العرف فصلاً طويلاً فهو طويل يضر، وما لا فلا. وللمتيمم الجمع على الصحيح ولا يشترط على الصحيح في جواز تأخير الأولى إلى الثانية سوى تأخيرها بنية الجمع بينهما، والأصح أنه إن نوى وقد بقي من الوقت ما يسع ركعة كفى على ما في الرافعي والروضة. واعتبر في شرح المهذب قدر الصلاة فإن لم ينو كما ذكرنا وأخر عصى في التأخير وكانت صلاته قضاء. قالوا: وإذا كان سائراً وقت الأولى فتأخيرها إلى وقت الثانية أفضل، وإن كان نازلاً فتقديم الثانية إلى وقت الأولى أفضل. ذكره ابن أمير حاج في مناسكه والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
And regarding joining two prayers in one time due to an excuse: i.e., it is prohibited to join them in one time because of an excuse, due to definitive texts specifying the times, so it is not permissible to abandon that except with evidence like it, and due to the narration in the two Sahihs: 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'By Him besides Whom there is no god, the Messenger of Allah never prayed any prayer except at its time, except two prayers: he joined Zuhr and Asr at Arafat, and Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah.' And what is narrated of joining them is interpreted as joining in action, by praying the first at the end of its time and the second at the beginning of its time. And the explicit mention of time by the narrator is interpreted as a metaphor meaning nearness to it. And the prohibition of the mentioned joining according to us necessitates invalidity if it is advance joining, and prohibition if it is delay joining, with validity, as is not hidden. And al-Shafi'i and other imams went to the permissibility of joining for the traveler between Zuhr and Asr and between Maghrib and Isha. I have seen many people on journeys, especially the Hajj journey, acting upon this, following Imam al-Shafi'i in that, except that they neglect the conditions mentioned by the Shafi'is in their books. So I desired to mention them to clarify the act correctly for the one who wants it. Know that after they agreed that performing each prayer in its time is better except for the pilgrim in Zuhr and Asr at Arafat and Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, they said: The conditions of advance joining are three: starting with the first, intention of joining between them, and the place of this intention is at the time of the first prayer, indeed it is apparent that this is obligatory because they reason that Maghrib is a personal obligation and the funeral prayer is a communal obligation, and because the general usage in their speech in such cases indicates obligation. Contemplate. And they said: the condition of continuity (muwalat) is that the interval between them should not be long; if it is long, the second prayer must be delayed to its time, and a short interval does not harm. What custom considers a long interval is long and harmful; what it does not consider is not. And for the one who performs tayammum, joining is valid according to the correct view. And it is not required, according to the correct view, for the permissibility of delaying the first to the second other than delaying it with the intention of joining between them. And the correct view is that if he intends while there remains enough time for one rak'ah, it suffices as in al-Rafi'i and al-Rawdah. And in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, the capacity for the whole prayer was considered. If he did not intend as we mentioned and delayed, he sinned in delaying and his prayer would be qada. They said: If he is traveling at the time of the first, delaying it to the time of the second is better; if he is stationary, advancing the second to the time of the first is better. Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned it in his Manasik. And Allah Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on combining (jam') two obligatory prayers in one time. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the Hanafi position first: combining prayers is prohibited except at Arafat (for Zuhr and Asr) and Muzdalifah (for Maghrib and Isha), based on the definitive texts of the fixed prayer times and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. Any narrations suggesting general permissibility are interpreted as 'suri jam' (formal joining) where the first prayer is prayed at the end of its time and the second at the beginning of its time. The Hanafi ruling is that advance joining (jam' taqdim) invalidates the prayer, while delay joining (jam' ta'khir) is prohibited but valid. Then the author presents the Shafi'i position: joining is permissible for travelers between Zuhr and Asr, and between Maghrib and Isha. He observes that many people, especially Hajj pilgrims, follow this, but often neglect the Shafi'i conditions. He then lists the Shafi'i conditions for advance joining: (1) starting with the first prayer, (2) intention of joining at the time of the first prayer, and (3) continuity (muwalat) without excessive gap. For delay joining, only the intention to delay is required. The passage also briefly discusses the ruling for a traveler: if moving, delaying is better; if stationary, advancing is better. This whole discussion functions as a warning against casual practice of combining without fulfilling conditions.

Key Terms
جمع تقديم (jam' taqdim): The act of joining an earlier prayer with a later prayer at the time of the earlier prayer
جمع تأخير (jam' ta'khir): Delaying an earlier prayer to be joined with a later prayer at the time of the later prayer
موالاة (muwalat): Continuity between the two prayers without a long gap

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a traveler prays Zuhr and Asr together at the time of Zuhr without being at Arafat, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid and permissible.
B) The prayer is invalid (fasid) and must be repeated.
C) The Zuhr prayer is valid but Asr is invalid.
D) Both are valid but makruh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts combining prayer to only the two specified locations, while the Shafi'i school allows it for travelers with specific conditions.

Adhan: Definition, Evidence, and the Mu'adhdhin's Qualities
Opening definition and evidentiary basis for adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of adhan, identify its primary proofs, and list the recommended qualities (sunan) of the mu'adhdhin, including the rulings on a discerning boy (sabi 'aqil) and a fasiq.

Core Idea
Adhan is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib; its origin is divine, and the mu'adhdhin must be trustworthy and knowledgeable.

This opening passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines adhan both linguistically and legally, traces its origin to the night of Isra', and provides the primary evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. It then categorises the sunan into those pertaining to the words of adhan and those pertaining to the caller himself. Here we focus on the caller's qualifications, including the key rulings on a discerning boy and a sinful caller.

Guided Path
1
Parse the legal definition
Identify the linguistic meaning (i'lam) and the legal definition (i'lam makhsus fi waqt makhsus). Note that it is a specific announcement tied to prayer times.
The definition distinguishes adhan from other calls.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the Quranic reference (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9) and note that the Sunnah and Ijma are also cited. Understand that the verse uses 'nida' to indicate adhan.
Dalil also includes the dream of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd and the hadith 'Let the best among you call the adhan'.
3
Distinguish the two categories of sunan
Recognise that sunan are divided: (1) sunan within the adhan words, (2) sunan regarding the mu'adhdhin's qualities. The passage elaborates on the latter.
The first category is deferred to later in the text.
4
Extract the mu'adhdhin's required qualities and rulings
List: male, sane, trustworthy, knowledgeable of Sunnah and prayer times. Then note the rulings on a sabi 'aqil (neither mustahabb nor makruh, valid) and a fasiq (makruh). Also note the prohibition of taking payment.
The zahir al-riwayah position is that the adhan of a sabi 'aqil is acceptable; the hadith 'Let the best among you' supports preferring a righteous caller.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأذان. هو لغة الأعلام ومنه قوله تعالى وأذان من الله ورسوله) [التوبة: ٣] وشرعاً إعلام مخصوص في وقت مخصوص وسبيه الابتدائي أذان جبريل عليه السلام ليلة الإسراء وإقامته حين صلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إماماً بالملائكة وأرواح الأنبياء، ثم رؤيا عبد الله بن زيد الملك النازل من السماء في المنام وهو مشهور وصححه الأسبيجابي. واختلف في هذا الملك فقيل جبريل، وقيل غيره كذا في العناية والبقائي. دخول الوقت ودليله الكتاب إذا نودي للصلاة من يوم الجمعة) [الجمعة: ۹] والسنة والإجماع. وصفته ستأتي وركنه الألفاظ المخصوصة وكيفيته معلومة وأما سننه فنوعان : سنن في نفس الأذان، وسنن في صفات المؤذن . أما الأول فسيأتي، وأما الثاني فأن يكون رجلاً عاقلاً ثقة عالماً بالسنة وأوقات الصلاة فأذان الصبي العاقل ليس بمستحب ولا مكروه في ظاهر الرواية فلا يعاد ويشهد له الحديث وليؤذن لكم خياركم»(۱) وصرحوا بكراهة أذان الفاسق من غير تقييد بكونه عالماً أو غيره. ثم يدخل في كونه خياراً أن لا يأخذ على باب الأذان قوله : (وعند أبي يوسف يحبسون ويضربون قال في فتح القدير : كذا نقله بعضهم بصورة نقل
Chapter of Adhan. It is linguistically an announcement, as in His statement: 'And an announcement from Allah and His Messenger' (9:3). Legally, it is a specific announcement at a specific time. Its beginning was the adhan of Jibril (peace be upon him) on the night of Isra' and his iqamah when the Prophet (peace be upon him) led the angels and souls of the prophets in prayer. Then came the dream of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd about the angel descending from the sky, which is famous and was authenticated by al-Usbijabi. There is disagreement about this angel: some say Jibril, others say otherwise, as in al-'Inayah and al-Biqa'i. [It indicates] the entry of time. Its proof is the Book: 'When the call is made for prayer on Friday' (62:9), and the Sunnah, and consensus. Its description will come, its pillar is the specific words, and its manner is known. As for its sunan, they are of two types: sunan within the adhan itself, and sunan regarding the qualities of the mu'adhdhin. The first will come later. As for the second: that the caller be a man, sane, trustworthy, knowledgeable of the Sunnah and prayer times. So the adhan of a discerning boy is neither mustahabb nor makruh in the apparent narration, so it is not repeated, and the hadith 'Let the best among you call the adhan for you' supports that. They explicitly stated the dislike of a fasiq's adhan, without restricting it to being knowledgeable or otherwise. Then being among the best includes that he not take payment for it. [Then the text breaks off with a note from Abu Yusuf about detention and beating.]
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on adhan. It first provides the definition of adhan: linguistically, it means announcement (i'lam), and legally, it is a specific form of announcement made at specified times to inform people of prayer times. The author then narrates the origin of adhan, tracing it to Jibril's adhan on the night of Isra', and also mentions the famous dream of 'Abdullah ibn Zayd which led to the institution of the verbal adhan. The proof for adhan is drawn from the Quran (Surah al-Jumu'ah, verse 9), the Sunnah of the Prophet, and the consensus of the Ummah. The pillar (rukn) of adhan is the specific phrases, and its description will be detailed later. The author then divides the sunan (recommended acts) into two categories: those related to the wording of adhan itself, and those related to the qualifications of the mu'adhdhin (caller). The second category is discussed here: the mu'adhdhin should be a man, sane, trustworthy, and knowledgeable of the Sunnah and prayer times. The adhan of a discerning adolescent boy (sabi 'aqil) is neither encouraged nor disliked, according to the zahir al-riwayah; it need not be repeated, as supported by the hadith 'Let the best among you call the adhan.' The adhan of a fasiq (sinner) is explicitly disliked (makruh), regardless of his knowledge. Additionally, the mu'adhdhin should not accept payment for adhan, as part of being 'the best'. The passage ends with a note citing Abu Yusuf's view that those who take payment should be detained and beaten, which is a stronger deterrent.

Key Terms
أذان (adhan): Legally, a specific announcement (i'lam makhsus) made at specific times to indicate the entry of prayer time.
مؤذن (mu'adhdhin): The person who recites the adhan; should be male, sane, trustworthy, and knowledgeable of the Sunnah and prayer times.
فاسق (fasiq): One who commits major sins or persists in minor sins; his adhan is disliked (makruh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the adhan of a discerning adolescent boy (sabi 'aqil)?
A) It is mustahabb and recommended.
B) It is neither mustahabb nor makruh, and does not need to be repeated.
C) It is makruh and should be repeated.
D) It is invalid because a boy is not qualified.

Key Takeaway
Adhan is a confirmed sunnah, its proof is clear, and the caller should be a trustworthy male free from major sin.

Taking Wages for Adhan and Imamah: Change in Hanafi Fatwa
Ruling on taking wages for adhan and imamah with later fatwa change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original and later Hanafi positions on taking wages for adhan and imamah, and explain the reason for the change.

Core Idea
The Hanafi ruling on wages for adhan changed from prohibition to permission due to necessity and changed circumstances.

The early Hanafi scholars held that taking wages for adhan and imamah was not permissible, as these are acts of worship. However, later Hanafi jurists, recognizing the changing needs of the community, permitted it. This lesson traces that shift and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its original ruling
The act is taking wages for adhan and imamah. According to early Hanafi scholars, it is not permissible to take a wage for these duties.
The text says 'لا يحل له أخذ شيء على ذلك'.
2
Note the exception for gifts
If the community gives a gift without prior stipulation, it is permissible. This is based on the principle of voluntary giving.
This is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir.
3
Identify the later fatwa change
The chosen opinion for fatwa in our time permits taking wages for the imam, mu'adhdhin, teacher, and mufti.
Referenced from the book of leases (Kitab al-Ijarat).
4
Understand the basis for change
The change is due to necessity and changed circumstances ('umum al-balwa). Later scholars recognized that prohibiting wages would cause hardship.
This is a shift from zahir al-riwayah to later fatwa.
5
Recognize the epistemological weight
This ruling comes from fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa collections), not from the core texts of Zahir al-Riwayah.
Authority is based on Fath al-Qadir and other later works.

واتخذ مؤذنا لا يأخذ على الأذان أجراً» قالوا : فإن لم يشارطهم على شيء لكن عرفوا حاجته فجمعوا له في وقت شيئاً كان حسناً ويطيب له، وعلى هذا المفتي لا يحل له أخذ شيء على ذلك لكن ينبغي للقوم أن يهدوا إليه كذا في فتح القدير وهو على قول المتقدمين. أما على المختار للفتوى في زماننا فيجوز أخذ الأجر للإمام والمؤذن والمعلم والمفتي كما صرحوا به في كتاب الإجارات. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان المؤذن إذا لم يكن عالماً بأوقات الصلاة لا يستحق ثواب المؤذنين. قال في فتح القدير: ففي أخذ الأجر أولى اهـ. وقد يمنع لما أنه في الأول للجهالة الموقعة في الغرر لغيره بخلافه في الثاني وهل يستحق المعلوم المقدر في الوقف للمؤذن؟ لم أره في كلام أئمتنا وصرح النووي في شرح المهذب بأنه لم يصح أذانه فيمن يولي ويرتب للأذان
And he appointed a mu'adhdhin who does not take wages for the adhan. They said: If he did not stipulate anything with them, but they knew his need and collected something for him at a time, it is good and permissible for him. According to this, the mufti said that it is not permissible for him to take anything for that, but the people should give him a gift. This is in Fath al-Qadir, and it is according to the earlier scholars. As for the chosen opinion for fatwa in our time, it is permissible to take wages for the imam, mu'adhdhin, teacher, and mufti, as they have stated in the book of leases. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: If the mu'adhdhin does not know the times of prayer, he does not deserve the reward of the mu'adhdhins. He said in Fath al-Qadir: Thus taking wages is more appropriate. And it may be prevented because in the first case it is ignorance leading to uncertainty for others, unlike the second. And does he deserve the fixed amount in the endowment for the mu'adhdhin? I have not seen it in the words of our imams, and al-Nawawi stated in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab that his adhan is not valid when he is appointed and assigned to the adhan.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on mu'adhdhins and imams taking wages. The original position from earlier Hanafi scholars was that it is not permissible to take a wage for adhan or imamah, but if the community gives a gift without stipulation, it is allowed. However, the later chosen position for fatwa in our time permits taking wages for these roles due to necessity. This change is recorded in Fath al-Qadir and other works. The passage also notes that if the mu'adhdhin is ignorant of prayer times, he does not deserve the reward of mu'adhdhins, so taking wages is more appropriate for him. There is also a discussion about whether a mu'adhdhin appointed to a waqf position deserves the fixed stipend, but the author says he has not seen a clear ruling from Hanafi imams on this.

Key Terms
الأجر (al-ajr): Wage or payment for performing adhan or imamah
المؤذن (al-mu'adhdhin): The person who calls the adhan
الإمامة (al-imamah): Leading the prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later chosen opinion for fatwa, what is the ruling on a mu'adhdhin taking wages?
A) It is absolutely prohibited
B) It is permissible
C) It is only permissible if he is ignorant of prayer times
D) It is mandatory

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the original prohibition and the later permissibility of wages for adhan and imamah, with the latter becoming the operative fatwa due to necessity.
